Broken Pawn: When Value Exceeds Weight
Presents Abu Hanifa's ruling on pawn breakage when value exceeds weight, with reasoning based on weight criterion and subsidiary logic.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state Abu Hanifa's ruling when a pawn's value exceeds its weight and explain the reasoning based on weight as the primary criterion and the subsidiary following the substance.

Core Idea
Weight is the sole criterion; if the full weight is pledged, the full value is guaranteed.

In pawn transactions, the weight of the pledged item often determines its liability. But what happens when the market value exceeds the weight? Imam Abu Hanifa provides a clear ruling: the mortgagee must guarantee the entire value, because weight—not quality—is the basis. This lesson unpacks his reasoning, grounded in the principle that quality (an accident) is subsidiary to substance (the metal itself).

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The pawn (a vessel weighing 10 dirhams) breaks. Its market value is 12 dirhams, exceeding its weight. The debt is 10 dirhams.
This is the second of two scenarios; the first had value equal to weight.
2
State Abu Hanifa's ruling
According to Abu Hanifa, the mortgagee (murtahin) guarantees the full market value (12 dirhams), and this amount becomes the new pawn in place of the original vessel.
3
Identify the primary criterion
The key principle: 'al-ibrah li al-wazn'—the criterion is weight, not quality (jūdah) or inferiority (radā'ah).
This is a foundational Hanafi precept in pawn contracts.
4
Understand the reasoning: subsidiary follows substance
Quality is an accident (arad) subsidiary to the substance (jawhar). Since the full weight (10 dirhams) is pledged and matches the debt, the substance is fully 'guaranteed' (madhmun). The subsidiary must follow: it is impossible for the substance to be guaranteed while the quality remains a trust (amānah).
The principle of taba'iyyah (subordination) is central here.
5
Apply to the scenario
Because the weight equals the debt (10 dirhams), the entire weight is pledged. Therefore, the entire value (including the extra 2 dirhams for quality) is also guaranteed. The mortgagee must pay 12 dirhams.
This logic prevents an impossible contradiction: having the substance guaranteed but its quality trust.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفى الوجه الثاني وهو ما اذا كانت قيمته اكثر من وزنه اثنی عشر عند ابي حنيفة يضمن جميع قيمته وتكون رهنا عنده لان العبرة للوزن عنده لا للجودة والردائة فان كان باعتبار الوزن كله مضمونا يجعل كله مضمونا وان كان بعضه فبعضه وهذا لان الجودة تابعة للذات ومتى صار الاصل مضمونا استحال ان يكون التابع امانة ... تشریح اور اگر صورت حال یہ ہو کہ لوٹے کی قیمت بارہ درہم ہو تو امام ابوحنیفہ فرماتے ہیں کہ مرتہن کونے کی پوری قیمت یعنی بارہ درہم کا ضامن ہوگا اور لوٹا مرتہن کی ملک ہوگا اور بارہ درہم مرہون کی جگہ رہن ہوں گے جب واہن قرض ادا کر دے تو مرہون کے قائم مقام یعنی بارہ دراہم کو لے گا۔ کیونکہ امام صاحب کے نزدیک اصل اعتبار و زن کا ہے جو یت اور دانت کا اعتبار نہیں ہے لیکن صورت حال یہ ہے کہ جہاں مرہون باعتبار وزن پورا کا پورا مضمون ہو تو اس کو باعتبار قیمت بھی پورا کو مضمون شمار کیا جائیگا اور جہاں وزن کا بعض حصہ مضمون ہے وہاں قیمت کا بھی بعض ہی حصہ مضمون ہو گا اور باقی امانت ہوگا۔ لیکن یہاں کیا کیا جائے یہاں تو پورا لوٹا باعتبار وزن مضمون ہے کیونکہ دین بھی دس درہم ہے اور اس کا وزن بھی دس درہم ہے تو جب پورا وزن مضمون ہوا تو قیمت بھی پوری مضمون ہوگئی اس وجہ سے امام صاحب نے یہاں فرمایا کہ پوری قیمت کا ضمان واجب ہوگا۔ اور عذر یہ بھی ہے کہ لوٹا جو ہر ہے اور اس کی جودت عرض ہے اور عرض کامل سے انفکاک محال ہے تو جب جو ہر پورا مضمون ہے تو بر بناء تبعیت جودت یعنی عرض کو بھی مانے گا اور پوری قیمت کا ضمان واجب ہو اور نہ جوہر کا مضمون اور عرض کا امانت ہونا لازم آتا اور یہ باطل ہے۔
And in the second aspect, and it is when its value is more than its weight, twelve (dirhams), according to Abu Hanifa he guarantees all of its value, and it becomes a pawn with him, because the criterion is weight according to him, not quality or inferiority. So if by weight all of it is guaranteed, its entirety is considered guaranteed; if some of it, then some. And this is because quality is subsidiary to substance, and when the original becomes guaranteed, it is impossible for the subsidiary to be a trust.
Source pages p. 244

Commentary
This passage discusses the second scenario of a broken pawn where the market value (12 dirhams) exceeds the weight (10 dirhams). Imam Abu Hanifa's ruling is that the mortgagee (murtahin) guarantees the entire value (12 dirhams), and this amount becomes a new pawn in place of the original vessel. The reasoning: the primary consideration is weight (wazn), not quality (jūdah) or inferiority (radā'ah). Since the weight of the vessel (10 dirhams) matches the debt (10 dirhams), the entire weight is 'guaranteed' (madhmun) as collateral. Because quality is an accident (arad) subsidiary to the substance (jawhar), once the substance is fully guaranteed, the quality must also be guaranteed. It is impossible for the substance to be guaranteed while the quality remains a trust (amānah). Therefore, the mortgagee must guarantee the full market value. The commentary clarifies that this is specific to Abu Hanifa's view; the positions of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani are not stated here but may differ.

Key Terms
جوهر (jawhar): Substance or essence of the pawn (the metal itself, as opposed to its quality).
عرض (arad): Accident or attribute; here, the quality (jūdah) is considered an accident that cannot be separated from the substance.
تبعیت (taba'iyyah): Subordination or following; quality follows the substance in liability.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, why must the mortgagee guarantee the full value (12 dirhams) when the pawn's weight is 10 dirhams?
A) Because the value determines the debt
B) Because the weight is the sole criterion, and the full weight is pledged; quality follows substance
C) Because the pawn is destroyed and the mortgagee is always liable for the market value
D) Because the debt is 10 dirhams and the value is 12, so the extra 2 are a penalty

Key Takeaway
When the weight of a pawn matches the debt, the full market value is guaranteed because quality follows substance and weight is the governing criterion.

Liability for Excess Value of Pledged Pot: Abu Hanifa vs. Abu Yusuf
Intra-Hanafi dispute on liability for a pledged copper pot when value exceeds weight

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi positions on pledgee liability when a pledged item's value exceeds its weight due to quality, and calculate the thamarah al-khilaf in dirhams.

Core Idea
In pledge, quality is subsidiary to substance for Abu Hanifa, but independently valuable for Abu Yusuf, leading to different liability.

When a pledged copper pot worth more than its weight is lost, should the pledgee (murtahin) pay the full market value or only a portion? This lesson unpacks a classic intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, revealing two distinct approaches to the role of quality (jūdat) in liability. By the end, you will not only know the positions but also grasp the legal reasoning behind each.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Note the facts: a copper pot weighing 10 dirhams is pledged for a 10-dirham debt, but its market value is 12 dirhams due to superior quality. The pot is lost, so how much must the pledgee pay?
The excess value (2 dirhams) is due to quality, not weight.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position and reasoning
Abu Hanifa rules the pledgee must pay the full 12 dirhams. His reasoning: the primary consideration is weight, not quality. Since the entire pot is liable by weight (debt = weight), the quality is subsidiary and must also be liable, otherwise a contradiction arises (substance liable but attribute a trust).
Key principle: al-ʿibra li-l-wazn (consideration is weight).
3
State Abu Yusuf's position and reasoning
Abu Yusuf rules the pledgee pays only 5/6 of the value (10 dirhams), while 1/6 of the pot remains as a pledge. He treats the increase in value due to quality as equivalent to an increase in weight (as if weight were 12 dirhams). His evidence: quality is inherently valuable (muttaqawwim), considered in exchanges of different genera and in sick person's transactions.
Key principle: al-jūdat muttaqawwima (quality is compensable).
4
Compare the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: Abu Hanifa's ruling gives no partial release of the pledged pot; the pledgee acquires the entire pot and owes 12 dirhams to the pledgor. Abu Yusuf's ruling entitles the pledgee to only 5/6 of the pot, with 1/6 remaining as pledge. The pledgor receives either 12 or 10 dirhams net liability.
The dispute hinges on whether quality can be separated from substance.
5
Evaluate the evidence
Abu Hanifa relies on the principle that quality is subsidiary (tabiʿ) and cannot be independent in liability. Abu Yusuf analogizes to cases where quality is considered (different genus sale, marad al-mawt). Both are valid qiyas but lead to different results. The text does not determine which is mufta bihi.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf within the school; both positions are transmitted in Zahir al-Riwayah.

Source Text

اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد - ۱۴ کے ہوں یا دوسری جنس کے دونوں جائز ہیں بس اس کا خیال رہے کہ سود کا شائبہ نہ ہونے پائے لہذا اگر درہم کے بجائے قیمت میں دینار رکھے تو عمدہ دینا ر ر کھنے میں کوئی حرج نہیں کیونکہ اختلاف جنس کی وجہ سے جودت مردائت کی وجہ سے کوئی خلل نہ ہوگا اور ربوالا زم نہ آئیگا۔ البتہ جب قیمت دراہم سے ہوتو وہ چاندی کھوئی ہونی چاہئے مرہون کے مثل تا کہ ربوا کا لزوم نہ ہو۔ بہر حال چونکہ احتیاط اول میں تھی اس لئے بدائع میں صرف اسی کا ذکر کیا گیا ہے اور گنجائش اس کی بھی ہے لہذا مصنف نے دونوں کو بیان کر دیا ہے۔ خلاصہ کلام خلاف جنس سے کھرا بال رکھنے کا حکم بطریق جواز ہے ورنہ اس کے عکس میں بھی کوئی مضائقہ نہیں ہے اور اتحاد جنس کی صورت میں کھوئے مال کا حکم بطریق وجوب ہے تا کہ سود نہ ہو جائے شروح ہدا یہ میں اس کو واضح نہیں کیا گیا اس لئے اصول کو سامنے رکھ کر جو بات سمجھ میں آئی وہ میں نے عرض کر دی ہے واللہ اعلم بالصواب۔
مذکورہ مسئلہ کی دوسری صورت
وفى الوجه الثاني وهو ما اذا كانت قيمته اكثر من وزنه اثنی عشر عند ابي حنيفة يضمن جميع قيمته وتكون رهنا عنده لان العبرة للوزن عنده لا للجودة والردائة فان كان باعتبار الوزن كله مضمونا يجعل كله مضمونا وان كان بعضه فبعضه وهذا لان الجودة تابعة للذات ومتى صار الاصل مضمونا استحال ان يكون التابع امانة
ترجمہ اور دوسری صورت میں اور وہ یہ ہے جبکہ لوٹے کی قیمت اس کے وزن سے زیادہ ہو یعنی بارہ در ہم تو ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک مرتہن لوٹے کی پوری قیمت کا ضامن ہوگا اور وہ قیمت مرتہن کے پاس رہن رہے گئی اس لئے کہ ان کے نزدیک اعتبار وزن کا ہے نہ کہ کھر نے اور کھوٹے ہونے کا پس اگر مر ہون وزن کے اعتبار سے پورا مضمون ہو تو باعتبار قیمت اس کے کل کو مضمون شمار کیا جائے گا اور اگر اس کا بعض ہو تو اس کے بعض کو ( باعتبار قیمت مضمون شمار کیا جائیگا ) اور یہ اس لئے کہ جودت ذات کے تابع ہے اور جب اصل مضمون ہوئی تو یہ محال ہو گیا کہ تابع امانت ہو۔
تشریح اور اگر صورت حال یہ ہو کہ لوٹے کی قیمت بارہ درہم ہو تو امام ابوحنیفہ فرماتے ہیں کہ مرتہن کونے کی پوری قیمت یعنی بارہ درہم کا ضامن ہوگا اور لوٹا مرتہن کی ملک ہوگا اور بارہ درہم مرہون کی جگہ رہن ہوں گے جب واہن قرض ادا کر دے تو مرہون کے قائم مقام یعنی بارہ دراہم کو لے گا۔ کیونکہ امام صاحب کے نزدیک اصل اعتبار و زن کا ہے جو یت اور دانت کا اعتبار نہیں ہے لیکن صورت حال یہ ہے کہ جہاں مرہون باعتبار وزن پورا کا پورا مضمون ہو تو اس کو باعتبار قیمت بھی پورا کو مضمون شمار کیا جائیگا اور جہاں وزن کا بعض حصہ مضمون ہے وہاں قیمت کا بھی بعض ہی حصہ مضمون ہو گا اور باقی امانت ہوگا۔
لیکن یہاں کیا کیا جائے یہاں تو پورا لوٹا باعتبار وزن مضمون ہے کیونکہ دین بھی دس درہم ہے اور اس کا وزن بھی دس درہم ہے تو جب پورا وزن مضمون ہوا تو قیمت بھی پوری مضمون ہوگئی اس وجہ سے امام صاحب نے یہاں فرمایا کہ پوری قیمت کا ضمان واجب ہوگا۔ اور عذر یہ بھی ہے کہ لوٹا جو ہر ہے اور اس کی جودت عرض ہے اور عرض کامل سے انفکاک محال ہے تو جب جو ہر پورا مضمون ہے تو بر بناء تبعیت جودت یعنی عرض کو بھی مانے گا اور پوری قیمت کا ضمان واجب ہو اور نہ جوہر کا مضمون اور عرض کا امانت ہونا لازم آتا اور یہ باطل ہے۔

امام صاحب کا مذہب ہے۔
۲۴۴
اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد - ۱۴
امام ابو یوسف کا نقطہ نظر
وعند ابي يوسف يضمن خمسة اسداس قيمته وتكون خمسة اسداس الا بريق له بالضمان وسدسه يفرز حتى لا يبقى الرهن شائعا ويكون مع قيمة خمسة اسداس المكسور رهنا فعنده تعتبر الجودة والرداءة و تجعل زيادة القيمة كزيادة الوزن كان وزنه اثنا عشر
ترجمہ اور ابو یوسف کے نزدیک مرتهن لوٹے کی قیمت کے ۵/۶ کا ضامن ہوگا اور لوٹے کا ۵/۶ ضمان کی وجہ سے مرتہن کی ملک ہوگا اور پر الگ کر لیا جائے گا یہاں تک کہ رہن شائع باقی نہ رہے اور یہ (سدس) ٹوٹے ہوئے لوٹے کے ۵/۶ کی قیمت کے ساتھ رہن ہوگا تو ابو یوسف کے نزدیک جودت وردائت کا اعتبار کیا گیا ہے اور قیمت کی زیادتی کو وزن کی زیادتی کے مثل کر دیا جائیگا گویا کہ اس کا وزن ۱۲ ور ہم ہے۔
تشریح صورت مذکورہ میں امام ابو یوسف کا مذہب یہ ہے کہ لوٹے کے چھ حصے کئے جائیں اس کے چھ حصوں میں سے پانچ ۵/۶ کی قیمت کا مرتبہن سے ضمان لیا جائے اور اس میں سے چھٹا حصہ جو باقی رہ گیا ہے اس کو الگ کر کے مع سابق قیمت کے مرتہن کے پاس رہن رکھا جائے گا اور لوٹے کا ۶ / ۵ مرتبہن کی ملکیت ہو گیا۔ کیونکہ وہ اس کا منعمان ادا کر چکا ہے اور ۶ / ۱ کا خلاصہ ۲/۱۲ اور ۶ / کا خلاصہ ۱۰/۱۲ ہے وفصلنا الحساب في درس السراجى.
بہر حال امام ابو یوسف نے وزن کے مثل جودت و ردائت کا اعتبار کیا ہے تو ان کے نزدیک قیمت کا زیادہ ہونا وزن کے زیادہ ہونے کے مثل ہے اور یوں شمار کیا گویا کہ اس کا وزن ہی ۱۲ دور ہم ہے۔
امام ابو یوسف کی دلیل
وهذا لان الجودة متقومة في ذاتها حتى تعتبر عند المقابلة بخلاف جنسها وفى تصرف المريض وان كانت لا تعتبر عند المقابلة بجنسها سمعا فامكن اعتبارها
ترجمہ اور یہ (جودت کا اعتبار ) اس لئے ہے کہ جودت بذات خود متقوم ہے یہاں تک کہ اس کی جنس کے خلاف مقابلہ کے وقت جودت کا اعتبار ہوتا ہے اور مریض کے تصرف میں اعتبار ہوتا ہے اگر چہ شریعت سے مع کی وجہ سے اپنی جنس کے مقابلہ کے وقت جودت کا اعتبار نہیں کیا جاتا تو ( رہن میں ) جودت کا اعتبار ممکن ہے۔ تشریح یہ ابو یوسف کی دلیل ہے کہ انہوں نے جودت کو قیمتی کیوں شمار کیا تو فرمایا کہ اگر کھری چاندی کے مقابلہ میں سونا ہو تو کھری چاندی کے اعتبار سے قیمت لگائی جائے گی اور اس میں کچھ اختلاف نہیں ہے اسی طرح اگر مریض نے مرض الموت میں سوکھرے درہم کو سو کھوٹے دراہم کے بدلہ میں بیچا تو صرف یہ تصرف تہائی مال سے معتبر ہو گا لہذا معلوم ہوا کہ جودت معتبر ہے لیکن جب جنس کے ساتھ مقابلہ ہو تو اس وقت جودت کا اعتبار نہیں ہوتا کیونکہ شریعت نے اس سے منع کر دیا ہے۔
Regarding the second scenario of the mentioned issue: In the second situation, when the value of the copper pot is more than its weight, e.g., twelve dirhams, according to Abu Hanifa, the pledgee (murtahin) is liable for the entire value, and that value remains as a pledge with him, because the consideration is weight, not quality or defect. So if the pledge is entirely liable in terms of weight, the entire value is considered liable; if partially, then partially. This is because quality is subsidiary to the substance, and when the substance becomes liable, it is impossible for the subsidiary to remain a trust. According to Abu Yusuf, the pledgee is liable for five-sixths of the value, and five-sixths of the pot becomes his property due to liability; one-sixth is separated so that the pledge does not remain undivided, and this sixth becomes a pledge together with the value of the broken five-sixths. Thus, according to him, quality and defect are considered, and the increase in value is treated like an increase in weight, as if its weight were twelve dirhams. Abu Yusuf's evidence: This is because quality is inherently valuable, such that it is considered when comparing with a different genus, and in the transaction of a sick person, even though it is not considered by revelation when comparing with its own genus, so it is possible to consider it.
Source pages p. 244

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning the ruling on a pledged copper pot when its value exceeds its weight due to superior quality. The discussion follows the author's order: first, the second scenario of the earlier ruling is introduced. Then, the position of Imam Abu Hanifa is presented: when the pot's value is twelve dirhams while its weight is ten, the pledgee is liable for the entire value (twelve dirhams), and that value becomes the pledge. The reason is that the primary consideration is weight, not quality. Since the entire pot is liable in terms of weight (the debt equals the weight), the value is fully liable as well, because quality is subsidiary to the substance. Next, the position of Imam Abu Yusuf is given: the pledgee is liable for five-sixths of the value, and that portion becomes his property. The remaining one-sixth is separated and remains as a pledge along with the value of the five-sixths. Abu Yusuf considers quality and defect, treating the increase in value as if it were an increase in weight. His evidence is that quality is inherently valuable, as it is considered when exchanging for a different genus (e.g., silver for gold) and in the transactions of a sick person (where quality affects valuation). However, it is not considered when exchanging for the same genus due to prohibition of riba. Since this case involves a pledge, not a sale of same genus, quality can be considered. The commentary thus clarifies the reasoning of both imams and the practical implications.

Key Terms
جودت (jūdat): Quality or fineness of the metal (e.g., silver or copper) in a pledged item.
ردائت (radā'at): Defect or poor quality of the metal.
ضمان (ḍamān): Liability or guarantee; here, the pledgee's liability to pay the excess value if the pledged item is lost or damaged.
رهن (rahn): Pledge or collateral; the item given as security for a debt.
قیمت (qīmat): Market value or price; here, the estimated value of the pot.
وزن (wazn): Weight; the physical weight of the metal.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Yusuf, why is the pledgee liable for only five-sixths of the value when a pledged copper pot (weight 10 dirhams, value 12 dirhams) is lost?
A) Because the pot's weight is only 10 dirhams, so the pledgee is liable for the weight only.
B) Because the quality is considered by treating the value increase as a weight increase, making the effective weight 12 dirhams, and the debt is 10 dirhams, so the ratio 10/12 = 5/6.
C) Because the pot is partly a trust and partly a guarantee, so the liability is split equally.
D) Because Abu Yusuf considers the entire value as liable but then deducts the debtor's equity.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school has two positions on whether quality (jūdat) is considered in pledge liability; Abu Hanifa holds full value liable, Abu Yusuf holds 5/6 liable, and the practical difference is the net amount the pledgee must pay.

Istihsan for Condition of Kafalah and Rahn in Sale
Istihsan proof and validity conditions for kafalah/rahn condition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on condition of kafalah and rahn in a sale contract, explain the istihsan proof, and identify the conditions for validity.

Core Idea
A condition of suretyship or pawn in sale is valid by istihsan when specified and the surety is present; otherwise it is corrupt.

This lesson examines the Hanafi position on inserting a condition of kafalah (suretyship) or rahn (pawn) into a sale contract. While generally a 'safqah dar safqah' (transaction within a transaction) is prohibited, the Hanafi school validates such conditions by istihsan due to their suitability to the contract's purpose of securing the price. We will walk through the istihsan proof and the specific conditions that determine validity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the apparent prohibition
Recognize that adding a condition like kafalah or rahn to a sale is literarily a 'safqah dar safqah' (transaction within a transaction), which is generally prohibited in Hanafi fiqh.
2
Understand the istihsan proof
The author argues that despite the literal objection, the condition is suitable (mulaim) to the contract because both kafalah and rahn serve to secure the price, which is obligatory. This suitability overrides the literal prohibition via istihsan.
3
Separate word and meaning
When the condition is specified (surety present, pawn defined), the meaning of suitability prevails and the contract is valid. When unspecified, the wording of prohibition prevails and the contract is corrupt (fasid).
4
Apply the conditions for validity
Ensure two conditions: (1) the surety (kafil) must be present in the contract session, and (2) the pawn (rahn) must be specified (ma'een). If either is missing, the contract becomes corrupt.
5
Handle the edge case of absent surety
If the surety is absent at the time of contract but later attends the session and accepts the suretyship before the parties separate, the contract becomes valid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
استحسانی دلیل
وجه الاستحسان انه شرط ملائم للعقه لأن الكفالة والرهن للاستيثاق وإنه يلائم الوجوب ترجمہ استحسان کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ یہ ایسی شرط ہے جو عقد بیج کے مناسب ہے اس لئے کفالت اور رہن مضبوطی شمن کے لئے ہے اور یہ وجوب شمن کے مناسب ہے۔ تشریح یہ استحسان کی دلیل ہے کہ اگر چہ عقد بیع اس کو مقتضی نہیں لیکن یہ عقد بیع کے تقاضہ کے مخالف بھی نہیں بلکہ مناسب ہے کیونکہ رہن اور کفالت کا مقصد یہ ہے کہ یمن کی مضبوطی حاصل ہو جائے اور شمن واجب ہے ہی تو اس کو وجوب شمن کے مناسب قرار دیا جائیگا تو یہ شرط ایسی ہے جیسے شمن کے کھرے ہونے کی شرط لگانا ۔
کفیل مجلس میں حاضر ہو اور رہن معین ہو تو اس کا حکم
فاذا كان الكفيل حاضرا فى المجلس والرهن معينا اعتبرنا فيه المعنى وهو ملائم فصح المعقد وان لم يكن الرهن ولا الكفيل معينا او كان الكفيل غائيا حتى افتر قالم يبق معنى الكفالة والرهن للجهالة فبقى الاعتبار لعينه فيفسد ولو كان غائبا فحضر في المجلس وقبل صح
ترجمہ پس جب کہ کفیل مجلس میں حاضر ہو اور بہن معین ہو تو ہم نے اس میں معنی کا اعتبار کیا ہے اورمعنی عقد کے مناسب ہیں پس عقد صحیح ہوگا اور جبکہ رہن اور کفیل معین نہ ہوں یا کفیل غائب ہو یہاں تک کہ وہ دونوں جدا ہو گئے تو کفالت اور رہن کے معنی جہالت کی وجہ سے باقی نہیں رہے تو عین شرط کا اعتبار باقی رہا پسن عقد فاسد ہو جائے اور اگر کفیل غائب ہو پس وہ مجلس میں حاضر ہو گیا اور کفالت کو قبول کر لیا تو عقد صحیح ہوگا۔ تشریح صورت مذکورہ میں رہن اور کفالت کو استحساناً جب جائز کہا گیا ہے جبکہ مرہون اور کفیل متعین ہوں ورنہ جہالت کی وجہ سے عقد فاسد ہو جائے گا اور اگر کفیل متعین ہے لیکن مجلس عقد میں حاضر نہیں تو اب بھی عقد فاسد ہوگا کیونکہ ہوسکتا ہے کہ کفیل کفیل بنے کو قبول نہ کرے اس تفصیل کے بعد سمجھئے۔
سوال. معین ہونے کی صورت میں آپ نے اس کو جائز کہا اور غیر معین ہونے کی صورت میں عقد کو فاسد کہا آخر کیوں؟ جواب ... کفالت اور رہن کی جو شرط عقد میں لگی ہے اس میں لفظ اور معنی دونوں کا لحاظ ہے لفظ کے اعتبار سے یہ صفقہ در صفقہ ہے اور معنوی اعتبار سے یہ ایسی شرط ہے جو عقد کے مناسب ہے تو ہم نے متعین ہونے کی صورت میں معنی کا اعتبار کیا ہے اور عقد کو جائز قرار دیا ہے اور غیر متعین ہونے کی صورت میں ہم نے لفظ کا اعتبار کیا ہے اور عقد کو فاسد قرار دیا ہے جیسے من کے اندر جمع اور واحد لفظی اور معنوی اعتبار سے ملحوظ ہیں اس وجہ سے اس کی جانب واحد اور جمع کی ضمیر راجع ہو جاتی ہے، اور اگر کفیل پہلے سے مجلس میں نہیں تھا لیکن جدا ہونے سے پہلے حاضر ہو گیا اور کفالت کو قبول کر لیا تو جائز ہے۔ تنبیہ دلیل میں حضرت مصنف کا صرف للجمالہ کہنا مخدوش ہے کیونکہ کفیل غائب میں یہ علت فٹ نہیں ہوگی لہذا اس کے بعد یہ اضافہ در مناسب تھا۔ والجواز ان لا يقبل الكفالة عند حضوره.
**Istihsan Proof:** The basis of istihsan is that it is a condition suitable to the contract because suretyship and pawn are for security, and it is suitable for the obligation. **Translation:** The proof of istihsan is that it is a condition that is suitable for the contract of sale; because suretyship and pawn are for strengthening the price, and it is suitable for the obligation of the price. **Explanation:** This is the proof of istihsan: even though the contract of sale does not necessitate it, it is not contrary to the requirement of the sale contract; rather it is suitable, because the purpose of pawn and suretyship is to secure the price, and the price is obligatory, so it will be considered suitable to the obligation of the price. So this condition is like the condition of the price being genuine.

**Ruling when the surety is present in the session and the pawn is specified:** So when the surety is present in the session and the pawn is specified, we consider the meaning in it, and the meaning is suitable, so the contract is valid. If neither the pawn nor the surety is specified, or if the surety is absent until they separate, then the meaning of suretyship and pawn does not remain due to ignorance, so the consideration remains for its wording, so it becomes corrupt. If the surety was absent but then attended the session and accepted, then it is valid. **Translation:** So when the surety is present in the session and the pawn is specified, we consider the meaning, and the meaning is suitable to the contract, so the contract will be valid. When the pawn and surety are not specified, or the surety is absent until they separate, then the meaning of suretyship and pawn does not remain due to ignorance, so the consideration of the wording remains, so the contract becomes corrupt. If the surety was absent but then attended the session and accepted the suretyship, then the contract will be valid. **Explanation:** In the mentioned case, pawn and suretyship are deemed permissible by istihsan only when the pawned item and surety are specified; otherwise the contract becomes corrupt due to ignorance. And if the surety is specified but not present in the contract session, then also the contract is corrupt because it is possible that the surety may not accept being a surety. Understand this detail.

**Question:** In the case of specification you said it is permissible and in the case of non-specification you said the contract is corrupt. Why? **Answer:** In the condition of suretyship and pawn that is inserted in the contract, both word and meaning are considered. From the perspective of wording, it is a transaction within a transaction; from the perspective of meaning, it is a condition suitable to the contract. So in the case of specification we consider the meaning and declare the contract valid, and in the case of non-specification we consider the wording and declare the contract corrupt. For example, in 'man' the plural and singular are considered verbally and meaning-wise, therefore the pronoun refers to both singular and plural. And if the surety was not present initially but attended before separation and accepted the suretyship, it is permissible. **Note:** The author's (Marghinani) statement 'only due to ignorance' is objectionable because this cause does not fit in the case of an absent surety; therefore the addition 'and its permissibility is that he does not accept suretyship when attending' was appropriate.
Source pages p. 247

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof (istihsan) about the condition of suretyship (kafalah) and pawn (rahn) in a sale contract. The author first presents the istihsan proof: although the sale contract does not require such a condition, it is suitable because both suretyship and pawn serve to secure the price, which is obligatory. The condition is therefore valid by istihsan, not by direct analogy to the contract's requisites. The ruling then details the conditions for validity: the surety must be present in the contract session, and the pawn must be specified. If either is unspecified, the contract becomes corrupt (fasid) due to ignorance. If the surety is absent but attends and accepts before the parties separate, the contract is valid. The question-and-answer section clarifies why specification matters: when specified, the meaning (suitability) prevails; when unspecified, the wording (transaction within a transaction) prevails, making the contract corrupt. The note criticizes the original Hidayah text for stating 'due to ignorance' as the sole reason for corruption in the absent surety case, because the real issue is that the absent surety may not accept. Thus the addition corrects this by stating that the permissibility is conditional upon the surety's acceptance when he appears.

Key Terms
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference; a method to depart from strict analogy (qiyas) in favor of a more suitable ruling based on a stronger evidence.
کفالت (kafalah): Suretyship; guaranteeing the obligation of another.
رہن (rahn): Pawn or pledge; giving an asset as security for a debt.
صفقہ در صفقہ (safqah dar safqah): Literally 'transaction within a transaction'; a condition that adds another contract within the main contract, which is generally prohibited.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Under which condition does the Hanafi school validate the condition of kafalah and rahn in a sale contract?
A) Always, regardless of specification
B) Only when the surety is present and the pawn is specified
C) Only when the surety is absent
D) Only when the pawn is unspecified

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school validates conditions of suretyship and pawn in a sale by istihsan when the surety is present and the pawn is specified, based on the suitability of the condition to the contract's purpose.

Buyer's Refusal to Deliver Pawn: Intra-Hanafi Dispute and Seller's Option
Intra-Hanafi dispute on compulsion for pawn delivery

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on compulsion for delivering a pawn and explain the seller's option when the buyer refuses.

Core Idea
A pawn is a gratuitous act; the buyer cannot be compelled to deliver it, but the seller may rescind.

When a sale is concluded with a condition that the buyer will give a pawn as security, what happens if the buyer later refuses to hand over the pawn? This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Zufar. Abu Hanifa holds that the buyer cannot be compelled because rahn is a gratuitous contract, while Zufar argues it becomes a binding right of the sale. The passage then explains the seller's remedy: he has an option (khiyar) to either waive the pawn or annul the sale.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core issue
The issue is whether a buyer who agreed to provide a pawn as part of a sale can be legally forced (jabr) to deliver that pawn.
The dispute is within the Hanafi school between Abu Hanifa and Zufar.
2
State the Hanafi (Abu Hanifa's) position
Abu Hanifa: The buyer is not compelled to deliver the pawn because rahn is a gratuitous contract (tabarru') from the pledgor's side, and there is no compulsion in gratuitous acts.
This is the Zahir al-Riwayah position and the mufta bihi.
3
Analyze Zufar's opposing argument
Zufar argues that the pawn, when stipulated in the sale, becomes a right of the sale, similar to a binding agency (wakalah) in a pawn transaction. Since the sale is binding, the pawn also becomes binding, so the buyer can be compelled.
Zufar's proof uses analogy (qiyas) with agency.
4
Examine the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response restates that rahn is fundamentally a gratuitous act; compulsion is not permissible in such acts. The analogy with agency does not apply because agency, though a gratuitous contract, can become binding under specific conditions, but rahn does not share that characteristic.
The distinction hinges on the nature of the contract: gratuitous vs. commutative.
5
Understand the seller's option (khiyar)
Since the buyer cannot be compelled, the seller has a choice: either waive the pawn and accept the sale without it, or rescind the sale entirely. This is because the pawn was a desired attribute (wasf marghub fih) that the seller only agreed to with that condition.
The option is lost if the buyer pays the full price immediately or offers the value of the pawn as alternative security.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مشتری مرہون کو سپر دکھنے سے رک جائے تو کیا حکم ہے
ولو امتنع المشترى عن تسليم الرهن لم يجبر عليه وقال زفر يجبر لان الرهن اذا شرط في البيع صارحقا من حقوقه كالوكالة المشروطة فى الرهن فيلزمه بلزومه ونحن نقول الرهن عقد تبرع من جانب الراهن على ما بيناه ولا جبر على التبرعات
ترجمہ اور اگر مشتری مرہون کو سپر ذکر نے اسے رک جائے تو اس پر جب نہیں کیا جائیگا اور مرنے فرمایا کہ جب کیا جائیگا اس لئے کہ رہن جب بیچ میں مشروط ہوا تو رہن حقوق بیچ میں سے ایک حق ہو گیا جیسے وہ و عمالت جو رہن میں مشروط ہے تو مشتری پر بیچ کے لازم ہونے کی وجہ سے رہن لازم ہو جائے گا اور ہم کہتے ہیں کہ رہن ایک عقد تبرع ہے راہن کی جانب سے اس تفصیل کے مطابق جس کو ہم بیان کر چکے ہیں اور تبرعات پر جبر نہیں ہوتا۔ تشریح عقد مذکور مع شرط رہن طے ہو گیا تھا لیکن اب مشتری رہن دینے سے منع کرتا ہے تو کیا اس پر جبر جائز ہے تو اس میں ہمارا اور امام زفر کا اختلاف ہے ہم نے کہا کہ ماقبل میں تفصیل گذر چکی ہے کہ عقدر من تبرع ہے اور اصول مسلم ہے کہ تبرعات پر جبر نہیں ہوا کرتا اس لئے مشتری پر جبر نہیں ہوگا۔
امام زفر فر ماتے ہیں اگر راہن نے عادل یا مرتہن کو وکیل بنا دیا کہ دین کی ادائیگی کا وقت آنے پر مرہون کوفروخت کر دے تو یہ وکالت لازم ہے اب راہن وکیل کو وکالت سے معزول نہیں کر سکتا اسی طرح یہاں بھی جب برہن عقد میں طے ہو گیا تو لازم ہوگا تو جب بیچ لازم ہے تو رہن بھی لازم ہے اور حق واجبی کی ادائیگی کے لئے جبر جائز ہے لہذا اس پر جبر جائز ہوگا ۔۔
بائع پر جبر ہے یا نہیں
ولكن البائع بالخيار ان شاء رضى بترك الرهن وان شاء فسخ البيع لانه وصف مرغوب فيه ومارضى الابه فيتخير بفواته الا ان يدفع المشترى الثمن حالا لحصول المقصود او يدفع قيمة الرهن رهنا لان يد الاستيفاء تثبت على المعني وهو القيمة
ترجمہ لیکن بائع اختیار کے ساتھ ہے اگر چاہے رہن چھوڑنے پر راضی ہو جائے اور چاہے تو بیع کو مسخ کر دے اس لئے کہ رہن ایسا وصف ہے جو مرغوب فیہ ہے اور بائع راضی نہیں ہوا مگر رہن کے ساتھ تو بائع اس کے فوات کی وجہ سے مختار ہوگا مگر یہ کہ مشتری ثمن نقد دیدے مقصود کے حاصل ہونے کی وجہ سے یا مشتری مرہون کی قیمت رہن دیدے اس لئے کہ وصولیابی کا قبضہ معنی پر ثابت ہوتا ہے او
**What is the ruling if the buyer refuses to deliver the pawn?**
And if the buyer refuses to deliver the pawn, he is not compelled to do so. Zufar said: He is compelled, because when the pawn is stipulated in the sale, it becomes one of its rights, like the agency stipulated in the pawn, so it becomes binding upon him due to the binding nature of the sale. But we (Hanafis) say: The pawn is a gratuitous contract from the side of the pledgor, as we have explained, and there is no compulsion over gratuitous acts. **Translation:** And if the buyer refuses to deliver the pawn, he will not be compelled. Zufar said: He will be compelled because when the pawn is stipulated in the sale, it becomes a right among the rights of the sale, like the agency that is stipulated in the pawn, so it becomes binding upon him due to the binding nature of the sale. But we say that the pawn is a gratuitous contract on the part of the pledgor, and there is no compulsion over gratuitous acts. **Explanation:** The sale contract with the condition of pawn was agreed, but now the buyer refuses to give the pawn. Is compulsion permissible? In this, there is a dispute between us and Imam Zufar. We said that the detail has passed earlier that the contract is a gratuitous act, and it is an established principle that there is no compulsion over gratuitous acts. Therefore, the buyer will not be compelled.

Imam Zufar says: If the pledgor appoints the just person or the mortgagee as agent to sell the pawn at the time of debt maturity, this agency is binding, and the pledgor cannot remove the agent. Similarly here, when the pawn is agreed upon in the contract, it becomes binding; when the sale is binding, the pawn is also binding, and compulsion for the payment of an obligatory right is permissible. Therefore, compulsion is permissible.

**Is there compulsion on the seller?**
But the seller has an option: if he wishes, he may agree to the waiver of the pawn; if he wishes, he may rescind the sale, because the pawn is a desired attribute, and he was not satisfied except with it, so he has an option due to its loss—unless the buyer pays the price immediately, for attaining the purpose, or pays the value of the pawn as a pawn, because the hand of receiving is established on the meaning, which is the value. **Translation:** But the seller has an option: if he wishes, he may agree to leaving the pawn, and if he wishes, he may rescind the sale, because the pawn is a desired attribute, and the seller was not satisfied except with it, so he will have an option due to its loss—unless the buyer pays the price immediately due to attaining the purpose, or pays the value of the pawn as a pawn, because the possession of receipt is established on the meaning, which is the value.
Source pages p. 248

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the buyer's refusal to deliver the pawn after agreeing to a sale with a condition of pawn. The main Hanafi position (Abu Hanifa) holds that the buyer is not compelled to deliver the pawn because rahn is a gratuitous contract (tabarru'), and there is no compulsion in gratuitous acts. Imam Zufar argues that since the pawn was stipulated in the sale, it becomes a right of the sale, binding like agency, and thus the buyer can be compelled. The text then explains the seller's remedy: the seller has an option (khiyar) to either waive the pawn and proceed with the sale, or rescind the sale entirely, because the pawn was a desired attribute. This option is lost if the buyer pays the price immediately or offers the value of the pawn as security. The commentary clarifies the reasoning and the practical consequence.

Key Terms
جبر (jabr): Compulsion; legally forcing someone to fulfill an obligation.
تبرع (tabarru'): Gratuitous act; a contract or act done without equivalent consideration.
خيار (khiyar): Option; the right of a party to annul or confirm a contract due to a defect or absence of desired attribute.
خيار الوصف (khiyar al-wasf): Option due to absence of a desired attribute; the seller may rescind if a stipulated attribute is missing.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what happens if the buyer refuses to deliver the pawn after agreeing to a sale with that condition?
A) The buyer is compelled by the court to deliver the pawn
B) The seller is compelled to accept the sale without the pawn
C) The seller has an option to either waive the pawn or rescind the sale
D) The sale becomes void automatically

Key Takeaway
The buyer cannot be compelled to deliver a pawn because it is a gratuitous act, but the seller may either waive the pawn or rescind the sale.

6 min
Buyer Cannot Be Compelled to Deliver Stipulated Mortgage; Seller Has Option
Dispute with Zufar on compulsion to deliver rahn; seller's option

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that a buyer is not compelled to deliver a stipulated mortgage and explain the seller's khiyar (option) to proceed without the mortgage or rescind the sale.

Core Idea
A stipulated mortgage is not enforceable by compulsion; it is a gratuitous contract, but the seller may choose to proceed or rescind.

In this lesson, we examine a specific dispute within the Hanafi school regarding a sale conditioned on a mortgage. The majority hold that the buyer cannot be forced to deliver the mortgage, while Imam Zufar argues otherwise. Understanding this ruling illuminates the Hanafi distinction between binding and voluntary obligations in contracts and the legal mechanism of khiyar for loss of a desirable attribute.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
State the majority Hanafi position: the buyer is not compelled to deliver the stipulated mortgage. The seller has the option to either proceed without the mortgage or rescind the sale.
This is the mufta bihi position from the Hanafi school.
2
Understand Zufar's Argument
Imam Zufar holds that the buyer is compelled, drawing an analogy to a binding agency stipulated in a mortgage contract. He argues that if the mortgage is stipulated in the sale, it becomes a right of the sale and thus binding.
Zufar's analogy relies on the idea that a condition becomes part of the contract's obligations.
3
Analyze the Hanafi Response
The Hanafi majority responds that the mortgage is a gratuitous contract (tabarru') and compulsion does not apply to voluntary acts. The principle is established that there is no compulsion in tabarru'.
This is a key usul principle: voluntary acts are not enforceable by coercion.
4
Explore the Seller's Option
Since the mortgage is a desirable attribute (wasf marghub fih), its loss gives the seller the right to rescind (khiyar) unless the buyer fulfills the objective by paying the price immediately or providing equivalent value as collateral.
The option exists because the seller only agreed to the sale with the mortgage.
5
Note Conditions Removing the Option
The seller loses the option if the buyer pays the price in cash or provides the value of the mortgaged property as a mortgage. In such cases, the objective (right of recovery) is achieved.
The right of recovery is over the value, not the specific asset.

And if the buyer refrains from handing over the mortgaged property, he is not forced to do so. Zufar said: He is forced, because when the mortgage is stipulated in the sale, it becomes one of the rights of the sale, like the agency stipulated in the mortgage, so it binds him by the binding of the sale. We say: The mortgage is a gratuitous contract from the side of the mortgagor, as we have explained, and there is no compulsion in gratuitous contracts. Translation: And if the buyer refrains from handing over the mortgaged property, he is not forced to do so, and Zufar said that he is forced, because when the mortgage is stipulated in the sale, it becomes one of the rights of the sale, like the agency that is stipulated in the mortgage, so the mortgage becomes binding on the buyer due to the binding of the sale. We say that the mortgage is a gratuitous contract from the side of the mortgagor, according to the detail we have explained, and gratuitous contracts are not subject to compulsion. Commentary: The mentioned contract was agreed upon with the condition of mortgage, but now the buyer refuses to give the mortgage. Is compulsion permissible upon him? There is a difference of opinion between us and Imam Zufar. We said that the detail has passed earlier that the contract of mortgage is a gratuitous act, and it is an established principle that gratuitous acts are not subject to compulsion. Therefore, the buyer will not be compelled. Imam Zufar says: If the mortgagor appointed a just person or the mortgagee as an agent to sell the mortgaged property when the time of payment arrives, that agency is binding. Now the mortgagor cannot dismiss the agent. Similarly here, when the mortgage was agreed upon in the contract, it becomes binding. So when the sale is binding, the mortgage is also binding, and compulsion is permissible for the fulfillment of a due right. Therefore, compulsion is permissible on him. On the seller: Is there compulsion or not? But the seller has the option: if he wishes, he may agree to forego the mortgage, and if he wishes, he may rescind the sale, because the mortgage is a desirable attribute, and he only agreed to the sale with it. So he has an option due to its loss, unless the buyer pays the price immediately to achieve the objective, or the buyer gives the value of the mortgaged property as a mortgage, because the right of recovery is established over the meaning, which is the value. Translation: But the seller has the option: if he wishes, he may agree to leave the mortgage, and if he wishes, he may rescind the sale, because the mortgage is a desirable attribute, and the seller did not agree except with the mortgage. So he will have an option due to its loss, unless the buyer pays the price in cash to achieve the objective, or the buyer gives the value of the mortgaged property as a mortgage, because the right of recovery is established over the meaning, and the meaning is the value. Commentary: In the mentioned scenario, according to us, compulsion is not permissible on the buyer, but what about the seller? Does he also have some option or not? So it is said that he also has an option: if he wishes, he may hand over the sale to the buyer without the mortgage and collect his due on time, and if he wishes, he may rescind the sale because he was satisfied with the credit sale due to the mortgage. So due to the loss of the desirable attribute, he will have an option. But if the buyer pays the price instead of the mortgage, then the seller no longer has an option because the objective is achieved. Or if the buyer gives the value of the mortgaged property as a mortgage instead, then also the seller no longer has an option because the objective is achieved. How is that? Because the physical mortgaged property is a trust, and the right of recovery is established for the mortgagee over the monetary value, and the monetary value is the price that is being given. The author has expressed this meaning as 'meaning'.
Source pages p. 248

Commentary
This passage deals with the situation where a sale is conditioned upon the buyer providing a mortgage (rahn), but the buyer later refuses to deliver the mortgaged item. The Hanafi ruling, based on the principle that rahn is a gratuitous contract (tabarru'), is that the buyer cannot be compelled (jabr) to deliver it. Imam Zufar disagrees, drawing an analogy to a binding agency stipulated in the contract. The Hanafi response emphasizes that compulsion does not apply to voluntary transactions. However, the seller is given a choice: he may either proceed with the sale without the mortgage or rescind the contract entirely. This option exists because the mortgage was a material condition of the sale. The seller loses this option if the buyer pays the price immediately or provides an equivalent value as collateral, as the essential objective (the right of recovery) is then met. The passage clarifies the Hanafi position on the enforceability of stipulations in contracts and the limits of compulsion in voluntary acts.

Key Terms
رهن (rahn): A contract where property is given as security for a debt, but the debt is not repaid; the property remains in the debtor's possession or is held by the creditor as a trust.
تبرع (tabarru'): A voluntary act or donation without obligation; a gratuitous contract.
جبر (jabr): Legal compulsion to perform an act.
خیار (khiyar): The right to rescind or confirm a contract due to a deficiency or missing condition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) The seller has no recourse; the sale becomes void automatically.
C) The seller may either proceed without the mortgage or rescind the sale.
D) The seller must demand the mortgage from a court.

Key Takeaway
A stipulated mortgage is not enforceable by compulsion; the seller's option to proceed or rescind preserves the balance between freedom of contract and right to rescind.

Saying 'Hold This Cloth Until I Pay' Makes It a Mortgage (Rahn)
Dispute on whether 'hold until I pay' creates rahn or wadi'ah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that such words create a valid rahn, identify the key principle of 'ibrah fi al-'uqud li al-ma'ani, and compare the opposing view of Zufar/Abu Yusuf.

Core Idea
Contracts are judged by their meanings, not words — so 'hold until I pay' creates a mortgage, not a deposit.

This passage from al-Jami' al-Saghir presents a classic Hanafi dispute: does a buyer's instruction to 'hold this cloth until I pay' create a mortgage or a deposit? The answer turns on a foundational principle: contracts are interpreted by their underlying intentions. Let's explore the proof and the intra-madhab disagreement.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the two competing classifications
The buyer says to the seller, 'Hold this cloth until I pay you the price.' The question: does this make the cloth a mortgage (rahn) or a deposit (wadi'ah)?
The act is already purchased; the seller is holding it for payment.
2
State the Hanafi position and its proof
The Hanafi school (Abu Hanifa, Muhammad) rules it is a rahn. The proof is the principle that contracts are judged by meanings, not words. The meaning here is detention for security, which is the reality of rahn.
The analogy with kafalah/hawalah illustrates the principle: if one says 'kafalah on condition of discharge,' it is actually hawalah because the meaning overrides the wording.
3
Examine the opposing view of Zufar and Abu Yusuf
Zufar and a transmission from Abu Yusuf hold it is a deposit (wadi'ah). Their argument: the word 'hold' is ambiguous, and the lighter obligation (deposit) should be presumed unless explicitly specified as a debt.
This is based on giving priority to the less burdensome interpretation.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response: the specific context (sale on credit, holding until payment) removes ambiguity; the intention is clearly for security. The lighter assumption does not apply when context clarifies intent.
The analogy with explicit mention of debt ('take it against your debt') further supports that meaning determines classification.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) and mufta bihi
If it is rahn, the seller holds as mortgagee with rights to claim value if unpaid; if wadi'ah, the seller holds as trustee with no such right. The mufta bihi is rahn.
The majority Hanafi position is relied upon for fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ومن اشترى ثوبا بدراهم فقال للبائع امسك هذا الثوب حتى اعطيك الثمن فالثوب رهن لانه اتى بما ينبنى عن معنى الرهن وهو الحبس الى وقت الإعطاء والعبرة في العقود للمعانى حتى كانت الكفالة بشرط برائة الاصيل حوالة والحوالة في ضد ذالك كفالة ترجمہ محمد نے جامع صغیر میں فرمایا اور جس نے دراہم کے بدلہ کپڑا خریدا پس اس نے بائع سے کہا کہ اس کپڑے کو رکھ لے یہاں تک کہ میں تجھے ثمن دیدوں پس کپڑا رہن ہے اس لئے کہ وہ ایسے الفاظ لایا ہے جو رہن کے معنی کی خبر دیتے ہیں اور وہ اعطاء ثمن کے وقت تک روکنا ہے اور عقود میں معانی کا اعتبار ہے یہاں تک کہ کفالت اصیل کی برائت کی شرط کے ساتھ حوالہ ہے اور اسکی ضد میں حوالہ کفالت ہے۔ تشریح زید نے خالد سے ایک کپڑا خریدا پھر اس کپڑے کے بارے میں یا کوئی اور دوسرا کپڑا ہو اس کے بارے میں زید خالد سے کہتا ہے کہ جب تک میں تیرا ثمن نہ دوں اس کپڑے کو رکھ لے تو یہ کپڑا خالد کے پاس رہن ہے یا امانت : تو امام زفر نے اس کو ودیعت کہا ہے اور ہم نے اس کو رہن کہا ہے ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ اگر چہ زید نے رہن کے الفاظ تو نہیں بولے مگر رہن کے معنی اس نے بولے ہیں کیونکہ اس نے کہا ہے کہ ثمن دینے تک اس کو رکھ لے اور یہی رہن بلک حقیقت ہے اور عقود میں الفاظ کا اعتبار نہیں بلکہ معانی کا اعتبار ہے اس کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ کفالت میں اصیل بری الذمہ نہیں ہوتا بلکہ اصیل اور کفیل دونوں سے مطالبہ کیا جاسکتا ہے اور حوالہ میں اصیل بری الذمہ ہوتا ہے تو اگر کفالت کو حوالہ کہا جائے تو یہ غلط ہے لہذا معلوم ہوا کہ عقود میں معانی کا اعتبار ہے الفاظ کا نہیں۔ امام زفر کا نقطہ نظر وقال زفر لا يكون رهنا ومثله عن ابى يوسف لان قوله امسک یحتمل الرهن ويحتمل الإيداع والثاني أقلهما فيقضى بثبوته بخلاف ما اذا قال امر بدینک او بمالک لانه لما قابله بالدين فقد عين جهة الرهن
Muhammad said in al-Jami' al-Saghir: And whoever buys a cloth for dirhams and then says to the seller, 'Hold this cloth until I give you the price,' then the cloth is a mortgage, because he brought words that convey the meaning of mortgage, which is detention until the time of payment. And consideration in contracts is for meanings, such that suretyship with a condition of the principal's discharge is a transfer of debt, and its opposite, transfer of debt, is suretyship. Translation: Muhammad said in al-Jami' al-Saghir: And whoever buys a cloth for dirhams and then says to the seller, 'Hold this cloth until I give you the price,' then the cloth is a mortgage, because he brought words that indicate the meaning of mortgage, and that is detention until the time of giving the price. And consideration in contracts is for meanings, such that suretyship with a condition of the principal's discharge is a transfer of debt, and its opposite, transfer of debt, is suretyship. Commentary: Zayd bought a cloth from Khalid, then regarding that cloth or another cloth, Zayd says to Khalid: 'Hold this cloth until I give you your price.' Is this cloth with Khalid a mortgage or a trust? Imam Zufar said it is a deposit (wadi'ah), and we say it is a mortgage. Our proof is that although Zayd did not use the specific words of mortgage, he expressed the meaning of mortgage, because he said 'hold it until I give the price,' and that is the reality of mortgage. And in contracts, consideration is not for words but for meanings. The proof of this is that in suretyship, the principal is not free from liability; rather, both the principal and the surety can be demanded. And in transfer of debt, the principal is free from liability. So if suretyship is called a transfer of debt, it would be wrong. Therefore, it is established that in contracts, consideration is for meanings, not for words. Imam Zufar's viewpoint: Zufar said it is not a mortgage, and a similar view is reported from Abu Yusuf, because his words 'hold' can mean either mortgage or deposit, and the second (deposit) is the lighter (obligation), so it is given priority. Unlike if he said 'take it against your debt' or 'against your property', because he then paired it with the debt, so he specified the nature of mortgage.
Source pages p. 249

Commentary
This passage from al-Jami' al-Saghir by Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani discusses the case of a buyer who purchases a cloth on credit and tells the seller to hold the cloth until the price is paid. The ruling is that this creates a valid mortgage (rahn) even though the word 'rahn' was not explicitly used, because the meaning (detaining the item as security for payment) is present. The Hanafi principle is that contracts are judged by their meanings and intentions, not by the literal words. This is illustrated by the contrasting cases of suretyship (kafalah) and transfer of debt (hawalah): if someone says he is surety on condition that the principal is discharged, it is actually a hawalah, not kafalah. Imam Zufar and Abu Yusuf disagree, arguing that the word 'hold' is ambiguous and could mean a deposit (wadi'ah), and since the least assumption is that the seller is a trustee, it should be treated as a deposit unless there is explicit mention of debt. The Hanafi school rejects this, insisting that the context and intention determine the contract type. The passage also notes that if the buyer says 'take it against your debt', that unequivocally makes it a mortgage.

Key Terms
رهن (rahn): A contract where a buyer gives possession of an item to the seller as security for a deferred price, with the item being held as a trust and the seller having a right over its value.
ودیعت (wadi'ah): A contract where one entrusts property to another to keep for free, without compensation; the holder is a trustee (amin).
عبرة فی العقود للمعانی ('ibrah fi al-'uqud li al-ma'ani): The principle that contracts are judged by their underlying meanings and intentions, not the literal words used.
کفالة (kafalah): Suretyship: a contract where one person (the surety) becomes liable for a debt along with the original debtor.
حوالة (hawalah): Transfer of debt: a contract where a debtor transfers the debt to another person who becomes solely liable; the original debtor is discharged.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A buyer says to the seller: 'Hold this cloth until I pay you the price.' According to the Hanafi school, this creates:
A) A deposit (wadi'ah) because the word 'hold' is ambiguous.
B) A mortgage (rahn) because the meaning of detention for security is present.
C) A sale (bay') because the cloth is already purchased.
D) A partnership because both parties share possession.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school prioritizes meaning over wording in contracts, so 'hold until I pay' creates a mortgage, not a deposit.

Validity of Pledge by Intended Meaning: The Cloth Scenario
Ruling with proof that a pledge is valid based on intended meaning, with intra-Hanafi dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school validates a pledge based on intended meaning and evaluate the intra-Hanafi dispute with Imam Zufar and Abu Yusuf.

Core Idea
Contracts are judged by intended meanings, not literal words.

This lesson examines a fundamental Hanafi principle: the validity of a pledge (rahn) can be established through the intended meaning, even without the word 'rahn'. We will explore a scenario from al-Jami' al-Saghir where a buyer tells the seller to hold the cloth until payment. The Hanafi position holds this as rahn, while Imam Zufar and Abu Yusuf consider it wadi'ah. Understanding the reasoning behind both views strengthens your grasp of contract law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the legal issue
The buyer says 'hold this cloth until I pay the price'. The issue is: is the cloth held as a rahn (pledge) or wadi'ah (deposit)?
The buyer has not used the word 'rahn' explicitly.
2
State the Hanafi position and its core principle
The Hanafi school (Imam Muhammad) holds it is rahn because contracts are based on intended meanings, not literal words. The phrase 'hold until payment' expresses the essence of rahn.
This principle is stated in the text: 'العبرة في العقود للمعانى'.
3
Examine the dalil: analogy with kafalah/hawalah
The Hanafi proof uses a qiyas: if a kafalah (suretyship) includes a condition releasing the original debtor, it becomes hawalah (transfer of debt) due to the intended meaning. Similarly, here the intention to secure payment transforms the holding into rahn.
The analogy shows that labels do not determine legal nature; intention does.
4
Analyze the opposing view and its reasoning
Imam Zufar and Abu Yusuf argue that the word 'imsaak' (hold) is ambiguous between rahn and wadi'ah. Since wadi'ah is the lighter obligation (no liability for loss), it should be presumed by default.
They rely on a principle of assigning the lesser probability when evidence is equal.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi response and the tarjih
The Hanafi response is that specifying a time limit ('until I pay the price') removes the ambiguity and clarifies the intention of rahn. The mufta bihi (relied-upon) position is rahn, as adopted in al-Hidayah.
If the buyer had said 'hold it for your debt' without a time limit, even Zufar agrees it is rahn.

وقال زفر لا يكون رهنا ومثله عن ابى يوسف لان قوله امسک یحتمل الرهن ويحتمل الإيداع والثاني أقلهما فيقضى بثبوته بخلاف ما اذا قال امر بدینک او بمالك لانه لما قابله بالدين فقد عين جهة الرهن
قلنا لمامده الى الاعطاء علم ان مراده الرهن
ترجمہ اور زفر نے فرمایا رہن نہیں ہوگا اور اس کے مثل ابو یوسف سے منقول ہے اس لئے کہ مشتری کا امسک کہنا رہن کا احتمال رکھتا ہے اور ابداع کا احتمال رکھتا ہے اور ثانی (ابداع) ان دونوں میں ہلکا ہے تو اسی کے ثبوت کا فیصلہ کیا جائیگا بخلاف اس صورت کے جبکہ اس نے کہا ہو کہ اس کو اپنے قرض یا اپنے مال کے بدلہ میں رکھ لے اس لئے کہ جب اس نے کپڑے کو دین کے مقابل ٹھہرایا تو رہن کی جہت کو متعین کر دیا ہم کہیں گے کہ جب اس نے امساک ثوب کو اعطاء ثمن تک دراز کیا تو یہ بات معلوم ہوگئی کہ اس کی مراد رہن ہے۔
تشریح امام زفر کا یہ قول ہے کہ اس کو رہن نہیں کہا جائے گا اور امام ابو یوسف سے یہی منقول ہے انہوں نے کہا کہ امسک میں رہن اور ودیعت دونوں کا احتمال ہے اور ان دونوں میں ودیعت ہلکی ہے کیونکہ اس کا ضمان واجب نہیں ہوتا اور اصول یہ ہے کہ ایسے موقع پر جب اقوی یا اکثر کے اثبات کی دلیل نہ ملے تو اس کو اقل اور اخف پر محمول کر لیا جاتا ہے لہذا اس قول کو ودیعت رکھنے پر محمول کیا جائیگا ہم نے ان کے استدلال کا یہ جواب دیا کہ جب مشتری نے امساک ثوب کی مدت اعطاء ثمن بیان کر دی تو رہن کے معنی خود بخود ظاہر ہو گئے اور یہ بات ثابت ہو گئی کہ مشتری کا قصد رہن ہے ودیعت نہیں اگر مشتری نے یہ الفاظ استعمال کیے ہوں کہ امسكه بدینک او مالک تو اس کو امام زفر بھی رہن شمار کرتے ہیں۔ کیونکہ کپڑے اور دین کا تقابل رہن کی دلیل قوی ہے۔
He bought a cloth for dirhams and said to the seller: 'Hold this cloth until I pay you the price.' Then this cloth is a pledge. He said in al-Jami' al-Saghir: Whoever buys a cloth for dirhams and then says to the seller: 'Hold this cloth until I give you the price,' then the cloth is a pledge, because he brought words that indicate the meaning of rahn, which is detention until the time of payment, and consideration in contracts is for meanings, so much so that kafalah with the condition of the original debtor's release is hawalah, and the opposite of that is kafalah. Commentary: Zaid bought a cloth from Khalid, then regarding this cloth or another cloth, Zaid says to Khalid: 'Hold this cloth until I pay you the price.' Then this cloth is a pledge or a trust with Khalid. Imam Zufar called it wadi'ah, but we call it rahn. Our proof is that although Zaid did not use the word rahn, he expressed its meaning because he said to hold it until payment, and that is the reality of rahn. Consideration in contracts is not for words but for meanings. The proof of this is that in kafalah, the original debtor is not released, but in hawalah, the original debtor is released; if the condition of release is present, it becomes hawalah, otherwise kafalah. Hence it is known that contracts are based on meanings, not words. Imam Zufar's view: He said it will not be a rahn, and similar is narrated from Abu Yusuf, because his saying 'hold' is ambiguous between rahn and deposit, and the second (deposit) is the lesser of the two, so its existence is judged, unlike the case when he said 'hold it for your debt' or 'for your property', because when he correlated it with debt, he specified the aspect of rahn. We say: When he extended the holding of the cloth until payment of the price, it became known that his intention was rahn. Commentary: This is Imam Zufar's statement that it will not be called rahn, and similar is narrated from Abu Yusuf. They said that 'hold' can imply rahn and wadi'ah, and wadi'ah is lighter because it does not require liability, and the principle is that when there is no evidence for the stronger or more likely, it is assigned to the lesser and lighter. So this statement is assigned to wadi'ah. We replied to their reasoning: When the buyer specified the duration of holding until payment, the meaning of rahn became evident, and it was established that his intention was rahn, not wadi'ah. If the buyer used the words 'hold it for your debt or for your property', then Imam Zufar also considers it rahn, because the correlation between the cloth and the debt is strong evidence for rahn.
Source pages p. 249

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling with proof from the Hanafi school regarding the validity of a pledge (rahn) based on intended meaning. The scenario: a buyer purchases cloth and tells the seller to hold the cloth until he pays the price. The Hanafi position, stated in al-Jami' al-Saghir by Imam Muhammad, is that this constitutes a valid rahn even without using the word 'rahn'. The proof is that contracts are judged by their meanings, not their literal wording. This is supported by an analogy to kafalah and hawalah: if kafalah includes a condition releasing the original debtor, it is actually hawalah, even if the word 'kafalah' is used. Similarly, the buyer's statement 'hold until I pay' conveys the essential meaning of rahn: detention until payment of a debt. Imam Zufar and Abu Yusuf object, arguing that the word 'hold' is ambiguous between rahn and wadi'ah (deposit), and since wadi'ah is the lighter obligation, it should be presumed. The Hanafi response is that specifying a time limit ('until I pay') removes the ambiguity and indicates the intention of rahn. This lesson highlights the Hanafi principle that the maqasid (objectives) govern contracts, a key difference from other schools that may require explicit terminology.

Key Terms
رہن (rahn): A contract where property is detained as security for a debt, with the right to sell if unpaid.
امسک (imsaak): To hold or detain; in this context, a command to retain possession.
ودیعت (wadi'ah): A deposit for safekeeping without liability for loss unless negligence.
کفالت (kafalah): Suretyship where the surety is liable alongside the original debtor.
حوالہ (hawalah): Transfer of debt where the original debtor is released.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the scenario where a buyer tells the seller to hold the cloth until payment, what is the Hanafi ruling on the cloth?
A) It is a deposit (wadi'ah).
B) It is a pledge (rahn).
C) It is a gift (hibah).
D) It is a sale (bay').

Key Takeaway
A pledge (rahn) can be validly formed by the intended meaning of detention until payment, even without the word 'rahn', based on the Hanafi principle that contracts are judged by their meanings.

Multiple Pledges: Detention of Each Item for Entire Debt
Ruling with proof that each pledged item is detained for the entire debt until full payment.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on multiple pledges and apply the rule that each pledged item is detained for the entire debt until full payment.

Core Idea
Each pledged item is held for the entire debt; partial payment does not release any item.

This lesson examines a key Hanafi principle in the law of pledge (rahn): when multiple items are pledged for a single debt, each item serves as security for the entire debt, not just a proportionate share. The passage from al-Hidayah establishes this rule with a clear analogy to the seller's right to detain the sold item until full payment. Understanding this rule is essential for correctly applying the law of pledges in cases of partial payment.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is pledging two slaves for a single debt of one thousand dirhams. The ruling is that the pledgor cannot take possession of a slave after paying its share until the full debt is paid.
The ruling applies to any multiple items pledged for one debt.
2
Locate the dalil
The author provides a qiyas (analogical deduction) using the analogy of a sold item in the seller's hand (المبيع في يد البائع).
The seller has the right to detain the entire item until full payment.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The analogy is based on the shared illa: both the pledge and the sold item serve as security for the entire payment. Therefore, the pledgee detains each item for every part of the debt.
The strength of the analogy is jaliy (evident).
4
Note the scope of application
The rule applies regardless of the value of each pledged item. The share of each item in the debt is determined by dividing the debt proportionally to their values, but that share does not limit detention.
This is emphasized to prevent misunderstanding that partial payment releases an item.

فـــــصــــل ترجمہ فصل ہے
تشریح اب تک رہن کے وہ مسائل بیان کئے گئے ہیں جن میں مرہون اور راہن اور مرتہن میں تعد نہیں ہے اب وہ مسائل بیان کرنا چاہتے ہیں جہاں مرہون متعدد ہوں یا راہن متعدد ہوں یا مرتہن متعدد ہوں۔
دو غلاموں کو رہن رکھنے کا حکم
ومن رهن عبدين بالف فقضى حصة احدهما لم يكن له ان يقبضه حتى يؤدى باقى الدين وحصة كل واحد منهما ما يخصه اذا قسم الدين على قيمتهما وهذا لأن الرهن محبوس بكل الدين فيكون محبوسا بكل جزء من أجزائه مبالغة في حمله على قضاء الدين وصار كالمبيع في يد البائع
ترجمہ اور جس نے ہزار کے بدلے میں دو غلام رہن رکھے پس ان میں سے ایک کا حصہ ادا کر دیا تو اس کے لئے یہ حق نہ ہوگا کہ اس پر قبضہ کرے یہاں تک کہ باقی قرض ادا کر دے اور ان میں سے ہر ایک کا حصہ وہ ہے جو خصوصاً اس کے حصہ میں آ جائے جبکہ قرض ان دونوں کی قیمت پر تقسیم کر دیا جائے اور یہ اس لئے کہ رہن پورے دین کے عوض محبوس ہے تو دین کے ہر ہر جزء کے عوض محبوس ہوگا راہن کو قضاء دین پر ابھارنے میں مبالغہ کی غرض سے اور یہ ایسا ہو گیا جیسے بائع کے قبضہ میں مبیع ۔
تشریح زید پر خالد کے ہزار روپے ہیں زید نے ہزار روپے کے بدلے اپنے دو غلام خالد کے پاس رہن رکھے ان میں سے ایک کی قیمت سات سو روپے اور دوسرے کی تین سو روپے ہے زید نے سات سو روپے ادا کر دیئے اور تین سو باقی رہے تو کیا زید کو یہ حق ہے کہ اس
Section. Translation: This is a section. Commentary: So far, the issues of rahn have been mentioned where there is no multiplicity of the mortagaged property, the pledgor, or the pledgee. Now issues are to be mentioned where the mortgaged property is multiple, or the pledgor is multiple, or the pledgee is multiple. The ruling on pledging two slaves: And whoever pledges two slaves for a thousand, then he pays off the share of one of them, it is not permissible for him to take possession of it until he pays the remaining debt. And the share of each one of them is what pertains to it when the debt is divided according to their values. And this is because the pledge is detained for the entire debt, so it is detained for every part of it, as an emphasis to compel him to discharge the debt, and it becomes like the sold item in the hand of the seller. Commentary: Zaid owes Khalid one thousand rupees. Zaid pledges his two slaves to Khalid for one thousand rupees. One slave is worth seven hundred rupees, the other three hundred. Zaid pays seven hundred rupees and three hundred remain. Then does Zaid have the right to that... (text cut off)
Source pages p. 250

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling on multiple pledges for a single debt. The matn from al-Hidayah states that if two slaves are pledged for one thousand dirhams, and the pledgor pays off the share of one slave (e.g., pays 500 of 1000), he cannot take possession of that slave until the remaining debt is fully paid. The reasoning is that each slave is detained for the entire debt, not just a proportionate part. The share of each slave in the debt is determined by dividing the debt according to their respective values. For example, if one slave is worth 700 and the other 300, the debt of 1000 is allocated as 700 and 300 respectively. Paying 700 (the share of the first slave) does not release it because the pledge is held for the whole debt until full payment. The analogy is to a sold item in the seller's hand: the seller can detain the entire item until full payment. This ruling emphasizes the principle that multiple items pledged for one debt are each bound for the entire debt, serving as a strong incentive for the debtor to discharge the full obligation. The Urdu commentary illustrates with a numerical example: Zaid owes 1000, pledges two slaves worth 700 and 300, pays 700, but still cannot reclaim the first slave until the remaining 300 is paid.

Key Terms
محبوس (mahbus): Detained or held as security; in this context, the pledged item is physically withheld by the pledgee.
حصة (hissah): Share or portion; here, the portion of the debt allocated to each pledged item based on its value.
قیمت (qimat): Value or price; used to divide the debt among multiple pledged items.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If two slaves are pledged for 1000 dirhams, and the pledgor pays 500 dirhams, can he take possession of one of the slaves?
A) Yes, because he paid half the debt.
B) No, because the entire debt remains; each slave is held for the whole debt.
C) Yes, if the value of that slave is 500 dirhams.
D) No, unless the creditor agrees.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, when multiple items are pledged for a single debt, each item is detained for the entire debt until full payment.

Can a Pawn Be Taken Piecemeal? — The Hanafi Dispute on Specifying Items for Portions of Debt
Explaining two riwayat on specifying items for portions of debt in pawn

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi riwayat on specifying items for portions of debt in a pawn contract and explain the reasoning behind each view.

Core Idea
A pawn contract is either unitary or multiple — the view determines whether the pledgee can take an item piecemeal.

In Hanafi fiqh, when a pledgor pawns multiple items and specifies each for a portion of the total debt, can the pledgee take one item upon paying its specified amount? The classical texts report two different transmissions from Imam Muhammad: one from al-Mabsut and one from al-Ziyadat. This lesson unpacks the legal reasoning behind each view and the practical consequences of the difference.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal issue
The scenario: a pledgor pawns multiple items and specifies each for a portion of the total debt. The question is whether the pledgee can take a specific item upon paying that portion.
The dispute is internal to the Hanafi school.
2
State the two riwayat
Al-Mabsut (al-Asl) holds that it is not allowed; al-Ziyadat holds that it is allowed.
Both riwayat are attributed to Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani.
3
Analyze the proof for each view
Al-Mabsut analogizes to sale: the contract is single and cannot be split. Al-Ziyadat argues that each item is a separate contract, and one contract is not conditional on another.
The proof for al-Mabsut is qiyas to bay' where tafarruq al-safqah is prohibited.
4
Identify the practical difference
Per al-Mabsut, the pledgee must wait until the full debt is paid; per al-Ziyadat, he can take an item piecemeal.
This affects how the pledgee can recover partial payments.
5
Note the scope
The text concludes that splitting is harmful in sale but not in pawn, due to different customs.
In pawn, there is no mixing of good and bad goods as in sale.

فان سمى لكل واحد من أعيان الرهن شيئا من المال الذى رهنه به فكذا الجواب في رواية الاصل وفي الزيادات له ان يقبضه اذا ادى ماسمى له وجه الاول ان العقد متحد لا يتفرق بتفرق التسمية كما في البيع وجه الثانى انه لا حاجة الى الاتحاد لان احد العقدين لا يصير مشروطا فى الاخر ألا ترى انه لو قبل الرهن في أحدهما جاز .. تشريح ايك صورت تو وهى تهى جو ماقبل میں گذرى ليكن اگر راهن نے تعين کر ديا كہ يہ غلام سات سو كے عوض ميں ہے اور يہ تين سو كے تو كيا جب اس نے سات سو ادا كر دئے تو سات سو والا غلام لينے كا حق ہوگا يا نہيں۔ ايسى طرح مثلاً قرض ہزار ہے اور اس نے غلام رہن ركھے اور يہ واضح كر ديا كہ يہ دونوں پانچ سو كے بدلہ ميں ہيں۔ اور بقيہ پانچ سو بغير رہن كے ہيں، پھر اس نے پانچ سوروپے ديدئے اور كہا كہ دونوں غلام ديدو كيونكہ يہ پانچ سودہ ہيں جن كے بدلہ ميں غلام مرہون ہميں تو كيا يہ جائز ہے؟ تو فرمايا كہ اس ميں مبسوط اور زيادات كى روايات مختلف ہيں۔ مبسوط ميں ہے كہ جائز نہيں اور زيادات ميں ہے كہ جائز ہے۔ روايت مبسوط كى دليل يہ ہے كہ يہ عقد متحد ہے ايك ہے تصريح مذكور سے اس كا تو جلد ختم ہو كر اس ميں تعدد اور تفرق پيدا نہ ہوگا لہذا جب يہ ايك ہوا تو وہى حكم سابقى اس كا بھى ہوگا، اور اس كى مثال بعينہ يہ ہے كہ اگر زيد نے دو غلام ہزار كے بدلہ فروخت كئے اور يہ واضح كر ديا كہ اس كى قيمت چھ سوروپے اور دوسرے كى چار سوروپے تو اگر مشترى ايك كى قيمت ديكر اس پر قبضہ كرنا چاہے تو اس كو يہ حق نہ ہوگا تا كہ تفرق صفقہ لازم نہ آجائے۔ روايت زيادات كى دليل يہ ہے كہ حقيقت ميں يہ الگ الگ عقد ہوئے اور اصول يہ ہے كہ ايك عقد دوسرے عقد كے لئے شرط نہيں ہوا كرتا۔ ديكھو ايسى صورت ميں جبكہ يہ واضح كر ديا گيا ہو كہ يہ چھ سو كے بدلہ ميں اور يہ چار سو كے بدلہ ميں ہے اگر مرتہن صرف ايك عقد كو قبول كرے اور دوسرے ميں نہ كرے تو جائز ہے۔ خلاصہ كلام رہن ميں تفرق ہے جو جائز ہے اور مضر نہيں ہے تو ان كو متحد كرنے كى كوئى ضرورت نہيں ، البتہ يہ ضرر صرف بيح كى صورت ميں لازم آتا ہے كيونكہ اس ميں تفرق مضر ہے۔ اور اس كى وجہ يہ ہے كہ بيح ميں جيد اور ردى ملا كر بيچنے كى عادت ہے تو بائع كا ضرر لازم آئيگا۔
Then if he specifies for each one of the pawned items a portion of the money for which he pawned it, then the answer is the same in the riwaya of al-Asl (al-Mabsut), and in al-Ziyadat he has the right to take possession of it when he pays what was specified for him. The first reason is that the contract is single and does not become multiple by the multiplicity of specification, as in sale. The second reason is that there is no need for unity because one of the two contracts is not made conditional upon the other. Do you not see that if he accepted the pawn in one of them, it is permissible. Explanation: One case was that which passed previously. But if the pledgor specified that this slave is for seven hundred and this for three hundred, then when he pays seven hundred, will he have the right to take the seven hundred slave or not? Similarly, for example, the debt is a thousand and he pawned slaves and made it clear that both are for five hundred, and the remaining five hundred are without pawn. Then he paid five hundred rupees and said, 'Give me both slaves because they are for five hundred for which the slaves are pawned to me,' is this permissible? He said that in this the riwayat of al-Mabsut and al-Ziyadat differ. In al-Mabsut it is not permissible, and in al-Ziyadat it is permissible. The proof of the riwaya of al-Mabsut is that this contract is single, it is one by the mentioned specification, so it does not become multiple or split. Therefore, when it is one, the same previous ruling applies. And its exact example is that if Zayd sold two slaves for a thousand and made it clear that this one's price is six hundred and the other's four hundred, then if the buyer pays the price of one and wants to take possession of it, he does not have this right to avoid splitting the transaction. The proof of the riwaya of al-Ziyadat is that in reality these are separate contracts, and the principle is that one contract is not a condition for another. Look at this case: when it is made clear that this is for six hundred and this for four hundred, if the mortgagee accepts only one contract and not the other, it is permissible. Summary: In pawn, splitting is permissible and not harmful, so there is no need to unify them. However, this harm occurs only in the case of sale, because splitting is harmful in it. And the reason is that in sale it is customary to mix good and bad, so the seller's harm would occur.
Source pages p. 251

Commentary
This passage discusses an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning the permissibility of a mortgagee (murtahin) taking possession of a specific pawned item upon paying the portion of debt specified for it. The text presents two transmissions (riwayat): one from al-Mabsut (a foundational work of Zahir al-Riwayah) and one from al-Ziyadat (also by Imam Muhammad). According to al-Mabsut, the contract is unitary and cannot be split; thus the mortgagee cannot take a particular item until the entire debt is paid, analogous to a sale where specifying individual prices does not permit partial delivery. According to al-Ziyadat, each item is a separate contract, so the mortgagee may take an item upon paying its specified amount. The commentator explains the reasoning behind each view, concluding that splitting is permissible in rahn but not in bay' due to the custom of mixing good and bad goods in sales. The text does not explicitly state which view is preferred (mufta bihi), but the structure suggests the Ziyadat view may be more accommodating.

Key Terms
الرهن (al-rahn): A contract by which property is held as security for a debt; the pawn.
تفرق الصفقة (tafarruq al-safqah): Splitting a single transaction into partial deliveries, which is generally prohibited in sales but allowed in rahn according to one view.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the riwaya of al-Mabsut, if a pledgor (rahin) pawns two slaves for a total debt of 1000, specifying that slave A is for 700 and slave B for 300, can the mortgagee (murtahin) take possession of slave A after payment of 700?
A) Yes, because the specification allows it.
B) No, because the contract is single and cannot be split.
C) Only if the other slave is also paid for.
D) It depends on the value of the slaves.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the permissibility of taking a pawned item piecemeal depends on whether the contract is seen as unitary or multiple — a difference reported from Imam Muhammad's own works.
