Pawning One Item to Two Creditors
Ruling on pawning a single item to two creditors for separate debts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on pawning a single indivisible item to two creditors and explain the rationale based on indivisibility of detention.

Core Idea
Pawning a single item to two creditors is valid because detention is indivisible — the whole item secures each debt.

A common question in pawn transactions is whether a single item can secure debts owed to two different creditors. The Hanafi school provides a clear ruling: it is valid, and the entire item is considered pawned to each creditor. This lesson unpacks the reasoning from al-Quduri, focusing on the concept of indivisibility of detention and contrasting it with the ruling on gifts to multiple recipients.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is pawning one indivisible item (e.g., a watch) to two creditors for their separate debts. The ruling is jā'iz (valid/sahih).
2
Locate the dalil (proof)
The proof is rational (qiyas): the pawn is attached to the entire item in one transaction; detention (حبس) is indivisible, so the whole item secures both debts.
The Arabic phrase: 'لان الرهن اضيف الى جميع العين في صفقة واحدة ولا شيوع فيه وموجبه صيرورته محتبنا بالدين وهذا مما لا يقبل الوصف بالتجزى'
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The effective cause (illa) is that the essence of pawn is detention, and detention of a single item cannot be divided. Therefore, the entire item is detained for each debt.
Contrast with gift (hibah) which requires specification of shares and is thus invalid if given to two persons without division.
4
Address the objection about shuyū'
An objector might claim multiple creditors create an undivided share (shuyū'), invalidating the pawn. The response: multiplicity of claimants in one subject does not create shuyū'.
Example: qisas (retaliation) due to a group does not divide the right into shares.
5
Note the contrast with hibah
Abu Hanifa holds that a gift to two persons is invalid because it requires specification of shares, which is impossible in an indivisible item. Pawn is different because its purpose is detention, not ownership transfer.
This distinction highlights that the ruling for pawn is not based on ownership division but on securing the debt.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ايک شے كو دو آدميوں كے قرضوں كے بدلے رہن ركھا تو كيا حكم ہے۔ قال فان رهن عينا واحدة عند رجلين بدين لكل واحد منهما عليه جاز وجميعها رهن عند كل واحد منهما لان الرهن اضيف الى جميع العين في صفقة واحدة ولا شيوع فيه وموجبه صيرورته محتبنا بالدين وهذا مما لا يقبل الوصف بالتجزى فصار محبوسا بكل واحد منهما وهذا بخلاف الهبة من رجلين حيث لا تجوز عند ابي حنيفة۔ ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمايا پس اگر كسى ايك چيز كو دو آدميوں كے پاس رہن ركھا اس قرض كے بدلہ ميں جو ان دونوں كا اس پر ہے تو جائز ہے اور پورى چيز ان دونوں ميں سے ہر ايك كے پاس رہن ہوگى اس لئے كہ ايك ہى معاملہ ميں پورى چيز كى طرف رہن كى اضافت كى گئى ہے اس ميں شيوع نہيں ہے اور رہن كا حكم مرہون كا قرض كے بدلہ ميں محبوس ہوتا ہے اور يہ ان چيزوں ميں سے ہے جو تجزى كے وصف كو قبول نہيں كرتا تو مرہون ان دونوں ميں سے ہر ايك كے بدلہ محبوس ہوگا اور يہ دو شخصوں كو ہبہ كرنے كے خلاف ہے جو ابوحنيفہ كے نزديك جائز نہيں ہے۔ تشريح زيد پر خالد اور بكر كے ورد پے قرض ميں زيد نے اپنى گھڑى سوروپے كے عوض ان دونوں كے پاس رہن ركھدى تو مير بہن جائز ہے اور يون سمجھا جائيگا كہ پورى گھڑى ہر ايك كے پاس مرہون محبوس ہے۔ سوال يہ تو جائز نہ ہونا چاہيے كيونكہ مستحقين ميں تعدد ہے جس كى وجہ سے رہن ميں شيوع پيدا ہو گيا جو جواز رہن سے مانع ہے؟ جواب محل واخد ميں مستحقين كا تعدد شيوع كو ثابت نہيں كرتا جيسے ايك جماعت كيلئے زيد پر قصاص واجب ہو تو يہ مستحقين كا تعد محل كے شيوع كو لازم نہيں كريگا۔ سوال ... جناب شيوع تو ہے اس لئے كہ رہن كى دو شخصوں كى جانب اضافت ان دونوں كے درميان نصفا نصف انقسام كو ثابت كريگى
He said: If he pawns one item with two persons for a debt due from him to each of them, it is valid, and the entire item is a pawn with each one of them, because the pawn is attached to the entire item in one transaction and there is no undivided share in it, and its necessary consequence is its detention for the debt, and this is something that does not accept description of divisibility, so it becomes detained for each one of them. And this is contrary to giving a gift from two persons, which is not valid according to Abu Hanifa. Translation: Al-Quduri said: So if he pawns one item with two persons for the debt that each of them has on him, it is valid, and the entire item is a pawn with each of them, because the pawn is attached to the entire item in one transaction and there is no shuyu' (undivided share) in it, and the ruling of pawn is that the pawned item is detained for the debt, and this is one of those things that do not accept the description of divisibility, so the pawned item is detained for each of them. And this is contrary to giving a gift to two persons, which according to Abu Hanifa is not valid. Explanation: Zayd owes Khalid and Bakr a debt; Zayd pawns his watch for a hundred rupees with both of them. This transaction is valid, and it will be understood that the entire watch is pawned with each of them. Question: This should not be valid because there are multiple claimants, which creates shuyu' in the pawn, preventing its validity? Answer: Multiplicity of claimants in a single subject does not establish shuyu', just as if qisas is due from Zayd to a group, this multiplicity does not necessitate shuyu' in the subject. Question: But shuyu' exists because the attribution of the pawn to two persons would establish a half-half division between them?
Source pages p. 252

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from al-Quduri on pawning a single, indivisible item to two creditors for their separate debts. The ruling is that it is valid, and the entire item is considered pawned to each creditor. The rationale is that the pawn contract attaches the entire item to the debt in a single transaction, and since pawn involves detention which is indivisible, the whole item secures both debts. The text contrasts this with a gift (hibah) to two persons, which Abu Hanifa considers invalid because a gift requires specification of shares. The commentary then answers a potential objection: multiple creditors do not create an undivided share (shuyu') in the pawned item, just as multiple claimants for qisas (retaliation) do not create shuyu' in the person. The questioner persists that attribution of the pawn to two persons implies a half-half division, but the text implies that the pawn is entire for each, not split.

Key Terms
شيوع (shuyū'): Undivided share or common ownership; in this context, the argument is that multiple creditors do not create shuyu' in the collateral because the whole item secures each debt.
تجزى (tajazzī): Divisibility; the pawned item is considered indivisible for the purpose of detention, so it remains with each creditor as a whole.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, is it valid to pawn a single, indivisible item (e.g., a watch) to two creditors for their separate debts?
A) Invalid, because the item cannot be shared between two creditors.
B) Valid, because the whole item is pawned to each creditor.
C) Valid only if the creditors agree to share the item.
D) Invalid, because it resembles a gift to two people which is invalid.

Key Takeaway
Pawning a single item to multiple creditors is valid because detention is indivisible by nature, so the whole item secures each debt without creating shares.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute: Unity of Pledge Contract for Multiple Debts
Intra-Hanafi dispute on unity of pledge contract

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between Riwayat Mabsut and Riwayat Ziyadat regarding the unity of a pledge contract for multiple debts and state the practical consequence of each view.

Core Idea
A pledge for multiple debts can be one contract or multiple contracts – separation is permissible in pledge unlike sale.

In this passage, we encounter a classical intra-Hanafi dispute between two narrations from Imam Muhammad’s works: al-Mabsut and al-Ziyadat. The question is whether a single pledge covering multiple debts constitutes one unified contract or several independent contracts. The answer determines whether the creditor may selectively take possession of part of the pledged asset. We will trace the reasoning of each narration and see how the commentary resolves the conflict.

Guided Path
1
State the dispute
Identify the exact legal issue: when a debtor pledges one asset for multiple debts, is the pledge contract one unit or multiple contracts?
The disagreement is between two Hanafi riwayat, not with another madhhab.
2
Examine the Mabsut position
Analyze the proof of Riwayat Mabsut: it argues for a single unified contract by analogy to a sale of multiple items with a lump sum price, where partial purchase is not allowed lest it cause tafarruq al-safqah.
The analogy is based on the idea that splitting a single contract harms the parties.
3
Examine the Ziyadat position
Analyze the proof of Riwayat Ziyadat: it argues that each debt creates a separate contract, since one contract is not a condition for another, and the pledgee may accept one and reject the other.
This view emphasizes the independence of each debt and contract.
4
Determine the tarjih and thamarah al-khilaf
Note that the commentary sides with Riwayat Ziyadat because separation in pledge is not harmful, unlike in sale where mixing good and bad items is customary. The practical difference: under Mabsut, creditor cannot take partial possession; under Ziyadat, he may.
The commentary distinguishes sale from pledge based on the custom (urf) of mixing goods in sale.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
روایت مبسوط کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ یہ عقد متحد ہے ایک ہے تصریح مذکور سے اس کا تو جلد ختم ہو کر اس میں تعدد اور تفرق پیدا نہ ہوگا لہذا جب یہ ایک ہوا تو وہی حکم سابقی اس کا بھی ہوگا، اور اس کی مثال بعینہ یہ ہے کہ اگر زید نے دو غلام ہزار کے بدلہ فروخت کئے اور یہ واضح کر دیا کہ اس کی قیمت چھ سوروپے اور دوسرے کی چار سوروپے تو اگر مشتری ایک کی قیمت دیکر اس پر قبضہ کرنا چاہے تو اس کو یہ حق نہ ہوگا تا کہ تفرق صفقہ ا لازم نہ آجائے۔
روایت زیادان کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ حقیقت میں یہ الگ الگ عقد ہوئے اور اصول یہ ہے کہ ایک عقد دوسرے عقد کے لئے شرط نہیں ہوا کرتا۔ دیکھو اسی صورت میں جبکہ یہ واضح کر دیا گیا ہو کہ یہ چھ سو کے بدلہ میں اور یہ چار سو کے بدلہ میں ہے اگر مرتہن صرف ایک عقد کو قبول کرے اور دوسرے میں نہ کرے تو جائز ہے۔ خلاصہ کلام رہن میں تفرق ہے جو جائز ہے اور مضر نہیں ہے تو ان کو متحد کرنے کی کوئی ضرورت نہیں ، البتہ یہ ضرر صرف بیع کی صورت میں لازم آتا ہے کیونکہ اس میں تفرق مضر ہے۔ اور اس کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ بیع میں جید اور ردی ملا کر بیچنے کی عادت ہے تو بائع کا ضرر لازم آئیگا۔
The proof of the Mabsut narration is that this contract is a single unit, one. Because of the explicit mention, it will conclude quickly and there will be no multiplicity or separation in it. Therefore, when it is one, the same previous ruling will apply to it. And an exact example of this is that if Zaid sold two slaves for one thousand, and he clarified that the price of this one is six hundred and the other four hundred, then if the buyer wishes to take possession of one by paying its price, he will not have this right, lest splitting of the contract (tafarruq al-safqah) become necessary.
The proof of the Ziyadat narration is that in reality these are separate contracts, and the principle is that one contract does not become a condition for another contract. Look at the same scenario: when it is clarified that this one is in exchange for six hundred and that one for four hundred, if the pledgee accepts only one contract and not the other, it is permissible. In summary, separation (tafarruq) in pledge is permissible and not harmful, so there is no need to unite them. However, this harm only occurs in the case of sale because separation is harmful there. And the reason is that in sale, it is customary to mix good and bad together, so the seller's harm would be necessary.
Source pages p. 252

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute between two narrations (Riwayat Mabsut and Riwayat Ziyadat) regarding the nature of a pledge contract when a single item is pledged for multiple debts owed to the same creditor. The Riwayat Mabsut (from Imam Muhammad's al-Mabsut) holds that the contract is one unified transaction; thus, the creditor cannot selectively enforce part of it, exemplified by the analogy of selling two slaves for a lump sum where the buyer cannot take one slave by paying a portion. The Riwayat Ziyadat (from al-Ziyadat) argues that each debt creates a separate pledge contract, as it says: in reality they are separate contracts, and one contract does not condition another; the pledgee may accept one and reject the other. The commentary then resolves that in pledge, separation is permissible and not harmful, unlike in sale where mixing good and bad items is customary and allowing separation would harm the seller.

Key Terms
تفرق صفقہ (tafarruq al-safqah): Splitting or partial enforcement of a single contract
عقد متحد (aql muttahid): A single unified contract, not separable into parts

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Riwayat Ziyadat, why is it permissible for a pledgee to accept only one of multiple pledge contracts for separate debts?
A) Because one contract can be a condition for another.
B) Because the contract is one unit, so partial enforcement is invalid.
C) Because each contract is separate and one does not depend on the other.
D) Because pledge, like sale, does not allow separation.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, a single pledge for multiple debts may be considered one contract (Riwayat Mabsut) or multiple contracts (Riwayat Ziyadat), with the latter being the preferred view in the commentary because separation in pledge is not harmful.

Pledging One Item to Two Creditors: Validity and the Non-Divisibility of Detention
Ruling on validity and effect of pledging a single item to two creditors

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on pledging a single item to two creditors and explain the legal reasoning (ta'lil) based on the indivisibility of detention (habs).

Core Idea
A single pledge to two creditors is valid because detention is indivisible – the entire item secures each debt.

This lesson examines a specific ruling from Al-Quduri's matn: a debtor may pledge a single item to two different creditors for separate debts, and the entire item is considered a pledge for each. At first glance, this might seem problematic due to potential conflict of interests. However, the Hanafi school clarifies that the nature of a pledge (rahn) is detention (habs), which does not admit division. We will walk through the ruling, its proof via analogy to qisas, and the distinction from hibah (gift).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the debtor doing? Pledging one item to two different creditors for their respective debts. The ruling in the Hanafi school is that it is valid (ja'iz) and the entire item is a pledge for each creditor.
The text states: 'وجميعها رهن عند كل واحد منهما' — the entire item is a pledge with each one.
2
Understand the rationale (ta'lil)
The pledge is made in a single transaction (safqah wahidah), so there is no shuyu' (common ownership) at the time of contract. The effect of a pledge is detention (habs), which is indivisible – you cannot detain half an item for one debt and the other half for another. Thus, the entire item is considered detained for each debt.
The author compares it to qisas: multiple heirs have a right to retaliation against one killer, but the right is not divided – each has a claim to the whole.
3
Analyze the counterarguments
An objector might say that multiplicity of creditors creates shuyu', invalidating the pledge. The reply: multiplicity of claimants in one subject does not create shuyu'; it only means the item is affected by multiple rights, but detention is one act. Another objection: at destruction, the item's value is divided proportionally, which proves shuyu'. The reply: division at destruction is for practical distribution, but during the pledge, the detention is considered whole for each right.
This shows the distinction between the legal effect (habs) and the eventual outcome (distribution upon destruction).
4
Contrast with hibah
Gifting a single item to two persons is invalid according to Abu Hanifa because the purpose of a gift is ownership (tamlik), and ownership cannot be shared in a single undivided item without shuyu'. Pledge, however, is detention, not ownership, so the same restriction does not apply.
This contrast highlights that the nature of the contract (ownership vs. security) determines whether shuyu' is problematic.
5
Apply the ruling in practice
If the pledged item is destroyed, its value is divided among the creditors proportionally to their debts. But during the pledge period, each creditor has the right to detain the entire item (though physically it can only be with one). The debtor cannot reclaim the item until all debts are paid.
The text only mentions the division at destruction, not the practical detention; but the principle is clear.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال فان رهن عينا وإحدة عند رجلين بدين لكل واحد منهما عليه جاز وجميعها رهن عند كل واحد منهما لان الرهن اضيف الى جميع العين في صفقة واحدة ولا شيوع فيه وموجبه صيرورته محتبنا بالدين وهذا مما لا يقبل الوصف بالتجزى فصار محبوسا بكل واحد منهما وهذا بخلاف الهمة من رجلين حيث لا تجوز عند ابي حنيفة
ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا پس اگر کسی ایک چیز کو دو منصوں کے پاس رہن رکھا اس قرض کے بدلہ میں جو ان دونوں کا اس پر ہے تو جائز ہے اور پوری چیز ان دونوں میں سے ہر ایک کے پاس رہن ہوگی اس لئے کہ ایک ہی معاملہ میں پوری چیز کی طرف رہن کی اضافت کی گئی ہے اس میں شیوع نہیں ہے اور رہن کا حکم مرہون کا قرض کے بدلہ میں محبوس ہوتا ہے اور یہ ان چیزوں میں سے ہے جو تجزی کے وصف کو قبول نہیں کرتا تو مرہون ان دونوں میں سے ہر ایک کے بدلہ محبوس ہوگا اور یہ دو شخصوں کو ہبہ کرنے کے خلاف ہے جو ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک جائز نہیں ہے۔ تشریح زید پر خالد اور بکر کے ورد پے قرض میں زید نے اپنی گھڑی سوروپے کے عوض ان دونوں کے پاس رہن رکھدی تو میر بہن جائز ہے اور یوں سمجھا جائیگا کہ پوری گھڑی ہر ایک کے پاس مرہون محبوس ہے۔
سوال یہ تو جائز نہ ہونا چاہیے کیونکہ مستحقین میں تعدد ہے جس کی وجہ سے رہن میں شیوع پیدا ہو گیا جو جواز رہن سے مانع ہے؟ جواب محل واخد میں مستحقین کا تعدد شیوع کو ثابت نہیں کرتا جیسے ایک جماعت کیلئے زید پر قصاص واجب ہو تو یہ مستحقین کا تعد محل کے شیوع کو لازم نہیں کریگا۔ سوال ... جناب شیوع تو ہے اس لئے کہ رہن کی دو شخصوں کی جانب اضافت ان دونوں کے درمیان نصفا نصف انقسام کو ثابت کریگی جیسے ہلاکت کی صورت میں انقسام مذکور مسلم ہے؟
جواب جواز کو تلاش کرنے کے لئے انقسام نہ ہوگا بلکہ مرہون کو ان دونوں کے حق میں محبوس قرار دیا جائیگا یعنی گویا بغیر انقسام کے مرہون ہر ایک کے پاس پورا ہے کیونکہ گھڑی میں یہ صورت تو ہو نہیں سکتی کہ دونوں کے پاس محبوس ہو لہذا یوں شمار کر لیا جائے گا کہ ان میں دونوں میں سے ہر ایک کے حق کے بدلہ میں محبوس ہے۔ اور ہبہ کا مقصد چونکہ تملیک ہے لہذا اگر ایک چیز دو شخصوں کو پوری ہبہ کی تو دونوں کو اس کا مالک بنانا محال ہے اس وجہ سے امام ابو حنیفہ نے اس کو جائز قرار نہیں دیا۔
He said: If he pledges a single item to two men for a debt owed to each of them, it is valid, and the entire item is a pledge with each of them. This is because the pledge is added to the entire item in a single transaction, and there is no common ownership (shuyu') in it. And its effect is that it becomes detained for the debt, and this is something that does not accept the attribute of division, so it becomes detained for each of them. This is contrary to gifting (hibah) to two men, which is not permissible according to Abu Hanifa.
Translation: Al-Quduri said: So if a person pledges a single item to two persons for the debt that both have against him, it is valid, and the entire item will be a pledge with each of them, because in one transaction the pledge is added to the entire item; there is no shuyu' in it. And the ruling of pledge is that the pledged item is detained for the debt, and this is from those things that do not accept the attribute of division, so the pledge will be detained for each of them. And this is contrary to giving a gift to two persons, which according to Abu Hanifa is not permissible. Explanation: Zaid owes Khalid and Bakr a debt. Zaid pledges his watch worth one hundred to both of them as a pledge. The transaction is valid, and it will be understood that the entire watch is detained as a pledge with each of them.
Question: This should not be valid because there is multiplicity of claimants, which creates shuyu' in the pledge, which prevents the validity of pledge? Answer: Multiplicity of claimants in one subject does not prove shuyu', just as when qisas is obligatory upon Zaid for a group, this multiplicity of claimants does not necessitate shuyu' in the subject. Question: ... there is shuyu' because addition of the pledge to two persons proves division between them half and half, just as in case of destruction this division is conceded? Answer: For the purpose of validity, division will not be assumed; rather the pledge will be considered detained for the right of both, meaning without division the pledge is entirely with each, because it is not possible for the watch to be physically detained by both, so it is considered that it is detained in exchange for each of their rights. And because the purpose of gift is ownership, if one item is given as a gift to two persons, making both owners is impossible; therefore Imam Abu Hanifa did not permit it.
Source pages p. 252

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from Al-Quduri's matn on pledging one item to two creditors. The ruling: it is valid, and the entire item is deemed to be a pledge with each creditor. The proof: the item is pledged in a single transaction, so there is no shuyu' (common ownership) — shuyu' would require division, but the pledge's effect (detention) is indivisible. An objection is raised: multiplicity of creditors should create shuyu' and invalidate the pledge. The answer: multiplicity of claimants in one subject does not create shuyu'; an analogy is qisas (retaliation) owed to multiple heirs — the claim of each is not divided. Another objection: at destruction, the item is divided proportionally, proving shuyu'. The answer: for validity, division is not considered; instead, the entire item is detained for each right, and only at destruction is it proportionally apportioned. The passage contrasts with hibah (gift) to two persons, which is invalid because ownership cannot be shared in a single gift.

Key Terms
شیوع (shuyu'): Common ownership or shared possession of an undivided part of an item.
محبوس (mahbus): Detained or held as a pledge; the pledged item is retained as security for the debt.
حَبس (habs): Detention; the legal effect of a pledge where the item is held as security.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The watch is divided equally between the two creditors.
B) The watch is void as a pledge due to shuyu'.
C) The entire watch is considered a pledge for each creditor.
D) The watch is treated as a gift to both creditors.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school validates pledging one item to multiple creditors because detention (habs) is indivisible, so the entire item secures each debt, unlike ownership-based contracts.

Muhāyā (Time-Sharing) of Pledged Items Among Multiple Creditors
Ruling on muhāyā (time-sharing) between creditors of a single pledged item

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on muhāyā (time-sharing) of a pledged item among multiple pledgees and explain the legal fiction of adl that preserves continuous possession.

Core Idea
Muhāyā (time-sharing) does not break possession; each pledgee acts as adl for the other.

The pledge (rahn) requires continuous possession (qabḍ) by the pledgee or his agent. When there are multiple pledgees, they may agree to share possession by turns. Does this interruption in physical possession invalidate the pledge? The Hanafi ruling is clear: the pledge remains valid because each pledgee, while holding, is considered an agent (adl) for the other, maintaining constructive possession for all.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is muhāyā (time-sharing agreement). The ruling is that it is permissible (sahih) and does not invalidate the pledge.
The matn states 'fain tahāyā' indicating permissibility.
2
Understand the key term 'adl'
An adl is a trustworthy agent who holds the pledged item on behalf of the pledgee. Possession by an adl is legally considered possession by the pledgee.
This preserves the continuous possession requirement.
3
Apply the analogy to muhāyā
When pledgees take turns, the one in possession is treated as an adl for the non-possessing pledgee. Therefore, the non-possessing pledgee's possession is not interrupted in the eyes of the law.
The matn says: 'كل واحد منهما في نوبته كالعدل في حق الآخر'.
4
Note the consequence
The pledge remains valid for all pledgees throughout the arrangement. No one loses their rights.
This is the muftā bihī position.
5
Memorize the key phrase
Memorise the wording: 'كل واحد منهما في نوبته كالعدل في حق الآخر' (each one of them in his turn is like an adl for the other).
This is a ruling statement often quoted in zabt (memorization) of Hanafi fiqh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فان تهـــایــــــا فـــكـــل واحـــد مـنهــمــا فــي نــوبـــــه کـــالــعــدل في حق الأخــر ترجمہ پس اگر ان دونوں نے ( دونوں قرض خواہوں نے ) مہایات کرلی تو ان دونوں میں سے ہر ایک اپنی باری میں دوسرے کے حق میں عادل کے مثل ہے۔ تشریح اگر ان دونوں نے یہ طے کر لیا ہو مر ہوں گھڑی آٹھ دن اس کے پاس اور آٹھ دن دوسرے کے پاس رہے گی تو دوسرے کا قبضہ ختم ہو گیا ؟ فرمایا کہ جس طرح مرہون عادل کے پاس رہتا ہے اس کے باوجود اس کو مرتمن کے پاس شمار کیا جاتا ہے اسی طرح یہاں بھی ہر ایک کو دوسرے کے حق میں عادل کے مثل سمجھیں گے اور کسی کا بھی قبضہ ختم نہ ہوگا۔
Then if they make a division (muhāyā), then each one of them, during his turn, is like an agent (adl) with respect to the right of the other. Translation: So if the two (creditors) make muhāyā, then each of them in his turn is like an adl for the other's right. Explanation: If they agree that the watch will be with one for eight days and with the other for eight days, then does the possession of the other end? It is said: Just as the pledged item remains with the adl yet it is considered as in the possession of the mortgagee, similarly here, each will be considered like an adl for the other, and the possession of neither will end.
Source pages p. 253

Commentary
This is a ruling statement from the matn (likely Quduri) regarding muhāyā (division of time) among multiple pledgees. The ruling: if the creditors agree on a time-sharing arrangement, each during his turn holds the pledged item as an agent (adl) for the other creditor. This means the item is considered in the possession of both continually; the turn-taking does not break the continuous detention required for a valid pledge. The commentary clarifies with an example: if the watch is kept by one for eight days and then the other for eight days, the other's possession does not end; rather, the watcher is considered an adl for the absent creditor.

Key Terms
مہایات (muhāyā): An agreement among co-owners or creditors to divide the use of a property by time or space
عادل (adl): A trustworthy agent or custodian who holds the pledged item on behalf of the pledgee

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The non-possessing creditor loses his right of pledge.
B) Each is considered an adl for the other during his turn.
C) The pledge becomes void due to interruption.
D) The item is considered jointly owned.

Key Takeaway
Muhāyā (time-sharing) between pledgees is valid in the Hanafi school; each pledgee in his turn is considered an adl (agent) for the other, maintaining continuous possession.

Proportional Liability Upon Destruction of a Pledged Item with Multiple Creditors
Ruling on proportional liability upon destruction of pledge

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling that upon destruction of a pledged item held by multiple creditors, each creditor's liability is proportional to his share of the debt, and calculate the loss distribution in given scenarios.

Core Idea
Destruction of a pledge held by multiple creditors is treated as proportional satisfaction of debts because receipt can be divided.

In the Hanafi school, when a pledged item (rahn) is held by multiple creditors and it is destroyed, the loss is not borne equally by default. Instead, each creditor is considered to have received his share of the debt proportionally, based on the principle that receipt (istifa') is divisible. This ruling from Al-Quduri's matn is explained with two key examples: one with equal debts and one with unequal debts and partial destruction. Understanding this rule is essential for correctly resolving disputes when collateral is lost.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling
The passage begins with the ruling: upon destruction, each creditor's liability is his share of the debt (حصته من الدين). This is not a penalty but a proportional satisfaction.
The ruling applies only if the pledge is destroyed (هلاك).
2
Understand the legal proof (ta'lil)
The proof is that receipt (استيفاء) is divisible (مما يتجزى). Therefore, the destruction is treated as if each creditor received his share of the debt in proportion to his claim.
This is a qiyas: the original rule that destruction extinguishes the debt proportionally is analogized to the divisibility of receipt.
3
Apply to the first example (equal debts)
Both creditors have 25 rupees each (total 50). The pledge is destroyed. Since receipt is divisible, each is deemed to have received 25, so both debts are fully extinguished.
No compensation from the debtor is needed.
4
Apply to the second example (unequal debts, partial destruction)
Debts: Khalid 10, Bakr 5 (total 15). Pledge value 30, of which 20 destroyed, 10 remain. The remaining 10 is divided proportionally: 2/3 (6.67) to Khalid, 1/3 (3.33) to Bakr. The shortfall is compensated by the debtor Zaid: he pays Khalid 3.33 (1/3 of 10) and Bakr 1.67 (1/3 of 5).
The compensation makes up the difference between the proportional share of the destroyed portion and the actual debt.
5
Generalise the rule
Whenever a pledged item held by multiple creditors is destroyed, divide the loss (or remaining value) in proportion to each creditor's debt. The debtor must compensate any shortfall if the destroyed value is less than the total debt.
This rule is specific to Hanafi fiqh; other schools may differ.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال والمضمون على كل واحد منهما حصته من الدين لان عند الهلاك يصير كل واحد منهما مستوفيا حصته اذ الاستيفاء مما يتجزى
ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور ان دونوں میں سے ہر ایک کے اوپر قرض میں سے اس کا حصہ مضمون ہوگا اس لئے کہ ہلاکت کے وقت ان دونوں میں سے ہر ایک اپنے حصہ کو وصول کرنے والا ہو جائیگا اس لئے کہ وصولیابی ان چیزوں میں سے ہے جس کی تقسیم ہو جاتی ہے۔ تشریح یعنی ہلاکت کے بغیر تو انقسام نہیں مانا گیا بلکہ یوں سمجھا گیا گویا ہر ایک کے قبضہ میں پورا مرہون ہے لیکن اگر مرہون ہلاک ہو جائے تو اب وہ اپنے دین کے مطابق ضامن قرار دیئے جائیں گے کیونکہ وصولیابی میں تجری ہو سکتی ہے۔
مثلاً دونوں کے زید پر پچاس روپے تھے ایک کے پچھپیں اور دوسرے کے چھپیں اور مرہون ہلاک ہو گیا تو دونوں کا قرض ساقط ہو گیا۔ دوسری مثال زید کے ذمہ پندرہ روپے ہیں ۱۰ خالد کے اور ۵ بکر کے زید نے ان دونوں کے پاس ۳۰ روپے رہن رکھے جن میں سے ۲۰ ہلاک ہو گئے اور باقی رہ گئے تو اب کیا حکم ہے؟
حکم یہ ہے کہ موجودہ دس کو خالد اور بکر تین حصوں میں تقسیم کر لیں پھر اس کا ۲/۳ خالد کا اور ۱/۳ بکر کا ہوگا اور زید ان دونوں کے قرض کی کمی کو اپنے پاس سے اس طرح پوری کریگا کہ وہ خالد کو اپنے پاس سے دس کا ثلث دیگا یعنی ۳ اور بکر کو پانچ کا تہائی دیگا یعنی است
He said: And the liability upon each one of them is his share of the debt, because at the time of destruction, each one of them becomes a recipient of his share, since receipt (istifa') is something that can be divided. Translation: Al-Quduri said: And upon each of them, his share of the debt is guaranteed, because at the time of destruction each of them becomes a recipient of his share, since receipt is something that can be divided. Explanation: That is, without destruction, division is not assumed; rather it is understood that the entire pledge is in the possession of each. But if the pledge is destroyed, then they become liable according to their debts, because receipt can be divided. For example, both had fifty rupees against Zaid: one had twenty-five and the other had twenty-five, and the pledge was destroyed; then both debts are extinguished. Second example: Zaid owes fifteen rupees: ten to Khalid and five to Bakr. Zaid pledged thirty rupees with them, of which twenty were destroyed and ten remain. The ruling: the remaining ten are divided between Khalid and Bakr in three parts: two-thirds (about 6.67) for Khalid and one-third (3.33) for Bakr, and Zaid will compensate the shortfall from his own wealth: he will give Khalid one-third of ten (3.33) and Bakr one-third of five (1.67).
Source pages p. 253

Commentary
This passage contains a ruling with proof from Al-Quduri's matn regarding liability when a pledged item held by multiple creditors is destroyed. The ruling: each creditor's liability is his share of the debt; upon destruction, each is considered to have received his share of the debt proportionally. The proof: receipt (istifa') can be divided, so the destruction is deemed proportionate satisfaction. The commentary provides two examples. First: both creditors have equal debts (25 each), total debt 50, pledge destroyed; both debts are extinguished. Second: debts are unequal (10 and 5), pledge value 30, 20 destroyed leaving 10. The remaining 10 is divided proportionally: 2/3 to Khalid (since his debt is 2/3 of total 15) and 1/3 to Bakr. But since the debts are 10 and 5, after receiving 6.67 and 3.33, Khalid's remaining 3.33 is compensated by Zaid paying him 1/3 of 10, and Bakr's remaining 1.67 by Zaid paying him 1/3 of 5. The example shows how the liability is apportioned.

Key Terms
استیفاء (istifa'): Receipt or collection of a debt or right. In this context, it refers to the creditors' act of receiving satisfaction of their debts from the pledged item.
مضمون (madmun): What is guaranteed or held as liability. Here, the pledged item becomes liable for the debt; upon destruction, each creditor bears the loss of his share.
تجزى (yatajazzā): It is divisible; capable of being divided.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A pledged item worth 120 is held by two creditors. Creditor A is owed 80, Creditor B is owed 40. The item is completely destroyed. What is the total loss borne by each creditor according to the Hanafi ruling?
A) A loses 80, B loses 40
B) A loses 60, B loses 60
C) A loses 80, B loses 40? Actually that is their debt, but loss is of the item. The item is worth 120, but debts sum to 120, so the loss extinguishes both debts. So A receives 80 satisfaction, B receives 40. So the loss is divided proportionally to debts.
D) The loss is ignored and debts remain.

Key Takeaway
When a pledged item held by multiple creditors is destroyed, liability is apportioned proportionally to each creditor's debt, because receipt (istifa') is divisible.

Undivided Possession in Pledge: The Principle
Principle of undivided possession in pledge

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why a single item pledged to two creditors is considered held fully for each, and distinguish this from the invalid gift of one item to two persons.

Core Idea
Possession of a pledge is undivided; each creditor holds the entire item, unlike gift which requires transfer of ownership.

When a single item is pledged to two creditors, the Hanafi school treats the item as held (mahbus) for the right of each creditor without physical division. This lesson explores the reasoning behind this principle and its contrast with the gift contract.

Guided Path
1
Identify the problem
A single physical item cannot be simultaneously possessed by two creditors. This creates a legal dilemma.
The problem arises because possession of a pledge is essential for the contract to be binding.
2
Understand the Hanafi solution
The item is considered legally held for the right of both creditors. This is a legal construction (hukman) that does not require actual division.
The Arabic term is 'mahbus' – held or impounded.
3
Compare with gift (hiba)
In gift, the purpose is transfer of ownership (tamlik). Making two persons owners of one item is impossible, so the gift is invalid.
Imam Abu Hanifa explicitly disapproves of gifting one item to two persons.
4
Apply the principle
The pledge remains valid without division. Each creditor has full security for his debt, and the pledgor cannot claim the item until all debts are paid.
This establishes the foundation for subsequent rulings on time-sharing and destruction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
جواب جواز کو تلاش کرنے کے لئے انقسام نہ ہوگا بلکہ مرہون کو ان دونوں کے حق میں محبوس قرار دیا جائیگا یعنی گویا بغیر انقسام کے مرہون ہر ایک کے پاس پورا ہے کیونکہ گھڑی میں یہ صورت تو ہو نہیں سکتی کہ دونوں کے پاس محبوس ہو لہذا یوں شمار کر لیا جائے گا کہ ان میں دونوں میں سے ہر ایک کے حق کے بدلہ میں محبوس ہے۔ اور ہبہ کا مقصد چونکہ تملیک ہے لہذا اگر ایک چیز دو شخصوں کو پوری ہبہ کی تو دونوں کو اس کا مالک بنانا محال ہے اس وجہ سے امام ابو حنیفہ نے اس کو جائز قرار نہیں دیا۔ اگر رہن میں دونوں مرتین باری مقرر کر لیں تو کیا حکم ہے فان تهـــایــــــا فـــكـــل واحـــد مـنهـــمــا فــي نــوبـــــه کـــالــعــدل في حق الأخــر ترجمہ پس اگر ان دونوں نے ( دونوں قرض خواہوں نے ) مہایات کرلی تو ان دونوں میں سے ہر ایک اپنی باری میں دوسرے کے حق میں عادل کے مثل ہے۔ تشریح اگر ان دونوں نے یہ طے کر لیا ہو کہ مرہون گھڑی آٹھ دن اس کے پاس اور آٹھ دن دوسرے کے پاس رہے گی تو دوسرے کا قبضہ ختم ہو گیا ؟ فرمایا کہ جس طرح مرہون عادل کے پاس رہتا ہے اس کے باوجود اس کو مرتمن کے پاس شمار کیا جاتا ہے اسی طرح یہاں بھی ہر ایک کو دوسرے کے حق میں عادل کے مثل سمجھیں گے اور کسی کا بھی قبضہ ختم نہ ہوگا۔ مرہون ہلاک ہو جائے تو وہ اپنے دین کے مطابق ضامن قرار دئیے جائیں گے قال والمضمون على كل واحد منهما حصته من الدين لان عند الهلاك يصير كل واحد منهما مستوفيا حصته اذ الاستيفاء مما يتجزى ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور ان دونوں میں سے ہر ایک کے اوپر قرض میں سے اس کا حصہ مضمون ہوگا اس لئے کہ ہلاکت کے وقت ان دونوں میں سے ہر ایک اپنے حصہ کو وصول کرنے والا ہو جائیگا اس لئے کہ وصولیابی ان چیزوں میں سے ہے جس کی تقسیم ہو جاتی ہے۔ تشریح یعنی ہلاکت کے بغیر تو انقسام نہیں مانا گیا بلکہ یوں سمجھا گیا گویا ہر ایک کے قبضہ میں پورا مرہون ہے لیکن اگر مرہون ہلاک ہو جائے تو اب وہ اپنے دین کے مطابق ضامن قرار دیئے جائیں گے کیونکہ وصولیابی میں تجری ہو سکتی ہے۔ مثلاً دونوں کے زید پر پچاس روپے تھے ایک کے پچھپیں اور دوسرے کے چھپیں اور مرہون ہلاک ہو گیا تو دونوں کا قرض ساقط ہو گیا۔ دوسری مثال زید کے ذمہ پندرہ روپے ہیں ۱۰ خالد کے اور ۵ بکر کے زید نے ان دونوں کے پاس ۳۰ روپے رہن رکھے جن میں سے ۲۰ ہلاک ہو گئے اور باقی رہ گئے تو اب کیا حکم ہے؟ حکم یہ ہے کہ موجودہ دس کو خالد اور بکر تین حصوں میں تقسیم کر لیں پھر اس کا ۲/۳ خالد کا اور ۱/۳ بکر کا ہوگا اور زید ان دونوں کے قرض کی کمی کو اپنے پاس سے اس طرح پوری کریگا کہ وہ خالد کو اپنے پاس سے دس کا ثلث دیگا یعنی ۳ اور بکر کو پانچ کا تہائی دیگا یعنی است راہن نے ایک کا دین ادا کر دیا تو پوری گھڑی دوسرے کے پاس رہن رہے گی قال فأن اعطى احدهما دينه كان كله رهنا في يد الأخر لان جميع العين رهن في يد كل واحد منهما من غير تفرق وعلى هذا حبس المبيع اذا ادى احد المشتريين حصته من الثمن. ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا پس اگر راہن نے ان دونوں میں سے ایک کا قرض دید یا تو پورا مرہون دوسرے کے قبضہ میں رہن رہے گا اس لئے کہ پوری چیز بغیر کسی تفرق کے ان دونوں میں سے ہر ایک کے قبضہ میں رہن ہے اور اسی طرح مبیع کو روکنا ہے جبکہ دو مشتریوں میں سے ایک نے ثمن میں سے اپنا حصہ ادا کر دیا ہو۔ تشریح اگر راہن نے ان میں سے ایک کا قرض ادا کر دیا تو اب پوری گھڑی دوسرے کے پاس رہن رہے گی کیونکہ اس کے پاس تو وہ پہلے ہی سے پوری رہن مانی گئی تھی تو اب بھی ایسے ہی باقی رہے گی جب تک کہ اس کا قرض ادا نہ کر دیا جائے ، جیسے اگر دو شخصوں نے ایک چیز خریدی اور ان میں سے ایک نے اپنے حصہ کا ثمن ادا تو جب تک دوسرا بھی اپنے حصہ کا ثمن ادا نہیں کر دیگا جب تک بائع کو حق ہوگا کہ مبیع ان کے حوالہ نہ کرے۔
For the sake of permissibility, division will not be made; rather the pledged item will be considered held for the right of both, meaning without division the pledged item is fully with each, because it is impossible for the watch to be held by both simultaneously. So it is considered that it is held in exchange for the right of each of them. And since the purpose of gift is ownership, if one item is gifted fully to two persons, making both owners is impossible, so Imam Abu Hanifa did not declare it permissible. If the two creditors make a time-sharing arrangement in the pledge, what is the ruling? Then if they make a time-sharing arrangement, each of them during his turn is like a trustee (عدل) regarding the other's right. So if they agreed that the pledged watch will be with one for eight days and with the other for eight days, has the other's possession ended? He said: Just as when a pledge is with a trustee, it is still considered in the possession of the pledgor, similarly here each will be considered like a trustee for the other, and no one's possession ends. If the pledged item is destroyed, they will be held liable according to their debts. He (al-Quduri) said: The liability of each is his share of the debt, because at the time of destruction each becomes as if he had received his share, since receipt can be divided. So without destruction, division is not assumed; rather it is considered that the entire pledge is in each one's possession. But if it is destroyed, they become liable according to their debts, because receipt can be divided. Example: If both had fifty rupees on Zaid, one had twenty and the other thirty, and the pledge is destroyed, both debts are cancelled. Another example: Zaid owes fifteen rupees, ten to Khalid and five to Bakr. Zaid pledged thirty rupees with both, of which twenty are destroyed and ten remain. The ruling: The remaining ten are divided between Khalid and Bakr in three parts: 2/3 for Khalid and 1/3 for Bakr. And Zaid will compensate the shortfall from his own pocket, giving Khalid one-third of ten (3) and Bakr one-third of five (1). If the pledgor pays one of them his debt, the entire watch will remain as pledge with the other. He (al-Quduri) said: If he pays one of them his debt, the entire item remains pledge in the hand of the other, because the entire item is pledge in the hand of each without division. And similarly, the retention of the sold item when one of two buyers pays his share of the price. So if the pledgor pays one of them, the entire watch remains pledge with the other, because it was already considered fully pledged with him, and it remains so until his debt is paid. Just as if two persons buy an item and one pays his share, the seller has the right to withhold the item until the other also pays.
Source pages p. 253

Commentary
This passage discusses the rulings for a single item pledged to two creditors, a common scenario in Hanafi fiqh. The passage type is a ruling with proof, combining matn (from al-Quduri) and commentary (sharh). The author addresses several sub-issues: (1) The concept of division (انقسام) in pledge: Since possession cannot be physically divided, the item is considered held fully for each creditor's right. This is contrasted with gift (ھبہ), which requires actual transfer of ownership and is invalid if given to two persons without division. (2) Time-sharing (مھایات): If the two creditors agree to alternate possession, each is treated as a trustee (عادل) for the other during his turn, so possession of both remains intact. (3) Destruction of the pledge: Upon destruction, each creditor is deemed to have received his share of the debt proportionally, because receipt (استیفاء) can be divided. Examples illustrate partial destruction and the resulting liability of the pledgor for any shortfall. (4) Payment to one creditor: If the pledgor pays off one creditor, the entire item remains as security for the other, because the pledge was considered fully in each hand from the beginning. An analogy to the sale of an item by two buyers is provided: if one buyer pays his share, the seller may retain the item until the other pays as well. These rulings all hinge on the principle that possession of a pledge is undivided (ghayr mufarraq) and that each creditor's right covers the entire item.

Key Terms
رهن (rahn): A pledge or collateral; an item given as security for a debt.
محبوس (mabhūs): Held or impounded; the legal status of a pledge being retained by the creditor.
ہبہ (hiba): A gift; a contract that transfers ownership without compensation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is a pledge to two creditors valid but a gift to two persons invalid in the Hanafi school?
A) Because gift requires immediate possession, while pledge does not.
B) Because pledge only requires retention, while gift requires transfer of ownership.
C) Because the pledge is based on contract, while gift is voluntary.
D) Because the pledge is revocable, while gift is not.

Key Takeaway
A pledge to two creditors is valid because possession is legally considered undivided, each holding the entire item for his right, in contrast to a gift which requires division of ownership.

Rahn — Pledge
intermediate
8 min
Time-Sharing Arrangement (Muhayat) in Pledge
Ruling on time-sharing (muhayat) in a pledge

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on time-sharing of a pledged item between two creditors and identify the legal status of each creditor's possession.

Core Idea
Even with physical possession alternating, each creditor is considered a trustee for the other; no one's possessory right ends.

If two creditors agree to take turns holding the pledged item, does the physical possession cancel the other's right? The Hanafi school answers by comparing each creditor's role to that of a trustee (adeel). This lesson explains the ruling on muhayat and its implications.

Guided Path
1
Define muhayat
Muhayat is a time-sharing arrangement where each creditor holds the pledge for a specified period (e.g., eight days each).
The arrangement must be agreed upon by both creditors.
2
Understand the problem
Since possession of a pledge is legally undivided, physically handing the item to one creditor seems to remove the other's possession.
But the legal right of the non-possessing creditor must be preserved.
3
Apply the trustee analogy
Each creditor during his turn is treated like a trustee (adeel) for the other. The item is still considered in the possession of both.
Just as a trustee holds for the pledgor, here the creditor holds for the other creditor's right.
4
Conclude the ruling
The possession of the other creditor does not end. The initial undivided possession remains legally intact.
This ensures the security of both debts is maintained.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

So without destruction, division is not assumed; rather it is considered that the entire pledge is in each one's possession. But if it is destroyed, they become liable according to their debts, because receipt can be divided. Example: If both had fifty rupees on Zaid, one had twenty and the other thirty, and the pledge is destroyed, both debts are cancelled. Another example: Zaid owes fifteen rupees, ten to Khalid and five to Bakr. Zaid pledged thirty rupees with both, of which twenty are destroyed and ten remain. The ruling: The remaining ten are divided between Khalid and Bakr in three parts: 2/3 for Khalid and 1/3 for Bakr. And Zaid will compensate the shortfall from his own pocket, giving Khalid one-third of ten (3) and Bakr one-third of five (1). If the pledgor pays one of them his debt, the entire watch will remain as pledge with the other. He (al-Quduri) said: If he pays one of them his debt, the entire item remains pledge in the hand of the other, because the entire item is pledge in the hand of each without division. And similarly, the retention of the sold item when one of two buyers pays his share of the price. So if the pledgor pays one of them, the entire watch remains pledge with the other, because it was already considered fully pledged with him, and it remains so until his debt is paid. Just as if two persons buy an item and one pays his share, the seller has the right to withhold the item until the other also pays.
Source pages p. 253

Commentary
This passage discusses the rulings for a single item pledged to two creditors, a common scenario in Hanafi fiqh. The passage type is a ruling with proof, combining matn (from al-Quduri) and commentary (sharh). The author addresses several sub-issues: (1) The concept of division (انقسام) in pledge: Since possession cannot be physically divided, the item is considered held fully for each creditor's right. This is contrasted with gift (ھبہ), which requires actual transfer of ownership and is invalid if given to two persons without division. (2) Time-sharing (مھایات): If the two creditors agree to alternate possession, each is treated as a trustee (عادل) for the other during his turn, so possession of both remains intact. (3) Destruction of the pledge: Upon destruction, each creditor is deemed to have received his share of the debt proportionally, because receipt (استیفاء) can be divided. Examples illustrate partial destruction and the resulting liability of the pledgor for any shortfall. (4) Payment to one creditor: If the pledgor pays off one creditor, the entire item remains as security for the other, because the pledge was considered fully in each hand from the beginning. An analogy to the sale of an item by two buyers is provided: if one buyer pays his share, the seller may retain the item until the other pays as well. These rulings all hinge on the principle that possession of a pledge is undivided (ghayr mufarraq) and that each creditor's right covers the entire item.

Key Terms
مھایات (muhāyāt): Time-sharing arrangement among creditors for possession of a pledge.
عادل (ādiil): Trustee; an impartial person entrusted with something.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) He loses his security temporarily.
B) He retains his right because the holder is his trustee.
C) He must also have actual possession to maintain his right.
D) The pledge becomes void.

Key Takeaway
A time-sharing arrangement (muhayat) in a pledge is valid; each creditor acts as a trustee for the other during his turn, and the undivided possession of both continues.

Destruction of Pledge and Payment to One Creditor
Rulings on destruction and partial payment in a pledge to two creditors

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rules for liability when a pledge to two creditors is destroyed, and explain the effect of the pledgor paying off one creditor on the remaining pledge.

Core Idea
Upon destruction, each creditor is deemed to have received his share proportionally; paying off one creditor leaves the entire item as security for the other.

What happens if the pledged item is destroyed? How is the loss apportioned? And what if the pledgor pays off one creditor – does the other's security shrink? This lesson covers the key Hanafi rulings on these practical scenarios, building on the principle of undivided possession.

Guided Path
1
Understand destruction liability
When a pledge to two creditors is destroyed, each creditor is considered to have received his share of the debt proportionally.
This is because receipt (istifa) can be divided, even though possession was undivided.
2
Apply the proportional example
If debts are different, the destruction of the item satisfies each debt according to its proportion of the total debt.
The pledgor may still owe the difference if the pledge value was less than total debt.
3
Analyze payment to one creditor
If the pledgor pays off one creditor, the entire item remains as security for the other, because the pledge was undivided.
This mirrors the rule for a sale: if one buyer pays his share, the seller may retain the item until the other pays.
4
Synthesize with undivided possession
Both rulings stem from the same principle: each creditor's right covers the entire item. Destruction makes proportion; payment does not reduce the item's encumbrance.
These are practical applications of the core concept.

میں سے ایک کا قرض ادا کر دیا تو اب پوری گھڑی دوسرے کے پاس رہن رہے گی کیونکہ اس کے پاس تو وہ پہلے ہی سے پوری رہن مانی گئی تھی تو اب بھی ایسے ہی باقی رہے گی جب تک کہ اس کا قرض ادا نہ کر دیا جائے ، جیسے اگر دو شخصوں نے ایک چیز خریدی اور ان میں سے ایک نے اپنے حصہ کا ثمن ادا تو جب تک دوسرا بھی اپنے حصہ کا ثمن ادا نہیں کر دیگا جب تک بائع کو حق ہوگا کہ مبیع ان کے حوالہ نہ کرے۔
For the sake of permissibility, division will not be made; rather the pledged item will be considered held for the right of both, meaning without division the pledged item is fully with each, because it is impossible for the watch to be held by both simultaneously. So it is considered that it is held in exchange for the right of each of them. And since the purpose of gift is ownership, if one item is gifted fully to two persons, making both owners is impossible, so Imam Abu Hanifa did not declare it permissible. If the two creditors make a time-sharing arrangement in the pledge, what is the ruling? Then if they make a time-sharing arrangement, each of them during his turn is like a trustee (عدل) regarding the other's right. So if they agreed that the pledged watch will be with one for eight days and with the other for eight days, has the other's possession ended? He said: Just as when a pledge is with a trustee, it is still considered in the possession of the pledgor, similarly here each will be considered like a trustee for the other, and no one's possession ends. If the pledged item is destroyed, they will be held liable according to their debts. He (al-Quduri) said: The liability of each is his share of the debt, because at the time of destruction each becomes as if he had received his share, since receipt can be divided. So without destruction, division is not assumed; rather it is considered that the entire pledge is in each one's possession. But if it is destroyed, they become liable according to their debts, because receipt can be divided. Example: If both had fifty rupees on Zaid, one had twenty and the other thirty, and the pledge is destroyed, both debts are cancelled. Another example: Zaid owes fifteen rupees, ten to Khalid and five to Bakr. Zaid pledged thirty rupees with both, of which twenty are destroyed and ten remain. The ruling: The remaining ten are divided between Khalid and Bakr in three parts: 2/3 for Khalid and 1/3 for Bakr. And Zaid will compensate the shortfall from his own pocket, giving Khalid one-third of ten (3) and Bakr one-third of five (1). If the pledgor pays one of them his debt, the entire watch will remain as pledge with the other. He (al-Quduri) said: If he pays one of them his debt, the entire item remains pledge in the hand of the other, because the entire item is pledge in the hand of each without division. And similarly, the retention of the sold item when one of two buyers pays his share of the price. So if the pledgor pays one of them, the entire watch remains pledge with the other, because it was already considered fully pledged with him, and it remains so until his debt is paid. Just as if two persons buy an item and one pays his share, the seller has the right to withhold the item until the other also pays.

Commentary
This passage discusses the rulings for a single item pledged to two creditors, a common scenario in Hanafi fiqh. The passage type is a ruling with proof, combining matn (from al-Quduri) and commentary (sharh). The author addresses several sub-issues: (1) The concept of division (انقسام) in pledge: Since possession cannot be physically divided, the item is considered held fully for each creditor's right. This is contrasted with gift (ھبہ), which requires actual transfer of ownership and is invalid if given to two persons without division. (2) Time-sharing (مھایات): If the two creditors agree to alternate possession, each is treated as a trustee (عادل) for the other during his turn, so possession of both remains intact. (3) Destruction of the pledge: Upon destruction, each creditor is deemed to have received his share of the debt proportionally, because receipt (استیفاء) can be divided. Key Terms
استیفاء (istīfā'): The act of receiving satisfaction of a debt; in pledge, it refers to the creditor obtaining payment through destruction of the pledge.
مضمون (madmūn): Liable; the amount for which a person is responsible.

Partial Payment Does Not Partly Release a Pledge
Ruling that entire pledge stays with remaining creditor

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the effect of partial debt payment on a pledge and explain the qiyas (analogy) to joint purchase.

Core Idea
Partial payment does not partly release a pledge; the entire property remains with the unpaid creditor.

This passage from Quduri's Mukhtasar, as explained in Ashraf al-Hidaya, presents a clear ruling on a common scenario: a debtor pledges a single item to two creditors, then pays off one. The key legal question is whether the pledge is divided or remains whole. The Hanafi answer, supported by a powerful analogy, ensures that the unpaid creditor's security is not diminished until full payment is received.

Guided Path
1
Identify the case and parties
Begin by identifying all parties: a rahin (debtor) who gives a single item as a pledge (marhun) to two murtahin (creditors). Then the debtor pays one creditor in full.
The item is undivided and held jointly by the two creditors.
2
State the ruling and its basis
State the ruling: the entire pledged property remains with the unpaid creditor. The basis is that each creditor originally held the entire item as security (min ghayri tafarruq), so payment to one does not release it.
The ruling is explicit in the matn: 'kulluhu rahnan fi yad al-akhar'.
3
Extract the illa (effective cause)
The illa is that the property is held collectively as security for the entire debt, without division. This means the unpaid creditor's claim extends to the whole item.
This illa is derived from the phrase 'min ghayri tafarruq'.
4
Apply the qiyas to the analogue case
The text draws an analogy (qiyas jali) to a joint purchase: if two buyers jointly buy an item and one pays his share, the seller may retain the entire item until the other buyer also pays. Apply this analogy to confirm that the pledge case is consistent.
This shows the Hanafi method of extending rulings through clear analogy.
5
Conclude with the practical consequence
Conclude that until the unpaid creditor's debt is fully satisfied, he may retain the entire pledge. The debtor cannot demand partial release.
This ruling is mufta bihi and unanimously held in the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
راہن نے ایک کا دین ادا کر دیا تو پوری گھڑی دوسرے کے پاس رہن رہے گی قال فأن اعطى احدهما دينه كان كله رهنا في يد الأخر لان جميع العين رهن في يد كل واحد منهما من غير تفرق وعلى هذا حبس المبيع اذا ادى احد المشتريين حصته من الثمن.
ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا پس اگر راہن نے ان دونوں میں سے ایک کا قرض دید یا تو پورا مرہون دوسرے کے قبضہ میں رہن رہے گا اس لئے کہ پوری چیز بغیر کسی تفرق کے ان دونوں میں سے ہر ایک کے قبضہ میں رہن ہے اور اسی طرح مبیع کو روکنا ہے جبکہ دو مشتریوں میں سے ایک نے ثمن میں سے اپنا حصہ ادا کر دیا ہو۔ تشریح اگر راہن نے ان میں سے ایک کا قرض ادا کر دیا تو اب پوری گھڑی دوسرے کے پاس رہن رہے گی کیونکہ اس کے پاس تو وہ پہلے ہی سے پوری رہن مانی گئی تھی تو اب بھی ایسے ہی باقی رہے گی جب تک کہ اس کا قرض ادا نہ کر دیا جائے ، جیسے اگر دو شخصوں نے ایک چیز خریدی اور ان میں سے ایک نے اپنے حصہ کا ثمن ادا تو جب تک دوسرا بھی اپنے حصہ کا ثمن ادا نہیں کر دیگا جب تک بائع کو حق ہوگا کہ مبیع ان کے حوالہ نہ کرے۔
If the pawnor pays the debt of one of them, the entire pledge remains as a pledge in the hand of the other, because the entire property is a pledge in the hand of each of them without division. And upon this is the retention of the sold item when one of the two buyers pays his share of the price. Translation: Al-Quduri said: So if the pawnor pays the debt of one of these two, then the entire pledged property remains as a pledge in the possession of the other, because the entire thing, without any division, is a pledge in the possession of each of them. And similarly, the sold item is retained when one of the two buyers has paid his portion of the price. Explanation: If the pawnor pays the debt of one of them, then the entire article remains as a pledge with the other, because it was already recognized as a full pledge in his hand, so it remains as such until his debt is paid. Like if two persons buy an item and one of them pays his share of the price, the seller has the right not to hand over the sold item until the other also pays his share.
Source pages p. 254

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from Quduri's Mukhtasar: when a debtor pledges a single item to two creditors, and then pays off one creditor entirely, the pledged item remains fully in the hands of the other creditor as security for the remaining debt. The reasoning is that each creditor originally holds the entire pledged property as security (not just a share), so payment to one does not release the property from the other's claim. The author supports this with an analogy (qiyas jali) to the case of a sale where two buyers jointly purchase an item. If one buyer pays his share, the seller is entitled to withhold the entire item until the second buyer also pays. Just as the seller's right to retain the sold item continues until full payment, so too does the creditor's right to retain the pledged property continue until all debts are satisfied. This ruling illustrates the Hanafi principle that a pledge secures the entire debt, and partial payment does not fractionally release the pledge.

Key Terms
رہن (rahn): The contract of pledge by which property is given as security for a debt.
رھن (مرهون) (murtahan (marhun)): The property that is pledged as security.
مرتہن (murtahin): The creditor who receives the pledge.
راہن (rahin): The debtor who gives the pledge.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a debtor pledges a watch to two creditors and then pays one creditor his full debt, what happens to the watch?
A) The watch is divided equally between the two creditors.
B) The watch is freed from pledge entirely.
C) The watch remains fully pledged to the unpaid creditor.
D) The watch goes to the debtor's heirs.

Key Takeaway
The entire pledge remains with the unpaid creditor until his debt is fully paid; partial payment to another creditor does not release any part of the pledged property.

Two Debtors Pledge One Item to One Creditor
Ruling on joint pledge by two pawnors

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a joint pledge by two pawnors and explain why the presence of multiple owners does not invalidate the contract due to the nature of possession.

Core Idea
When two debtors pledge one item, possession is unitary, so shuyu' does not invalidate.

This passage from the Hidayah commentary on the Mukhtasar of Al-Quduri addresses a practical scenario: two debtors owe money to one creditor and jointly pledge a single item as security. The apparent problem is that the item is co-owned (shuyu'), which normally invalidates a pledge because the mortgagee cannot possess a share in isolation. The Hanafi reply is clear and instructive: possession of the entire item is taken without any indivision, so the pledge is valid. This lesson unpacks the reasoning and its application.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi ruling
Identify what Al-Quduri rules: two men pledging one item to one creditor is valid, and the creditor may hold it until the full debt is paid.
2
Identify the potential objection
The apparent problem is shuyu' (undivided co-ownership), which normally invalidates rahn because the creditor cannot possess a share without indivision.
Shuyu' is generally a barrier in contracts requiring full possession.
3
Analyze the author's response
The commentator rebuts by stating 'possession of the pledge occurs in its entirety without indivision' – the creditor physically holds the whole item, not a theoretical share.
Physical possession overrides the theoretical ownership division.
4
Trace the qiyas
Compare with a single pawnor: possession is unitary. The same applies here despite multiple pawnors because possession is not divisible.
The illa (cause) is that possession does not admit of shuyu'.
5
Apply the ruling
Explain to a layperson: the pledge is valid because the creditor takes the entire item in hand, and ownership shares do not affect the unity of possession.
Focus on the concrete act of taking possession.

دو قرض خواہوں کا ایک آدمی کے پاس رہن رکھنے کا حکم
قال وان رهن رجلان بدين عليهما رجلا رهنا واحداً فهو جائز والرهن رهن بكل الدين وللمرتهن ان يمسكه حتى يستوفى جميع الدين لان قبض الرهن يحصل في الكل من غير شيوع
ترجمہ امام کرتی نے اپنی مختصر میں فرمایا ہے اور اگر دو شخصوں نے اس قرض کے بدلہ میں جو ان پر ہے ایک شخص کے پاس رہن رکھا تو یہ جائز ہے اور رہن پورے قرض کے بدلہ رہن ہو گا اور مرتہن کو حق ہوگا کہ مرہون کو روکے رکھے یہاں تک کہ پورا قرض وصول کر لے اس لئے کہ رہن کا قبضہ بغیر شیوع کے کل میں داخل ہوا ہے۔ تشریح زید اور بکر کے اوپر خالد کا قرض ہے تو ان دونوں نے خالد کے پاس ایک چیز رہن رکھی تو رہن جائز ہے اور اس مرہون کو دونوں کے قرض کا بدل شمار کیا جائے گا اور خالد جب تک پورا قرض وصول نہ کر لے اس کو حق ہوگا کہ مرہون کو روکے رکھے۔ سوال اس میں تو بظاہر شیوع معلوم ہو رہا ہے کہ نصف مرہون زید کی ملکیت ہے اور نصف مثلاً بکر کی اور شیوع جواز رہن کے منافی ہے؟ جواب مصنف نے لان قبض الرھن سے اس کا جواب دیا ہے جس کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ جیسے اگر ایک راہن ہو اور ایک ہی مرتہن ہو اور اس وقت شیوع نہیں تھا اس طرح اگر دو راہن اور ایک مرتہن ہو تب بھی شیوع نہ ہوگا کیونکہ قبضہ میں کوئی شیوع نہیں ہے لہذا یہ عقد رہن جائز ہوگا۔
Ruling on two debtors pledging to one person. He said: And if two men pledge a single item as security for a debt owed to one man, it is valid, and the pledge is a pledge for the entire debt, and the mortgagee (creditor) has the right to hold it until he recovers the full debt, because possession of the pledge occurs in its entirety without indivision. Translation: Imam Quduri said in his Mukhtasar: If two persons pledge a single item to one person in lieu of a debt they owe him, it is valid. The pledge will be a pledge for the entire debt, and the mortgagee has the right to retain the pledged property until he recovers the full debt, because possession of the pledge is taken of the whole without indivision. Explanation: Zaid and Bakr owe a debt to Khalid. They pledge one item to Khalid. The pledge is valid, and the pledged property is considered security for both of their debts. Khalid has the right to hold the pledged property until he recovers the full debt. Question: Apparent indivision (shuyu') seems to exist here because half of the pledged property belongs to Zaid and half to Bakr, and shuyu' is contrary to the permissibility of a pledge. Answer: The author answers from the statement 'because possession of the pledge occurs in its entirety without indivision.' The gist is: just as when there is one pawnor and one pledgee there was no shuyu', similarly when there are two pawnors and one pledgee, there is still no shuyu', because possession does not involve indivision. Therefore this pledge contract is valid.
Source pages p. 254

Commentary
This passage discusses the validity of a pledge when two debtors jointly pledge a single item to one creditor. According to the Hanafi school, this is valid. The pledged item secures the entire debt from both debtors. The creditor may retain the item until the full debt is paid. The potential objection is that the item is owned by two persons (shuyu' - undivided shares), and such indivision normally invalidates a pledge because the pledge requires exclusive possession. The response, based on the phrase 'possession of the pledge occurs in its entirety without indivision,' is that possession is a physical reality that does not admit of theoretical division. When a creditor takes possession of the item, he holds the entire item, not a share. Therefore, the fact that ownership shares are divided does not affect the validity of the pledge. The Hanafi school applies the same principle as when a single pawnor pledges: possession is unitary. This ruling shows the Hanafi emphasis on the actual nature of possession (qabd) over theoretical ownership shares.

Key Terms
شیوع (shuyu'): Undivided co-ownership or indivision; ownership shares that have not been physically separated.
قبض (qabd): Taking physical possession of the pledged property by the creditor.
جائز (ja'iz): Permissible and valid in the sense of legal binding effect.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Two debtors (Zaid and Bakr) owe money to Khalid and pledge one item jointly. Is the pledge valid?
A) Invalid because the item has shared ownership (shuyu').
B) Valid only if each debtor pledges his half separately.
C) Valid because possession of the whole item is taken without indivision.
D) Invalid because only one debtor can pledge items.

Key Takeaway
A joint pledge by two debtors is valid because possession is taken of the entire item, and indivision in possession overrides indivision in ownership.

Conflicting Claims: Two Claimants Each Prove Pledge of Same Slave
Ruling that contradictory evidence cancels out

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when two claimants each prove an identical claim over a single pledged item and explain why the evidence is rejected.

Core Idea
When two contradictory proofs cannot be reconciled, both must be canceled — preferring one without basis is invalid.

This lesson examines a scenario where two creditors both claim the same slave was pledged to them individually. The Hanafi ruling is that both claims are invalid because any possible judgment — awarding the whole slave, or half, or picking one — is either impossible or unjust. Understanding this helps clarify how Islamic courts handle contradictory evidence in pledge cases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the case
We have two claimants (Zaid and Bakr) each providing evidence that the same slave, currently in the debtor's possession, was pledged to them separately.
The slave is not in either claimant's hand.
2
Recognize impossibility of awarding the whole slave to both
Awarding the entire slave to each claimant is impossible because a single item cannot be wholly pledged to two different people simultaneously.
This is physically and legally impossible.
3
Examine alternatives
Two other alternatives are considered: (a) awarding the whole slave to one claimant arbitrarily is invalid due to lack of preference (tarjih bila murajjah), and (b) awarding half to each is invalid because it introduces indivision (shuyu') into possession.
All three possible judgments are impermissible.
4
Conclude mutual cancellation
Since both evidences lead to impossible outcomes, they cannot be acted upon. They cancel each other out (tasaqut), and no judgment is given.
The slave remains with the debtor.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
دو آدمیوں میں سے ہر ایک نے بینہ قائم کئے کہ جو اس کے قبضے میں غلام ہے وہ میں نے رہن رکھا تھا اور اس پر قبضہ کیا تھا تو یہ باطل ہے
فان اقام الرجلان كل واحد منهما البيئة على رجل انه رهنه عبده الذى فى يده وقبضه فهو باطل لان كل واحد منهما اثبت ببيئته انه رهنه كل العبد ولا وجه الى القضاء لكل واحد منهما بالكل لان العبد الواحد يستحيل ان يكون كله رهنا لهذا وكله رهنا لذالك فى حالة واحدة ولا الى القضاء بكله لواحد بعينه لعلم الأولوية ولا الى القضاء لكل واحد منهما بالنصف لانه يؤدى الى الشيوع فتعذر العمل بهما وتعين التهاتر
ترجمہ: پس اگر دو آدمیوں نے ان میں سے ہر ایک نے کسی شخص پر بعینہ قائم کیا کہ اس نے اپنے اس غلام کو جو اس کے قبضہ میں ہے اس کے پاس رہن رکھا تھا اور اس نے اس پر قبضہ کیا تھا تو یہ باطل ہے اس لئے کہ ان میں سے ہر ایک نے اپنے بینہ سے یہ ثابت کیا ہے کہ اس نے پورے غلام کو اس کے پاس رہن رکھا تھا اور ان میں سے ہر ایک کیلئے پورے غلام کے فیصلہ کی کوئی وجہ نہیں ہے اس لئے کہ محال ہے کہ ایک پورا غلام اس کے پاس بھی رہن ہو اور اس کے پاس بھی ایک ہی حالت میں اور اولویت نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے پورے غلام کا ایک کیلئے فیصلہ کرنے کی بھی کوئی وجہ نہیں ہے اور ان میں سے ہر ایک کیلئے نصف کے فیصلہ کی بھی کوئی وجہ نہیں ہے اس لئے کہ یہ شیوع کی جانب مؤدی ہوگا تو دونوں بینہ پر عمل متعذر ہے تو تساقط و ترک متعین ہو گیا۔ تشریح زید اور بکر دونوں دعوی کرتے ہیں کہ خالد کے قبضہ میں جو غلام ہے اس نے ہمارے پاس اس کو رہن رکھا تھا جس پر ہم نے قبضہ بھی کر لیا تھا یعنی زید کا دعویٰ اپنے لئے اور بکر کا اپنے لئے ہے اور دونوں نے گواہوں سے اپنا دعوا ثابت کر دیا تو اب کیا حکم ہے؟ اس میں مختلف صورتیں ہیں۔  1- زید اور بکر میں سے اگر وہ غلام کسی ایک کے قبضہ میں ہو تو جس کے قبضہ میں ہوگا اس کے لئے فیصلہ کر دیا جائیگا اس کو حق تقدم حاصل ہے۔ 2- ان دونوں کے قبضہ میں ہے تو کسی دلیل سے اگر تقدم و تاخر معلوم نہ ہو سکے تو قاضی کچھ فیصلہ نہ کر سکے گا۔ 3- غلام راہن یعنی خالد کے قبضہ میں ہے تو قاضی کچھ فیصلہ نہ کر سکے گا اور ان کا اقامت بینہ باطل ہوگا اور مصنف نے یہی آخری صورت کتاب میں ذکر فرمائی ہے۔ کیونکہ فیصلہ کرنے کی تین ہی صورتیں ہو سکتی تھیں اور تینوں باطل ہیں۔ 
- پورے پورے غلام کا ہر ایک کیلئے فیصلہ کیا جائے یہ باطل و محال ہے کیونکہ ایک ہی غلام ایک ہی وقت میں دونوں کے قبضہ میں الگ الگ ہو محال ہے۔
- پورے غلام کا فیصلہ ان دونوں میں سے ایک کیلئے کیا جائے یہ بھی باطل ہے کیونکہ ترجیح بلا مرجح ہے۔
If two men each provide evidence against a man that he pledged his slave who is in his hand and took possession, it is invalid, because each of them proved by his evidence that he pledged the entire slave, and there is no basis to give judgment to each of them for the entire slave, since it is impossible for one slave to be entirely a pledge for this one and entirely a pledge for that one in the same state. Nor to give judgment of the entire slave to one specifically, due to lack of preference. Nor to give judgment to each of them for half, because that would lead to indivision (shuyu'). So acting upon both evidences is impossible, and mutual cancellation (tasaqut) is determined. Translation: So if two men each establish evidence that he pledged the slave who is in the hand of the other and took possession, it is invalid... Explanation: Zaid and Bakr both claim that the slave in Khalid's possession was pledged to them and they took possession. They each prove their claim with witnesses. What is the ruling? There are different scenarios. 1) If the slave is in the possession of one of the claimants, judgment is given to the one in possession due to priority. 2) If in the possession of both, and no evidence of precedence, the judge cannot decide. 3) If the slave is in the hand of the pawnor (Khalid), the judge cannot decide and their evidence is invalid. This last case is what the author mentions. Because three possible judgments are all invalid: a) awarding entire slave to each is impossible; b) awarding to one without preference is invalid; c) awarding half to each leads to shuyu'.
Source pages p. 255

Commentary
This passage deals with a situation where two claimants (Zaid and Bakr) each provide evidence (bayyinah) that the same slave, currently in the possession of Khalid (the original pawnor), was pledged to them individually and they took possession. The ruling is that both evidences are invalid (batil) because any possible judgment is impossible or impermissible. The text considers three potential judgments: (1) awarding the entire slave to each claimant – impossible because one item cannot be entirely pledged to two different creditors simultaneously. (2) awarding the entire slave to one claimant arbitrarily – invalid due to lack of preference (tarjih bilā murajjah). (3) awarding half to each – invalid because it would introduce shuyu' (indivision) into possession, which is prohibited in pledge. Therefore, both sets of evidence are mutually contradictory and cannot be acted upon; they cancel each other out (tasaqut). The commentary further distinguishes three scenarios based on physical possession: if the slave is in the hand of one claimant, that claimant prevails due to prior possession; if in the hands of both, the judge cannot decide without proof of precedence; if in the hand of the debtor (Khalid), as in the given case, judgment is impossible. This ruling illustrates the Hanafi principle that evidence leading to contradictory and impossible outcomes is rejected.

Key Terms
بینہ (bayyinah): Legal evidence, typically the testimony of two male witnesses or one male and two females.
باطل (batil): Invalid or void; producing no legal effect.
تساقط (tasaqut): Mutual cancellation or rejection of conflicting evidence when it is impossible to act upon both.
ترجیح بلا مرجح (tarjih bila murajjah): Preferring one over the other without any valid basis for preference.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the case where two claimants each prove that the same slave in the debtor's hand was pledged to them, why is awarding half the slave to each claimant invalid?
A) Because the slave is indivisible.
B) Because it would introduce shuyu' (indivision) into possession.
C) Because the claimants did not request half.
D) Because the slave belongs to the debtor.

Key Takeaway
When contradictory proofs lead to impossible or impermissible outcomes, both must be canceled (tasaqut).
