Pawn of a Slave Claimed by Two Creditors: Qiyas Overrides Istihsan
Intra-Hanafi dispute on pawn with conflicting claims

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on a pawn claimed by two creditors with unknown dates, and identify why Imam Muhammad preferred qiyas over istihsan in this exceptional case.

Core Idea
When two pawn claims conflict with unknown dates, the pawn is batil — qiyas overrides istihsan in this exceptional case.

In this lesson, we examine a complex scenario in the law of pawn (rahn): two creditors each claim the same slave was pawned to them, with no known priority. The Hanafi school faces a tension between qiyas (analogy) and istihsan (juristic preference). Imam Muhammad, who is known for favoring istihsan, here adopts the stricter qiyas ruling. Understanding why is key to mastering the principles of rahn and the hierarchy of evidence in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core scenario
Two creditors each claim that a slave was pawned to them, but the dates of the pawn contracts are unknown. The judge cannot give full possession to both.
This conflicts with the condition that a pawn must be fully possessed by one creditor.
2
Understand why shuyu' invalidates division
Dividing the slave half-half would create shuyu' (common ownership) in the pawn, which is impermissible in rahn. Shuyu' makes the contract invalid (batil).
Shuyu' is a condition of validity: the pawn must be exclusively held.
3
Examine the qiyas position
By qiyas, since both claims cannot be upheld, the judge should not rule in favor of either; the pawn is void. This is the default Hanafi position.
Qiyas here is based on the impossibility of acting on two conflicting evidences.
4
Consider the istihsan alternative
Istihsan would allow dividing the slave half-half, based on the analogy of simultaneous death where all are considered to have died together. But this contradicts each claimant's evidence.
Imam Muhammad recorded this istihsan in al-Mabsut but then rejected it.
5
Analyze why Imam Muhammad adopted qiyas
Because each claimant's evidence proves exclusive right to the whole, a half-ruling contradicts the evidence. Qiyas is stronger here, making this one of the seven exceptional cases where qiyas prevails over istihsan.
This shows that istihsan is not always superior; evidence integrity can override it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

رہن ہے یا نہیں ولا يقال انه يكون رهنا لهما كانهما ارتهناه معا اذجهل التاريخ بينهما وجعل فى كتاب الشهادات هذا وجه الاستحسان لا نانقول هذ اعمل على خلاف ما اقتضته الحجة لان كلا منهما اثبت ببينته حبسا ساتھ اس کو رہن لیا تھا جیسے اگر کچھ لوگ ایک ساتھ دریا میں ڈوب جائیں یا آگ میں جل جائیں یا مکان کے گرنے سے مرجائیں اور موت کے تقدم و تاخر کا علم نہ ہو تو یوں سمجھا جاتا ہے کہ سب ایک ساتھ مرے ہیں اسی نے مبسوط کی کتاب الشهادات میں استحسان کی دلیل ذکر کیا ہے۔ تنبیه ۲ مصنف کی یہ عبارت حبسا يكون الخ کا خلاصہ یہ ہے کہ ان کا مقصد پورے غلام کے رہن کو اپنے پاس ثابت کرنا ہے تو صورت مذکورہ میں دعوے کے خلاف فیصلہ کرنا لازم آئیگا یعنی مثلہ سے مراد تمامہ لیا جائے اب مطلب ہو گیا الى استيفاء تمام حقه امام محمد کا نقطہ نظر وما ذكرناه وان كان قياسا لكن محمدا اخذ به لقوته ترجمہ اور جو ہم نے ذکر کیا ہے اگر قیاس ہے لیکن محمد نے اس کو اختیار کیا ہے اس کی قوت کی وجہ سے۔ تشریح مصنف یہ فرمانا چاہتے ہیں کہ یہاں امام محمد نے استحسان کو چھوڑ کر قیاس پر عمل کیا ہے کیونکہ قیاس استحسان سے قوی اور مضبوط ہے۔ ورنہ عموماً استحسان کو قیاس پر ترجیح دی جاتی ہے کل سات مقامات ہیں جہاں قیاس کو استحسان پر مقدم کیا جاتا ہے ورنہ ہر جگہ اس کے بر عکس ہوتا ہے ( وفصلنا نكتة وسرة في درس الحسامي)
The slave is to be made half-half between the two, and this is also invalid because shuyu' (common ownership) becomes necessary. Summary of speech: when acting on both evidences became impossible, then dropping and abandoning became determined. Is that slave a pawn for them or not? And it should not be said that it becomes a pawn for them as if they both took it as pawn together when the date is unknown between them, and he made in the Book of Testimonies this the face of istihsan. We say this is acting contrary to what the evidence required, because each of them established by his evidence a habs (right to hold) which is a means to the like of it in recovery, and by this judgment a habs is established which is a means to half of it in recovery, and this is not acting in accordance with the evidence. Translation: And it should not be said that the slave will become a pawn for the two of them, as if both took it as pawn together, while the date between the two evidences is unknown, and Muhammad in the Mabsut in the Book of Testimonies considered this the proof of istihsan. Because we will say that this (its being a pawn for both) is acting contrary to the requirement of the evidence (bayyinah), because each of them by his own evidence established a habs which is a means to the like of him in recovery, and by this judgment a habs is established which is a means to half of it in recovery, and this is not acting in accordance with the evidence. Explanation: The question is that it is possible to make the slave half-half between them because the date is unknown, so it will be considered that both took it as pawn together, just as if some people drown together in a river or burn in fire or die from collapse of a building and the precedence and delay of death is unknown, then it is considered that all died together; similarly here will it be considered? Answer: In doing so, there would be acting against the requirement of each one's establishment of evidence, because the purpose of each one's establishment of evidence is that he is entitled to the entire slave, and here entitlement will only be to half, and there is no right to act against the requirement of evidence. Warning: Not making a judgment is qiyas, and istihsan is to make a judgment, i.e., to decide it as half-half between them, and Imam Muhammad mentioned this same proof as the proof of istihsan in the Mabsut in the Book of Testimonies. Warning 2: The summary of the author's phrase 'habsan yakunu al-kh' is that their purpose is to prove the pawn of the entire slave with them, so in the mentioned case, a judgment contrary to the claim becomes necessary, meaning by 'mithlihi' is meant the entirety, so the meaning becomes 'to recover all of his right'. Imam Muhammad's viewpoint: And what we mentioned, even if it is qiyas, but Muhammad adopted it due to its strength. Translation: And what we mentioned, even if it is qiyas, but Muhammad adopted it due to its strength. Explanation: The author wants to say that here Imam Muhammad left istihsan and acted on qiyas because qiyas is stronger and more powerful than istihsan. Otherwise, generally istihsan is given preference over qiyas; there are seven places where qiyas is given precedence over istihsan, otherwise everywhere it is the opposite (and we have detailed the point and secret in the lesson of al-Husami).
Source pages p. 256

Commentary
This passage deals with a complex scenario in the law of pawn (rahn): two creditors each claim that a particular slave was given to him as pawn by the same pawnor (rahin), but the dates of the two pawn contracts are unknown. The text first states that it is invalid to divide the slave half-half between them because that would entail shuyu' (common ownership) in the pawn, which is impermissible in a pawn contract (since a pawn cannot be co-owned). The core problem is that both claims cannot be upheld simultaneously because each requires exclusive possession. The author explains that when it becomes impossible to act on both evidences, they are dropped (tasaqut), and the judge should not rule in favor of either. Then the text considers an alternative: could the slave be considered pawn to both as if they took it together at the same time? The answer is no, because each claimant's evidence proves a right to the whole slave, and a judgment giving only half would contradict the evidence. This is the position of qiyas (analogy). However, Imam Muhammad in his al-Mabsut (Book of Testimonies) mentions that istihsan (juristic preference) would allow giving half to each, but then he himself abandons istihsan in this case and adopts the qiyas position because here qiyas is stronger. This is one of the exceptional seven cases where qiyas is preferred over istihsan. The commentary clarifies that generally istihsan is given precedence, but this case is an exception.

Key Terms
رہن (rahn): A contract where a valuable item (here a slave) is given as security for a debt, held by the creditor until repayment.
شیوع (shuyu'): Shared ownership of the pawn; considered invalid in a pawn contract because a pawn must be fully possessed by the creditor to secure the full debt.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference; deviating from an established analogy (qiyas) for a stronger reason, usually based on ease, necessity, or a specific text.
قیاس (qiyas): Analogical reasoning; deriving a ruling for a new case based on an existing ruling due to a shared effective cause ('illah).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why did Imam Muhammad adopt qiyas (batil) over istihsan (division) in the case of two creditors claiming the same pawn with unknown dates?
A) Because istihsan is not a valid proof in the Hanafi school.
B) Because dividing would create shuyu', and each claimant's evidence proves exclusive right to the whole, so a half-ruling contradicts the evidence.
C) Because the pawnor was not present to confirm either claim.
D) Because the slave was already dead.

Key Takeaway
When two pawn claims conflict with unknown dates, the pawn is invalid (batil) because dividing would create shuyu' and contradict the evidence – this is one of the seven exceptional cases where qiyas overrides istihsan.

Invalid Pawn: Perishing as a Trust
Ruling that an invalid pawn perishes as a trust

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the maxim 'al-batil la hukma lahu' to determine that an invalid pawn's destruction while with the pawnor incurs no liability.

Core Idea
An invalid pawn gives no legal effect; its destruction is a trust – no guarantee.

This lesson examines a concise ruling: what if a pawned item is destroyed after the pawn contract is ruled invalid? The Hanafi school applies the fundamental maxim 'al-batil la hukma lahu' – the invalid has no ruling. This means the void contract produces no legal consequences, so the destruction is treated as a trust (amanah), and the possessor bears no liability. We will unpack the reasoning and its practical implication.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The slave (pawned item) is in the possession of the pawnor (rahn), and the pawn contract is batil (invalid). Determine the legal status of the destruction.
The destruction occurs while the pawnor holds the item.
2
Grasp the ruling
The author states it perishes as a trust (amanah) – no guarantee (daman) is owed. This is the core ruling.
3
Understand the rationale
Because the contract is batil, it has no legal effect (al-batil la hukma lahu). The item is not considered a pawn, so pawn-related liability does not apply.
This maxim is central in Hanafi fiqh.
4
Apply to similar cases
The commentary extends the same ruling to the case where two claimants have possession and precedence cannot be determined. The same reasoning applies.
Consistency of the maxim.
5
Draw practical consequence
The pawnor is not liable for the value of the destroyed item because the invalid contract produced no legal obligations.
This protects the possessor from unfair liability.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
غلام راہن کے قبضہ میں تو کیا حکم ہے واذا وقع باطلا فلو هلک هلک أمانة لان الباطل لا حكم له ترجمہ اور جبکہ رہن باطل واقع ہوا پس اگر وہ ہلاک ہو جائے تو امانت کے طور پر ہلاک ہو گا اس لئے کہ باطل کے لئے کوئی حکم نہیں ہے۔ تشریح ہم ماقبل میں بتا چکے ہیں کہ اسمسئلہ کی مخلف صورتیں ہیں لیکن کتاب میں مصنف مشرف اس صورت کا حکم بیان کیا ہے جس میں وہ غلام راہن کے قبضہ میں ہے اور اتفاق سے اس صورت کا بھی یہی حکم ہے جس میں وہ غلام دونوں مدعی کے پاس ہوا اور تقدم و تاخر کا نہ ہو سکے تو اب صورت کا ایک حکم بیان کرتے ہیں کہ اگر اس صورت میں وہ غلام ان کے پاس ہلاک ہو جائے تو چونکہ اس کو رہن شمار نہیں کیا تھا لہذا اس پر رہن کے احکام بھی جاری نہ ہوں گے اور ان پر منمان واجب نہ ہوگا۔
What is the ruling when the slave is in the pawnor's possession? And when it (the pawn) becomes invalid, then if it perishes, it perishes as a trust (amanah), because the invalid has no ruling. Translation: And when the pawn becomes invalid, then if it perishes, it perishes as a trust, because the invalid has no ruling. Explanation: We have already mentioned in the preceding that this issue has different forms, but in the book the author has stated the ruling of this form in which the slave is in the pawnor's possession, and incidentally this same ruling applies to the form in which the slave came into the possession of both claimants and the precedence and delay could not be determined. Now we state one ruling of the form: if in this form the slave perishes while with them, then because it was not considered a pawn, therefore the rulings of pawn will not apply to it, and they will not be liable for a guarantee (damn).
Source pages p. 257

Commentary
This brief passage clarifies the consequence of an invalid pawn contract. The author states that if the pawn contract is batil (invalid) and the pawned item (here the slave) is destroyed while in the possession of the pawnor (rahn), then the destruction is treated as an amanah (trust). This means the pawnor does not incur any liability (daman) because the pawn contract had no legal effect due to its invalidity. The commentary explains that this same ruling applies to the earlier scenario where the slave was in the possession of the two claimants: since the pawn was not validly established, if the slave perishes, no one is liable. The reason given is that 'the invalid has no ruling' (al-batil la hukma lahu), a fundamental legal maxim in Hanafi fiqh. Thus, the pawnor is not held responsible for the value of the slave.

Key Terms
امانت (amanah): A trust; an item in one's possession without liability for loss unless due to negligence. Here, the destroyed pawn is treated as a trust, so no guarantee is owed.
باطل (batil): Invalid; a contract that is void from its inception, producing no legal effects.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a pawn contract is batil and the pawn is destroyed while in the pawnor's possession, how is the destruction treated?
A) As a guarantee (daman) – the pawnor must compensate.
B) As a trust (amanah) – no liability.
C) As a pawn (rahn) – the pawnor must return the value.
D) As a gift (hibah) – the pawnor owes the debt.

Key Takeaway
An invalid pawn contract has no legal effect; its destruction is a trust, not a guarantee.

The Dispute on Pawn Validity After the Pawnor's Death: Istihsan vs Qiyas
Intra-Hanafi dispute on istihsan vs qiyas after pawnor's death.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to differentiate between the positions of Abu Hanifa/Muhammad and Abu Yusuf on the validity of a pawn after the pawnor's death when two creditors claim the same pawn, and explain the reasoning based on istihsan and qiyas.

Core Idea
After the pawnor's death, istihsan allows each creditor half the pawn; qiyas rejects it due to shared possession (shuyu').

In the previous lesson, we considered a case where the pawnor was alive. Here, the pawnor dies, and two creditors each claim the same slave as a pawn with conflicting evidence. The Hanafi school is divided: Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad apply istihsan to permit each creditor to hold half as a valid pawn, while Imam Abu Yusuf insists on qiyas, rejecting it due to the inherent problem of common ownership (shuyu') in a pawn contract. This lesson unpacks the reasoning—known as talil—behind each position and its practical consequence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the factual scenario
The pawnor dies leaving a slave that is physically in the hands of two creditors. Each creditor claims the slave as a pawn for their debt, but the timing of the pawn is unknown and conflicting. The judge must decide on the validity of the pawn and the creditors' rights.
The scenario involves conflicting evidence of equal strength, leading to a judicial dilemma.
2
State the two positions
Abu Hanifa and Muhammad hold that by istihsan, each creditor is entitled to half of the slave as a valid pawn, which they can sell to recover their debt. Abu Yusuf holds that by qiyas, the pawn is invalid (batil) and thus no sale is possible.
These are both Hanafi positions; the disagreement is internal to the school.
3
Analyze the reasoning (talil) of each
Istihsan reasoning: The pawnor's death removes the possibility of his objection, so the creditors can benefit from the pawn to recover their rights. Qiyas reasoning: The right to hold (habs) is a primary ruling of the pawn contract; a judgment of half-pawn effectively affirms a valid contract, but the contract is void from the start due to shuyu' (common ownership), just as it would be invalid during the pawnor's lifetime.
Abu Yusuf sees shuyu' as a fatal defect regardless of the pawnor's death.
4
Identify the key point of disagreement
The disagreement centers on whether the pawnor's death changes the shuyu' problem. Abu Yusuf says no: shuyu' is an inherent defect in the contract itself, independent of the pawnor's presence. Abu Hanifa and Muhammad say yes: the practical obstacle of the pawnor's objection is gone, so istihsan allows a half-pawn to serve the purpose of debt recovery.
This is a classic case of istihsan overriding a strict qiyas.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and the mufta bihi
Practical consequence: Under the istihsan view, each creditor can sell the half-slave and recover part of their debt. Under the qiyas view, no sale is possible, and creditors must seek alternative legal remedies. The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is the istihsan view of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, as recorded in al-Jami' al-Saghir and adopted in later fatwa.
The mufta bihi facilitates recovery after the pawnor's death, aligning with the purpose of the pawn contract.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
را ہن فوت ہو جائے اور غلام دونوں کے قبضہ میں ہو تو قاضی کس کے حق میں فیصلہ دیگا قال ولو مات الراهن و العبد في أيديهما فأقام كل واحد منهما البيئة على ما وصفنا كان في يدكل واحد منهما نصفه رهنا يبيعه بحقه استحسانا وهو قول أبي حنيفة ومحمد وفي القياس هذا باطل وهو قول ابي يوسف لان الحبس للاستيفاء حكم اصلى لعقد الرهن فيكون القضاء به قضاء بعقد الرهن وانه باطل للشيوع كمافي حالة الحيوة ترجمہ ام محمد نے جامع صغیر میں فرمایا اور اگر راہن مر جائے اور غلام ان دونوں ( مدعی ) کے ہاتھوں میں ہو پس ان دونوں میں سے ہر ایک نے مذکورہ طریقہ کے مطابق بینہ قائم کر دیا تو غلام کا نصف ان دونوں میں سے ہر ایک کے قبضہ میں ہو گا بطور رہن کے جبس کو وہ اپنے حق میں بیچ سکتا ہے یہ حکم استحسانا ہے۔ اور یہی ابو حنیفہ اور محمد کا قول ہے اور قیاس میں یہ باطل ہے اور یہی ابو یوسف کا قول ہے اس لئے کہ جس کا وصولیابی کے لئے ہونا ہی عقد رہن کا حکم اصلی ہے تو استیفاء کے لئے جس کا فیصلہ مقدر ہن کا فیصلہ ہوگا اور عقد رہن کا فیصلہ شیوع کی وجہ سے باطل ہے جیسا کہ راہن کی زندگی کی حالت میں۔ تشریح پہلی صورت میں حکم مذکور جب تھا کہ راہن زندہ ہو۔ اور اگر راہن مر جائے اور غلام ان دونوں کے قبضہ میں ہو تو قاضی یہ فیصلہ کر دیا کہ غلام ان دونوں کے لئے آدھا آدھا رہن ہوگا جس کو وہ اپنے حق میں فروخت کر سکتے ہیں مگر طرفین کا قول ہے۔ اور امام ابو یوسف کا قول اب بھی وہی ہے یعنی فیصلہ نہ ہوگا۔ خلاصہ کلام پہلے مسئلہ میں بالاتفاق قیاس پر عمل کیا گیا ہے اور اس مسئلہ میں طرفین نے استحسان پر اور امام ابو یوسف نے قیاس پر عمل کیا ہے امام ابو یوسف کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ جیسے پہلی صورت میں اس شکل میں شیوع لازم آ رہا تھا وہ اب بھی لازم آ رہا ہے جو راہن کی حیات وممانعت سے متفرق نہیں ہوگا کیونکہ رہن کا مقصد تو بہر صورت یہ ہے استیفا حق کے لئے مرہون مرتہن کے پاس محبوس رہے۔
If the pawnor dies and the slave is in the hands of both, then in favor of whom will the judge decide? He said: And if the pawnor dies and the slave is in their hands, then each of them establishes the evidence as we described, then in the hand of each of them will be half of it as a pawn; he can sell it for his right, by istihsan. And this is the saying of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. And in qiyas, this is invalid, and this is the saying of Abu Yusuf because the habs for recovery is the primary ruling of the pawn contract, so the judgment for it is a judgment for the pawn contract, and it is invalid due to shuyu' as in the case during the life of the pawnor. Translation: Imam Muhammad said in al-Jami' al-Saghir: And if the pawnor dies and the slave is in the hands of both claimants, then each of them establishes the evidence in the manner described, then half of the slave will be in the possession of each of them as a pawn; he can sell it for his right, this is by istihsan. And this is the saying of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. And in qiyas, this is invalid, and this is the saying of Abu Yusuf because the habs for recovery is the primary ruling of the pawn contract, so the judgment for it is a judgment for the pawn contract, and it is invalid due to shuyu', as in the case during the life of the pawnor. Explanation: In the first case, the mentioned ruling was when the pawnor was alive. And if the pawnor dies and the slave is in the possession of both, then the judge may decide that the slave will be half-half pawn for both, which they can sell for their right; this is the saying of the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad). And Imam Abu Yusuf's saying remains the same, i.e., no judgment will be given. Summary: In the first issue, qiyas was acted upon by consensus, and in this issue, the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) acted on istihsan, and Imam Abu Yusuf acted on qiyas. Imam Abu Yusuf's proof is that just as in the first case, shuyu' was necessary in that form, it is also necessary here, which will not be separated by the life or prohibition of the pawnor, because the purpose of pawn is in any case that the pawn remains detained with the pawnee for recovery of the right.
Source pages p. 257

Commentary
This passage presents the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the validity of a pawn when the pawnor dies and two creditors each claim the same slave as pawn with conflicting evidence of unknown date. The text quotes Imam Muhammad from al-Jami' al-Saghir: if the pawnor dies and the slave is in the hands of both claimants, each produces evidence as before, then the judge rules by istihsan that each gets half of the slave as a pawn and can sell it to recover his debt. This is the position of Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad. In contrast, Abu Yusuf holds by qiyas that this is invalid (batil) because the right to hold (habs) for recovery is a primary ruling of the pawn contract; so a judgment of half-pawn is effectively a judgment of the pawn contract itself, but such a contract is invalid due to shuyu' (common ownership), just as it was invalid during the pawnor's lifetime. The commentary explains that the key difference between this case and the earlier case (when the pawnor was alive) is that here the pawnor's death removes the possibility of the pawnor objecting (since he is dead), so istihsan allows the division to facilitate the creditors' recovery. The summary clarifies that in the first scenario (pawnor alive), all agreed on qiyas (batil), but here Abu Hanifa and Muhammad adopt istihsan, while Abu Yusuf remains consistent with qiyas. Abu Yusuf's argument is that shuyu' arises regardless of the pawnor's death, so the ruling should remain the same.

Key Terms
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference; here, allowing half-pawn for each creditor after the pawnor's death to facilitate recovery, overriding the normal qiyas that would deem it invalid.
حبس (habs): The right to hold the pawn; the primary purpose of a pawn contract is to secure detention of the pawn until the debt is paid.
شیوع (shuyu'): Common ownership or shared possession; invalid in pawn because the creditor's right to hold must be exclusive to secure the full debt.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Abu Hanifa and Muhammad say the pawn is invalid; Abu Yusuf says it is valid.
B) Abu Hanifa and Muhammad say each gets half as a valid pawn by istihsan; Abu Yusuf says it is invalid due to shuyu'.
C) All three imams agree that the pawn is invalid.
D) Abu Hanifa and Muhammad say the pawnor's heirs should return the slave.

Key Takeaway
In the intra-Hanafi dispute, the istihsan view of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad that each creditor gets half the pawn after the pawnor's death is the operative ruling, overriding Abu Yusuf's qiyas.

Istihsan Argument for Mortgage Validity with Joint Creditors After Death
Explains why a shared mortgage is valid after death but not during life using istihsan.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a mortgage with multiple creditors and explain the istihsan reasoning based on the change in legal purpose after death.

Core Idea
A mortgage with joint creditors is invalid during life but valid after death because the contract's purpose changes from indivisible retention to divisible sale.

This passage from the sharh of Al-Hidayah explains a nuanced ruling in mortgage (rahn) law. The Hanafi school holds that if multiple creditors (shuyu') jointly hold a pledge, the mortgage is invalid during the pledgor's life but becomes valid after death. The reasoning uses istihsan (juristic preference), drawing an analogy from marriage law. We will unpack this reasoning step by step.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two legal contexts
The passage distinguishes between the pledgor's life and after death. In each context, the legal effect (hukm) of the mortgage differs: during life it is retention (habs), after death it is sale and recovery of debt.
This distinction is key to understanding the ruling.
2
Analyze how shuyu' affects each purpose
Joint ownership (shuyu') harms retention because retention requires exclusive possession. But it does not harm sale because sale can be divided among creditors.
The harm element determines validity.
3
Examine the analogical precedent
The author cites the case of two men claiming marriage to a woman: during life, evidence is rejected because marriage cannot be shared; after death, inheritance is divided. This shows a parallel shift in ruling based on change in purpose.
4
Formulate the istihsan argument
Istihsan is used to prefer the adjusted ruling over the apparent analogy (qiyas jaliy) that would treat both contexts the same. The stronger consideration is the change in the contract's objective.
Istihsan here is not arbitrary but grounded in sound analogy.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وجه الاستحسان ان العقد لا يراد كذاته وانما يراد لحكمه وحكمه فى حالة الحيوة الحبس والشيوع يضره وبعد الممات الاستيفاء بالبيع في الدين والشيوع لا يضره وصار كما اذا ادعى الرجلان نكاح امراة او ادعت اختان النكاح على رجل واقاموا البينة لها ترت فى حالة الحيوة ويقضى بالميراث بينهم بعد الممات لانه يقبل الانقسام والله اعلم
The face of istihsan is that the contract is not intended for its own sake but rather for its legal effect. And its legal effect during life is retention (habs), and joint ownership (shuyu') harms that. After death, its legal effect is recovery by sale for the debt, and joint ownership does not harm that. And it becomes like the case where two men claim marriage to a woman, or two sisters claim marriage to a man, and they produce evidence: the evidence is rejected during life, but after death inheritance is adjudicated between them because it accepts division. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 258

Commentary
This passage from the sharh explains the Hanafi ruling on the validity of a mortgage (rahn) involving multiple creditors (shuyu'). The passage type is a ruling with a proof based on istihsan (juristic preference). The author first distinguishes between the purpose of the contract in the pledgor's life and after death. During life, the purpose of a mortgage is for the mortgagee to retain possession of the pledged item as security. If the item is jointly owned (e.g., two creditors hold a pledge together), this joint possession (shuyu') is harmful because neither can have exclusive retention, so the mortgage is invalid. After the pledgor's death, the purpose shifts to selling the item to recover the debt. Joint ownership does not harm sale and division, so the mortgage becomes valid. The author supports this by an analogy from marriage law: if two men claim marriage to the same woman, their claims are rejected during her life because marriage cannot be shared. But after her death, their claims are accepted for inheritance, which can be divided. Similarly, a joint pledge is invalid during life but valid after death. This reasoning is based on istihsan (preferring a different ruling due to a change in circumstances).

Key Terms
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference; preferring a different ruling from the apparent analogy due to a stronger consideration of public interest or change of circumstances.
شيوع (shuyu'): Joint ownership or indivisibility; here it refers to multiple creditors sharing a single pledged item.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is a mortgage with multiple creditors (shuyu') valid after the pledgor's death but not during his life?
A) Because the purpose during life is retention (habs) which cannot be shared, but after death the purpose is sale and distribution, which accepts division.
B) Because the mortgagee's consent is not required after death.
C) Because the pledgor's heirs can agree to it.
D) Because the mortgage becomes a debt that must be paid.

Key Takeaway
The validity of a mortgage with joint creditors depends on the contract's purpose: it is invalid during life due to indivisible retention, but valid after death when the purpose shifts to divisible sale.

Placing a Pledge with a Trustworthy Custodian: Hanafi Validity
States the ruling and proof for placing a pledge with an impartial custodian, rebutting Imam Malik's objection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on placing a pledge with a trustworthy custodian and evaluate the Maliki counter-argument.

Core Idea
The custodian’s hand is dual: preservation for the owner, guarantee for the mortgagee.

This lesson examines a key dispute between the Hanafi school and Imam Malik regarding the validity of placing a pledged item with a neutral third party. The Hanafi school holds that such an arrangement is valid because the custodian’s possession serves two distinct legal functions. Imam Malik, however, objects on the grounds that the custodian’s hand is solely that of the owner. Understanding this dispute clarifies the Hanafi concept of possession (qabd) and its role in pledge contracts.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi Position
Identify the ruling: placing a pledge with a trustworthy person is permissible (jaez) when both parties agree.
2
Identify the Opponent and Their View
Imam Malik holds it is invalid. Understand his reasoning: the custodian’s hand is the owner’s, so the mortgagee lacks possession.
3
Follow the Opponent’s Proof
Malik’s evidence: in case of a third-party claim (istihqaq), the custodian returns the item to the owner, not the mortgagee, proving the hand belongs to the owner.
4
Analyze the Hanafi Response
The Hanafi rebuttal distinguishes physical preservation (hifz) from financial guarantee (daman). The custodian’s hand is the owner’s for preservation but the mortgagee’s for guarantee.
The analogy of a depository (wadi‘) is used: the custodian is a deputy of the owner only in preservation.
5
Determine the Thamarah al-Khilaf
Practical consequence: Hanafis allow neutral third-party custodians in pledges; Malikis require direct possession by the mortgagee.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال واذا اتفقا على وضع الرهن على يد العدل جاز قال مالك لا يجوز ذكر قوله في بعض النسخ لان يد العدل يد المالك ولهذا يرجع العدل عليه عند الاستحقاق فانعدم القبض ولنا ان يده على الصورة يد المالك فى الحفظ اذ العين امانة وفى حق المالية يد المرتهن لان يده يد ضمان والمضمون هو المالية فنزل منزلة الشخصين تحقيقا لما قصداه من الرهن وانما يرجع العدل على المالك في الاستحقاق لانه نائب عنه في حفظ العين كالمودع
He said: And if they both agree to place the pledge in the hand of a trustworthy person, it is permissible. Malik said: It is not permissible. His statement is mentioned in some copies. Because the hand of the trustworthy person is the hand of the owner, and therefore the trustworthy person returns to him (the owner) at the time of recovery (istihqaq), so the possession (qabd) is absent. And our proof is that his (the custodian's) hand is, in form (surah), the hand of the owner in terms of preservation, because the object is a trust (amanah), but in terms of financial value (maliyah), it is the hand of the mortgagee (murtahin) because his hand is a hand of guarantee (daman), and the guaranteed thing is the financial value. So he is treated as having the status of two persons, to achieve what they intended from the pledge. And the trustworthy person only returns to the owner in case of recovery because he is the owner's deputy in preserving the object, like a depository (al-mudi').
Source pages p. 259

Commentary
This passage from the sharh of Al-Hidayah addresses the validity of placing a pledged item with a trusted third party (al-'adl). The passage type is an inter-madhhab dispute, specifically between the Hanafi school and Imam Malik. The matn states: If the pledgor and mortgagee agree to place the pledge with a trustworthy person, it is valid (jaez). Then it reports that Imam Malik said it is invalid, with the reasoning that the custodian's hand is essentially the owner's hand, as evidenced by the fact that if the item is later claimed by a third party (istihqaq), the custodian recovers the loss from the owner, not the mortgagee. Therefore, the mortgagee's possession is not established, invalidating the pledge. The Hanafi response (our proof) is that the custodian's hand serves a dual function: in terms of physical preservation (hifz), it is the owner's hand because the object is an amanah (trust). But in terms of financial value (maliyah) and guarantee (daman), it is the mortgagee's hand because he has the right to sell the item if the debt is unpaid. Thus, the custodian is treated as if he stands in the place of both parties, achieving the intended purpose of the pledge. The custodian's recourse to the owner in case of loss is only because he is a deputy (na'ib) in preservation, similar to a depository (wadi'), and does not negate the mortgagee's right to possession in terms of financial interest. Therefore, the Hanafi ruling is that such an arrangement is valid.

Key Terms
يد العدل (yad al-'adl): The hand/possession of the trustworthy custodian who is neutral between pledgor and mortgagee.
يد ضمان (yad daman): A 'hand of guarantee'; possession that entails liability for the value of the object (similar to a buyer's possession).
استحقاق (istihqaq): Recovery of property by a rightful owner from a possessor; here it refers to a third party proving ownership and claiming the pledged item.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is a pledge placed with a trustworthy person (al-'adl) valid despite the mortgagee not having direct possession?
A) Because the custodian's hand is solely that of the owner, but the owner delegates the right of sale.
B) Because the custodian's hand serves dual roles: preservation for the owner and financial guarantee for the mortgagee.
C) Because the custodian is considered an agent of both parties with equal power.
D) Because the mortgagee can still take possession at any time.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, a pledge is valid when placed with a neutral custodian because the custodian's possession serves a dual function: preserving the owner's property and securing the mortgagee's financial right.

The Validity of Pledge with a Third-Party Trustee ('Adl) – Hanafi vs Maliki
Hanafi response to Maliki objection about 'adl's possession

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi argument for the validity of a pledge held by an 'adl and refute the Maliki objection by applying the distinction between essence and value.

Core Idea
The pledge is valid because the 'adl's possession represents the pledgee's claim on value, not the physical essence.

This lesson examines a classic inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafi and Maliki schools regarding the validity of a pledge (rahn) when the pledged property is held by a third-party trustee ('adl). The Maliki school requires the pledgee to take direct physical possession, while the Hanafis argue that possession of the property's value through a trustee suffices. Understanding this disagreement reveals how differences in the conception of legal possession (qabd) and the subject of pledge lead to divergent rulings.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the Hanafi ruling: the pledge is valid when the 'adl holds the property. Note that the Hanafis distinguish between the essence ('ayn) and value (maliyyah) of the pledged item.
The 'adl is considered an agent for both parties: for the pledgor (rahin) concerning the physical item, and for the pledgee (murtahin) concerning its value.
2
Identify the Maliki objection
Imam Malik's reported view is that the pledge is invalid unless the pledgee has direct physical possession. The 'adl's possession does not transfer possession to the pledgee.
This objection is based on the apparent meaning of the hadith 'La rahn illa bi-qabd' (No pledge without taking possession).
3
Follow the Hanafi proof (dalil aqli)
The Hanafi proof uses rational analogy (qiyas) to a deposit (wadi'ah). In the deposit example, if a depositary pays compensation to a claimant, he can recover from the depositor. Similarly, the 'adl's possession suffices for the pledgee's right to value, and the pledge is valid. The subject of pledge is value, not the physical essence.
This is an argument based on the purpose (maqsad) of the pledge: securing the debt, which relates to value, not physical custody.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response to the Maliki objection
The Hanafi response argues that the 'adl's possession is equivalent to the pledgee's for the purpose of establishing the pledge because the pledge's subject is value. Also, Imam Malik's own view that the pledge is binding at the contract (luzum bi-mujarrad al-'aqd) contradicts his objection.
The tanbih (caution) in the text notes a possible inconsistency in Imam Malik's position, suggesting two narrations.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
In a Hanafi court, a pledge deposited with an 'adl is valid; in a Maliki court, it would be invalid unless the pledgee takes direct possession. This affects how secured transactions are structured in different jurisdictions.
The Hanafi position is mufta bihi and is relied upon in Hanafi fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اس قول کی دلیل ہوئی جو امام مالک کی جانب منسوب کیا گیا ہے۔
ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ جس طرح امام متقدین اور خدا دونوں کا نائب ہے اور یہ اس لئے ضروری ہے تا کہ رہن کا مقصد پورا ہو جائے تو جب عادل دونوں کا نائب ہوا تو یوں کہا جائیگا کہ مرہون میں دو چیزیں ہیں ایک اسکی ذات اور دوسری اس کی مالیت تو عادل ذات و صورت میں تو راہن کا نائب ہے اور مالیت میں مرتہن کا نائب ہے اور مضمون مالیت ہوا کرتی ہے نہ کہ صورت و عین ۔ خلاصہ کلام جب عادل کے واسطہ سے مرہون پر اس کی مالیت میں مرتین کا قبضہ ثابت ہو گیا تو رہن درست ہو گیا اور امام مالک کا اعتراض غلط ثابت ہوا۔ سوال : تو پھر عادل صورت مذکورہ میں تاوان رہن سے کب وصول کرتا ہے۔ جواب: اس لئے کہ عادل مین کی حفاظت میں راہن کا نائب ہے۔ اور یہ بالکل ایسا ہے کہ زید نے خالد کے پاس اپنی ودیعت رکھ دی تو خالد مودع ہے خالد کے پاس یہ ودیعت ہلاک ہوگئی پھر بکر نے اس ودیعت میں اپنا استحقاق ثابت کر کے خالد سے تاوان لیا تو خالد اس تاوان کو زید سے وصول کر یگا ایسے ہی اس صورت میں ہوا ہے۔ تنبیہ - مصنف نے اول کتاب الرہن میں فرمایا ہے کہ امام مالک کے نزدیک نفس عقد سے رہن لازم ہو جاتا ہے تو پھر ان کا قول مذکورہ درست نہیں رہتا کہ مرتہن کا قبضہ معدوم ہے ممکن ہے کہ مالک سے اس میں دو روایتیں ہوں۔
تنبية ... ذكر قوله في بعض النسخ ... الخ اس سے مصنف کی مراد یہ بھی ہو سکتی ہے کہ مختصر القدوری کے بعض نسخوں میں امام مالک کا یہ قول مذکور ہے اور بعض میں نہیں ہے۔ اور یہ بھی ہوسکتا ہے کہ سلف کی بعض کتابوں میں امام مالک کا یہ قول مذکور ہے۔ اور بعض میں امام مالک کے بجائے یہاں ابن ابی لیلی مذکور ہیں۔ مبسوط اور شرح الاقطع میں ابن ابی لیلی ہے۔ مجمع الانہر میں زفر اور ابن ابی لیلیٰ کا یہی قول مذکور ہے۔
This became the proof of that statement which is attributed to Imam Malik. Our proof is that just as the 'adl is the deputy of both the early imam and the Lord, and this is necessary so that the purpose of the pledge is fulfilled. So when the 'adl became the deputy of both, it will be said that in the pledged property there are two things: its essence and its value. Thus the 'adl in essence and form is the deputy of the rahin, and in value is the deputy of the murtahin. And the subject matter is value, not form and essence. In summary, when through the 'adl, possession of the murtahin is established over the pledged property in terms of its value, the pledge becomes valid, and Imam Malik's objection is proved false. Question: Then when does the 'adl recover the compensation from the pledge in the mentioned case? Answer: Because the 'adl in protecting the essence is the deputy of the rahin. And this is exactly like Zaid placed his deposit with Khalid, so Khalid is the depositary. This deposit was destroyed with Khalid. Then Bakr proved his entitlement in this deposit and took compensation from Khalid, so Khalid will recover that compensation from Zaid. Similarly, it happened in this case. Caution: The author said at the beginning of Kitab al-Rahn that according to Imam Malik, the pledge becomes binding from the contract itself. Then his mentioned statement that the murtahin's possession is non-existent is not correct; it is possible that there are two narrations from Malik. Notification: 'Mentioned his statement in some copies...' etc. From this, the author's intent may be that in some copies of Mukhtasar al-Quduri, this statement of Imam Malik is mentioned, and in some it is not. And it is also possible that in some books of the predecessors, this statement of Imam Malik is mentioned, and in some, instead of Imam Malik, Ibn Abi Layla is mentioned here. In al-Mabsut and Sharh al-Aqta', it is Ibn Abi Layla. In Majma' al-Anhur, this same statement of Zufar and Ibn Abi Layla is mentioned.
Source pages p. 260

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafi school and Imam Malik regarding the validity of a pledge (rahn) when the pledged item is placed with a third-party trustee ('adl). The Maliki position, as reported here, holds that without physical possession by the pledgee (murtahin), the pledge is invalid. The Hanafi response, which is the mufta bihi position in the school, argues that the 'adl acts as a representative for both parties: regarding the physical essence ('ayn), the 'adl is the agent of the pledgor (rahin), and regarding the value (maliyyah), the 'adl is the agent of the pledgee. Since the subject of the pledge is value, not the physical item per se (a key Hanafi distinction), the pledgee's constructive possession through the 'adl is sufficient. The Hanafi proof uses qiyas (analogy) to a deposit (wadi'ah): if a depositary holds an item and a third party proves a claim, the depositary becomes liable for compensation, which he can then recover from the original depositor. Similarly, if the 'adl's possession is equivalent to the pledgee's for value, the pledge is valid. The tanbih (caution) notes a potential contradiction in Imam Malik's own view, suggesting two narrations. The additional tanbiyah notes textual variations in the source manuscripts. This passage illustrates the Hanafi reliance on rational analogy (istihsan) and the nuanced understanding of possession (qabd) in pledges.

Key Terms
عادل ('adl): A trustworthy third-party trustee appointed to hold the pledged property.
مرہون (marhun): The pledged property or asset.
قبض (qabd): Possession; taking control of the pledged property.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Because the 'adl is the owner of the property.
B) Because the 'adl's possession represents the pledgee's interest in the value of the property.
C) Because the pledgee has given explicit permission.
D) Because the pledgor also has possession through the 'adl.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, possession of the pledged property can be constructive through a trustee ('adl), as the pledge concerns value, not the physical item itself.

Neither Party May Take the Pledge from the 'Adl
Ruling statement with ta'lil

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling that neither the rahin nor the murtahin may remove the pledged property from the 'adl, and explain the legal reasoning (ta'lil) based on mutual rights.

Core Idea
Neither party can take the pledge from the trustee because doing so invalidates the other's right.

In a pledge contract (rahn), the pledged property is often placed with a neutral trustee (al-'adl). This passage from al-Quduri establishes a key rule: neither the pledgor nor the pledgee has the right to take the property from the trustee. Why? Because each has a distinct right attached to it—the pledgor's right to preservation, the pledgee's right to recover value. Understanding this interplay of rights is essential to maintaining the balance of the contract.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being ruled upon? Taking the pledged property from the 'adl. What is the hukm? It is prohibited (haram) for both the rahin and the murtahin.
2
Locate the ta'lil (legal reason)
The reason given is that each party has a right attached to the pledged property which would be nullified if the other unilaterally takes it.
The rights are: rahin's right to preservation (tied to his ownership), murtahin's right to recover his debt from its value.
3
Analyse the two rights
The rahin's right is in the specific property (preservation, trust), while the murtahin's right is in the value (security for the debt). Both coexist through the 'adl's possession.
4
Determine the consequence of loss
If the pledged property perishes with the 'adl, it is considered under the murtahin's guarantee, and the debt is discharged. This is because the 'adl's possession for value is equivalent to the murtahin's possession.
The loss falls on the murtahin, not the rahin.
5
Understand the practical implication
The 'adl's role neutralizes the conflict: neither party can unilaterally disrupt the arrangement. Any change requires mutual consent.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
راہن اور مرتہن میں سے کسی کو دوسرے کا حق باطل کرنے کی اجازت نہیں
قال وليس للمرتهن ولا للراهن أن يأخذه منه لتعلق حق الراهن فى الحفظ بيده وامانته وتعلق حق المرتهن به استيفاء فلا يملك احدهما ابطال حق الآخر فلو هلک فی یده هلک فی ضمان المرتهن لان يده في حق المالية المرتهن وهى المضمونة
ترجمہ ... قدوری نے فرمایا اور مرتہن اور راہن کو یہ حق نہیں کہ مرہون کو عادل سے لے لے عادل کے قبضہ اور اس کی امانت کی وجہ سے حفاظت کے سلسلہ میں راہن کا متعلق ہونے کی وجہ سے اور حق مرتہن کے متعلق ہونے کی وجہ سے مرہون کے ساتھ استیفاء کے اعتبار سے تو ان میں سے کوئی ایک دوسرے کا حق باطل کرنے کا مالک نہ ہوگا پس اگر مرہون عادل کے قبضہ میں ہلاک ہو جائے تو مرتبہن بنی کا قبضہ ہے اور مالیت ہی مضمون ہوتی ہے۔ تشریح وہ مرہون جو عادل کے پاس رکھا گیا ہے چونکہ اس میں راہن اور مرتبہن دونوں کا حق ہے اول کا باعتبار معین اور ثانی کا باعتبار مالیت لہذا عاقدین میں سے کسی کو یہ حق نہ ہوگا کہ دوسرے کا حق باطل کر دے۔ لہذا ان میں سے کسی کو یہ حق بھی نہ ہوگا کہ مرہون کو عادل سے لے لے۔ پھر اگر یہ مرہون عادل کے پاس بلاک ہو جائے تو مرتہن کی ضمانت میں بلاک ہو گا اور حسب تفصیل سابق قرض ساقط ہوگا کیونکہ مرہون پر اعتبار مالیت عادل کا قبضہ مرتہن کے قبضہ کے قائم مقام ہے اور مالیت ہی مضمون ہوا کرتی ہے۔
Neither the rahin nor the murtahin is permitted to take it from him. He (al-Quduri) said: And neither the murtahin nor the rahin has the right to take it from him because the right of the rahin is attached to his hand and trusteeship for preservation, and the right of the murtahin is attached to it for recovery. So neither of them can invalidate the right of the other. If it perishes in his hand, it perishes in the guarantee of the murtahin, because his hand in regard to the right of value is the murtahin's hand, and value is what is guaranteed. Translation: Al-Quduri said: The murtahin and the rahin do not have the right to take the pledged property from the 'adl, due to the attachment of the rahin's right concerning preservation with his hand and trusteeship, and the attachment of the murtahin's right concerning recovery with the pledged property. So neither of them can nullify the other's right. Thus if the pledged property perishes in the 'adl's possession, it perishes in the guarantee of the murtahin, because his hand in respect of value is the murtahin's hand, and value is what is guaranteed. Explanation: The pledged property placed with the 'adl, since both the rahin and murtahin have a right in it—the former in terms of the specific property, the latter in terms of value—therefore neither party has the right to nullify the other's right. Hence neither of them has the right to take the pledged property from the 'adl. Then if the pledged property perishes with the 'adl, it perishes in the murtahin's guarantee, and as per previous detail, the debt is discharged because regarding value, the 'adl's possession stands in place of the murtahin's possession, and it is value that is guaranteed.
Source pages p. 260

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from al-Quduri's matn, followed by its translation and commentary (sharh). The ruling is that neither the pledgor (rahin) nor the pledgee (murtahin) is allowed to take the pledged property from the trustee ('adl). The reason (ta'lil) is that both parties have rights in the pledged property: the rahin has a right to its preservation (since it is his property), and the murtahin has a right to recover his debt from its value. These rights are attached to the 'adl's possession. If either party takes the property, they would be invalidating the other's right, which is not permitted. The consequence of the pledged property being destroyed in the 'adl's hand is that it is considered under the murtahin's guarantee, meaning the murtahin loses his claim, and the debt is discharged (as per prior discussion). This is because the 'adl's possession for value is equivalent to the murtahin's possession, and value is the subject of guarantee. The commentary emphasizes that the interplay of rights prevents unilateral action. This lesson clarifies the mutual constraints in a pledge arrangement.

Key Terms
راہن (rahin): The pledgor, the person who gives the pledge as security for a debt.
مرتہن (murtahin): The pledgee, the person who receives the pledge as security.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is neither the rahin nor the murtahin allowed to take the pledged property from the 'adl?
A) Because the 'adl is the owner during the pledge period.
B) Because each party has a right in the pledged property that prevents the other from nullifying it.
C) Because taking it would void the contract entirely.
D) Because the 'adl must hold it until a court decides.

Key Takeaway
Neither party can unilaterally remove the pledge from the trustee because each has a protected right that the other may not nullify.

Liability of the 'Adl for Delivery of the Pledge
Ruling with proof by analogy

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling that the 'adl becomes liable upon delivering the pledge to either party, and explain the rationale using the analogy of a depositary (mudi').

Core Idea
Delivering the pledge to either party is ta'addi—each party is a stranger to the other's right.

The 'adl is a neutral trustee holding the pledged property for both the rahin and the murtahin. Normally, a trustee is not liable for accidental loss. However, if he commits ta'addi (breach of trust), he becomes liable. This lesson examines the specific case where the 'adl hands the pledge to one of the parties, explaining why this constitutes ta'addi and triggers liability.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and the act that triggers liability
The text states: if the 'adl delivers the pledged property to either the rahin or the murtahin, he becomes liable (damin). The act is the delivery; the consequence is liability for the value if the property perishes.
The liability attaches immediately upon delivery, not only after loss.
2
Understand the dual capacity of the 'adl
The 'adl is a depositary (mudi') for the rahin regarding the physical essence ('ayn) of the property, and a trustee for the murtahin regarding the monetary value (maliyyah). This means each party has a separate right in the pledge.
The rahin owns the substance; the murtahin has a security interest in the value.
3
Recognize why each party is a 'stranger' to the other's right
From the perspective of the rahin's right in the essence, the murtahin is a stranger. From the perspective of the murtahin's right in the value, the rahin is a stranger. Therefore, delivering the pledge to either party is delivering it to a stranger with respect to the other party's right.
The term 'ajnabi' (stranger) here refers to someone who has no right in that particular aspect.
4
Apply the analogy of the depositary (mudi')
The text draws qiyas: a depositary who delivers deposited property to a stranger without consent becomes liable if the property is lost. Here, the 'adl is like a depositary for each party separately. Delivering to the rahin breaches the trust toward the murtahin, and vice versa.
The illa (effective cause) is that each party is a stranger to the other's rights, so delivery constitutes ta'addi.
5
Conclude with the ruling and its basis
Thus, the 'adl's delivery is ta'addi, removing his immunity. He is liable for the value of the property if it perishes after delivery. The ruling is based on the general principle that a trustee who commits ta'addi becomes a guarantor.
This reinforces the 'adl's duty to remain neutral and hold the property until the debt is settled.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

ولو دفع العدل الى الراهن او المرتهن ضمن لانه مودع الراهن في حق العين ومودع المرتهن في حق المالية واحدهما اجنب جنبي عن الاخر والمودع يضمن بالدفع الى الاجنبي
ترجمہ اور اگر عادل نے اہن یا مرتہن کو دیا تو عادل ضامن ہوگا اس لئے کہ عادل مین کے حق میں راہن کا مودع ہے اور مالیت کے حق میں مرتہن کا امین ہے اور ان دونوں میں سے ہر ایک ( راہن و مرتہن میں سے ) دوسرے کے حق میں اجنبی ہے اور امین اجنبی کو دینے کی وجہ سے ضامن ہوا کرتا ہے۔
تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ امین پر ہلاکت امانت کی وجہ سے ضمان نہیں مگر یہ حکم جب ہے جبکہ اس کی جانب سے کوئی تعدی نہ ہوئی ہو ورنہ ضمان واجب ہوگا اور راہن و مرتہن آپس میں ایک دوسرے کے حق میں اجنبی ہیں لہذا اگر عادل نے مرہون ان میں سے کسی کو دیدیا اور وہ اس کے پاس ہلاک ہو گیا تو عادل پر ضمان واجب ہوگا کیونکہ یہ اس کی جانب سے تعدی ہے اور یہ مختلف لحاظ سے ان دونوں کا امین ہے تو بر بناء تعدی اس پر ضمان واجب ہوگا۔
The 'adl will become liable if he hands over to the rahin or murtahin. And if the 'adl delivers to the rahin or murtahin, he becomes liable because he is a depositary (mudi') of the rahin regarding the essence, and a depositary of the murtahin regarding the value. Each of them is a stranger (ajnabi) to the other, and the depositary becomes liable by delivering to a stranger. Translation: And if the 'adl gave to the rahin or murtahin, the 'adl will be liable because the 'adl in respect of the essence is the depositary of the rahin, and in respect of value is the trustee of the murtahin. And each of them (the rahin and murtahin) is a stranger to the other. And the trustee becomes liable by giving to a stranger. Explanation: The issue is that a trustee is not liable for destruction of the trust unless there is transgression (ta'addi) from his side; otherwise liability becomes obligatory. And the rahin and murtahin are strangers to each other. Thus if the 'adl gave the pledged property to one of them and it perished in his possession, then the 'adl will be liable because this is transgression from his side. And he is a trustee for both with different considerations, so due to transgression, liability becomes obligatory on him.
Source pages p. 260

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof, using the analogy of a depositary (mudi'). The ruling is: if the 'adl (trustee) hands over the pledged property to either the pledgor (rahin) or the pledgee (murtahin), the 'adl becomes liable (damin) for its value. The reason is that the 'adl holds the pledged property in two capacities: as a depositary for the rahin regarding the physical essence ('ayn), and as a trustee for the murtahin regarding the value (maliyyah). From the perspective of each party, the other is a stranger (ajnabi). In Hanafi law, a depositary who delivers the deposited property to a stranger without the owner's consent becomes liable if the property is lost or destroyed. Here, delivering to the rahin is a breach of trust toward the murtahin, and delivering to the murtahin is a breach toward the rahin. Therefore, the 'adl's delivery constitutes transgression (ta'addi), making him liable for compensation. The commentary clarifies that normally an amin (trustee) is not liable for accidental loss, but if he commits ta'addi, liability follows. This ruling reinforces the duty of the 'adl to hold the pledge impartially.

Key Terms
تعدی (ta'addi): Transgression or breach of trust by the 'adl that removes his immunity from liability.
عدل ('adl): The neutral trustee who holds the pledged property on behalf of both the rahin and murtahin.
مودة (mudi'): Depositary; one who holds property as a trust (wadi'ah).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because the rahin is the owner and can do as he wishes.
B) Because the rahin is a stranger to the murtahin's right in the value, making the delivery a breach of trust.
C) Because the 'adl should never give the property to anyone.
D) Because the 'adl becomes the owner after delivery.

Key Takeaway
The 'adl must not deliver the pledged property to either party without the other's consent, as it is ta'addi triggering liability.

Value of Pledge Cannot Be Held as Pledge by 'Adl; Disposition by Qadi
Ruling on handling the value when 'adl becomes liable and subsequent steps

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state why the 'adl cannot unilaterally retain the value as a pledge and apply the rule for disposition of that value via mutual agreement or qadi intervention.

Core Idea
When the 'adl becomes liable for the value, he cannot hold it as pledge himself due to conflict of roles; compromise or qadi decides.

After the 'adl becomes liable for the pledge's value, what happens to that value? Can he just keep it as a new pledge? This lesson explains why he cannot, and then traces the permissible paths: either both parties agree to place it with him or another, or the qadi arranges it. A second scenario shows what happens after the debt is paid.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The 'adl delivers the pledge to one party and it is destroyed. He becomes liable for its value. The ruling: he cannot make that value a pledge in his own hand.
2
Understand the reasoning (talil)
The reason is that the 'adl would become both the giver (paying compensation) and the receiver (holding as pledge). This contradiction is not allowed.
Hanafi principle: a person cannot be both debtor and pledge-holder of the same asset.
3
State the permissible alternatives
The rahin and murtahin may agree to take the value and place it as a pledge with the same 'adl or a third party. If they cannot meet, one refers to the qadi to arrange the pledge.
Consent or judicial intervention resolves the conflict.
4
Apply to the qadi scenario
If the qadi places the value with the 'adl, then the rahin pays the debt, the value's owner depends on to whom the 'adl originally delivered the pledge.
The substitute (value) cannot coexist with the original (debt) in one ownership.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عادل نے کسی ایک کو ( راہن یا مرتہن کو رہن دیدیا اور اس نے ہلاک کر دیا تو عادل پر اس کی قیمت کا ضمان واجب ہے
واذا ضمن العدل قيمة الرهن بعد ما دفع الى احدهما وقد استهلكه المدفوع اليه او هلك في يده لا يقدر ان يجعل القيمة رهنا فى يده لأنه يصير قاضيا ومقتضيا وبينهما تناف لكن يتفقان على أن يأخذاها منه ويجعلاها رهنا عنده او عند غيره وان تعذر اجتما عهما يرفع احدهما الى القاضي ليفعل كذالك
ترجمہ اور جبکہ عادل مرہون کو ان دونوں میں سے کسی ایک کو دینے کی وجہ سے رہن کی قیمت کا ضامن ہوا اور اس مدفوع الیہ نے ہلاک کر دیا ہو یا وہ اس کے قبضہ میں ہلاک ہو گیا ہو قادر نہیں ہے عادل اس بات پر کہ قیمت کو اپنے قبضہ میں رہن کرے اس لئے کہ عادل اداء کرنے والا اور دینے والا ہو جائے گا اور ان دونوں کے درمیان منافات ہے لیکن وہ اتفاق کرلیں اس بات پر کہ قیمت کو عادل سے لے لیں اور اس کو اس کے یا اس کے غیر کے پاس رہن رکھیں اور اگر متعذر ہو جائے ان دونوں کا اجتماع تو ان میں سے قاضی کی جانب مرافعہ کرے تا کہ قاضی ایسا کر دے۔

قاضی نے عادل کے پاس قیمت رہن رکھ دی اور راہن نے مرتہن کا قرض ادا کر دیا تو قیمت کس کی ہوگی
ولو فعل ذالك ثم قضى الراهن الدين وقد ضمن العدل القيمة بالدفع الى الراهن فالقيمة سالمة له لوصول المرهون الى الراهن ووصول الدين الى المرتهن فلا يجتمع البدل والمبدل في ملك واحد وان كان ضمنها بالدفع الى المرتهن فالراهن ياخذ القيمة منه لان العين لو كانت قائمة فى يده ياخذها اذا ادى الدين
The 'adl delivered the pledge to one of them (rahin or murtahin) and he destroyed it, then the 'adl is liable for its value. And when the 'adl becomes liable for the value of the pledge after delivering to one of them, and the recipient consumed it or it perished in his hand, the 'adl cannot make the value a pledge in his own hand because he would become both payer and receiver, and there is contradiction. But they (rahin and murtahin) may agree to take the value from him and make it a pledge with him or with someone else. And if it becomes difficult for them to come together, one of them may refer to the qadi so that he does that. Translation: And when the 'adl becomes liable for the value of the pledge due to delivering it to one of them, and the recipient destroyed it or it perished in his hand, the 'adl is not able to make the value a pledge in his hand because he would become the giver and taker, and between them is contradiction. But they may agree to take it from him and make it a pledge with him or with someone else. If their meeting becomes difficult, one of them refers to the qadi to do so. Explanation: When the 'adl delivered the pledge to one of them and he destroyed it or it perished by itself, the 'adl becomes liable for its value. Now does the 'adl have the right to keep this value as a pledge with himself? It is said: No, because he would then be both the deliverer and the recipient, which is contradictory. But it is permissible if both parties agree to take the value and place it as a pledge with him or another. If there is an obstacle preventing the meeting of rahin and murtahin, one of them may request the qadi to place the pledge with someone. Then: If the qadi placed the value as a pledge with the 'adl, and the rahin paid the debt, to whom does the value belong? And if he (the qadi) did that, then the rahin paid the debt, and the 'adl had become liable for the value by delivering to the rahin, then the value is clear for him (the rahin) because the pledged property reached the rahin and the debt reached the murtahin, so the substitute and the substituted cannot come together in one ownership. And if he (the 'adl) became liable by delivering to the murtahin, then the rahin takes the value from him because if the 'ayn (essence) were still in his hand, he would take it when he pays the debt.
Source pages p. 261

Commentary
This passage contains two related rulings. First: When the 'adl becomes liable for the value of the pledged property (after delivering it to either party and it is destroyed), he cannot simply keep that value as a pledge in his own hand. Doing so would create a conflict where he is both the one giving the compensation and the one holding it as security, which is contradictory (mani'). Instead, the rahin and murtahin must agree to take the value from the 'adl and then place it as a pledge either with the same 'adl or with a third party. If they cannot agree or meet, they may refer to the qadi to arrange the pledge. Second: If the qadi places the value as a pledge with the 'adl, and then the rahin pays off the debt, the value's destination depends on to whom the 'adl originally delivered. If the 'adl delivered to the rahin (and became liable), the value belongs to the rahin because the pledged property has returned to him and the debt has been paid to the murtahin—there cannot be both the substitute (value) and the original (debt) in one ownership. If the 'adl delivered to the murtahin, then the rahin takes the value from the murtahin, just as he would take the original pledge if it existed. This lesson illustrates the elaborate rules governing liability and substitution in Hanafi pledge law, emphasizing the avoidance of conflict of interest and the role of the qadi in resolving disputes.

Key Terms
قیمت (qimah): The monetary value or compensation payable by the 'adl for loss of the pledged property.
بدل و مبدل (badal wa mubdal): The substitute (value) and the original subject (debt or pledged property). They cannot coexist in one ownership.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If the 'adl becomes liable for the value of the pledged property, why can't he keep that value as a pledge himself?
A) Because he is not trustworthy.
B) Because he would then be both the giver and receiver of the pledge, causing contradiction.
C) Because the value is no longer subject to pledge.
D) Because the rahin must immediately take the value.

Key Takeaway
When the 'adl becomes liable for the pledge's value, he cannot unilaterally hold it as a new pledge; only mutual agreement or qadi intervention can resolve the disposition.

Liability of the 'Adl for Delivering the Pawned Item to One Party
Ruling on trustee's liability when he delivers pawned item to pawner or pledgee

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the 'adl's liability when he delivers the pawned item to either the rahin or murtahin, and explain why he cannot keep the value as a new pledge.

Core Idea
The 'adl becomes liable for the pawn's value if he delivers it to either party because that constitutes ta'di.

This source chunk from a classical Hanafi text addresses a critical issue in pawn (rahn) law: the liability of the 'adl (trustee) who holds the pledged item. The passage establishes that delivering the pawn to either the pawner (rahin) or the pledgee (murtahin) without authorization is a transgression (ta'di) that makes the 'adl financially liable. It further explains that the 'adl cannot simply hold the compensation as a new pledge, and outlines the proper resolution through mutual agreement or judicial intervention.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the 'adl delivering the pawned item to either the rahin or murtahin. The ruling is that the 'adl becomes liable (ḍāmin) for the item's value.
Liability here means financial compensation, not ritual obligation.
2
Understand the 'adl's dual role
The 'adl is a depositee (mudi') for the rahin regarding the physical item, and a trustee (amin) for the murtahin regarding the value. Each party is a stranger to the other in the context of the pledge.
This dual role is key to understanding why delivery is ta'di.
3
Recognize why delivery constitutes ta'di
An amin is liable only if there is ta'di (transgression). Delivering to a stranger (the other party) is ta'di because the 'adl was appointed to hold for both jointly.
Without joint consent, delivery breaks the trust.
4
Analyze the consequence and limitation
Once liable, the 'adl must pay the value. He cannot keep that value as a new pledge in his hand because that would make him both payer and receiver, which is contradictory.
The 'adl cannot unilaterally convert the liability into a new pledge.
5
Note the remedy procedure
The rahin and murtahin can agree to place the value as a pledge with the 'adl or someone else. If they cannot agree, either may refer the matter to a judge who will arrange the pledge.
This ensures fairness and prevents deadlock.

وان تعذر اجتما عهما يرفع احدهما الى القاضي ليفعل كذالك ترجمہ اور جبکہ عادل مرہون کو ان دونوں میں سے کسی ایک کو دینے کی وجہ سے رہن کی قیمت کا ضامن ہوا اور اس مدفوع الیہ نے ہلاک کر دیا ہو یا وہ اس کے قبضہ میں ہلاک ہو گیا ہو قادر نہیں ہے عادل اس بات پر کہ قیمت کو اپنے قبضہ میں رہن کرے اس لئے کہ عادل اداء کرنے والا اور دینے والا ہو جائے گا اور ان دونوں کے درمیان منافات ہے لیکن وہ اتفاق کرلیں اس بات پر کہ قیمت کو عادل سے لے لیں اور اس کو اس کے یا اس کے غیر کے پاس رہن رکھیں اور اگر متعذر ہو جائے ان دونوں کا اجتماع تو ان میں سے قاضی کی جانب مرافعہ کرے تا کہ قاضی ایسا کر دے۔ تشریح جب عادل نے ان میں سے کسی کو مرہون دیدیا اور اس نے اس کو ہلاک کر دیا یا خود ہلاک ہو گیا تو عادل پر اس کی قیمت کا ضمان واجب ہوتا ہے اب عادل یہ چاہتا ہے کہ اس قیمت کو اپنے پاس رہن رکھ لوں تو کیا اس کو یہ حق ہے؟ تو فرمایا کہ نہیں ورنہ وہی دینے والا اور وہی لینے والا ہوگا اور یہ جائز ہے کیونکہ اب منافات نہیں رہی اور اگر چاہیں تو اس کے علاوہ کسی اور کے پاس بھی رکھ سکتے ہیں یا قاضی سے درخواست کریں وہ کسی کے پاس رکھدے۔ اور اگر کوئی ایسا مانع ہو جس کی وجہ سے راہن و مرتہن کا اجتماع نہ ہو سکتا ہو تو ان میں سے ایک قاضی سے درخواست کرے تا کہ قاضی رہن کسی کے پاس رکھدے۔
And if the 'adl gives it to the rahin or murtahin, then the 'adl will be liable, because the 'adl is a depositor (mudi') on behalf of the rahin regarding the substance, and a trustee (amin) for the murtahin regarding the value, and each of them is a stranger to the other. And a trustee becomes liable when giving to a stranger. Explanation: The trustee is not liable for destruction of the trust unless there is ta'di. The rahin and murtahin are strangers to each other. So if the 'adl gives the pledge to one of them and it is destroyed, the 'adl is liable. If the 'adl guarantees the value of the pledge after delivering it to one of them and the receiver destroys it or it perishes in his hand, the 'adl cannot make that value a pledge in his own hand, because he would become both payer and receiver, which is contradictory. But they can agree to take it from him and make it a pledge with him or someone else. If they cannot agree, one of them may refer to the judge. Explanation: When the 'adl gives the pledge and it is destroyed, he must pay its value. He cannot keep that value as a pledge. They can agree to leave it with him or another, or apply to the judge. If there is an obstacle preventing their agreement, one may apply to the judge to place it with someone.
Source pages p. 261

Commentary
This is a ruling from the Hanafi school concerning the liability of the 'adl (trustee) in a pawn (rahn) transaction. The 'adl is appointed to hold the pawned item. He is a depositee (mudi') for the rahin (pawner) regarding the physical item, and a trustee (amin) for the murtahin (pledgee) regarding the value. The rahin and murtahin are strangers (ajnabi) to each other in this context. If the 'adl delivers the pawned item to either of them, he commits ta'di (transgression) because he is an amin with respect to that party's interest, and giving to a stranger is a breach. The text explains the underlying principle: an amin is not liable for loss unless there is ta'di. Since the 'adl delivered to a stranger (the other party), he becomes liable for the value. The second part addresses what happens after the 'adl becomes liable for the value. He may not keep that value as a new pledge in his own hand, because that would make him both the payer (mu'addi) and receiver (mustawfi), which is contradictory. Instead, the rahin and murtahin may agree to hold the value as a pledge with the 'adl or with someone else. If they cannot agree, either party may refer the matter to the judge, who will arrange the pledge. The ruling is based on the principle of preventing conflict of interest and ensuring that compensation does not cause further contradiction.

Key Terms
عدل (‘adl): The trusted third party who holds the pawned item (rahn) until the debt is paid.
تعدي (ta‘dī): Transgression or breach of trust, such as delivering the pledge to an unauthorized party.
ضمان (ḍamān): Liability to compensate for loss or destruction, here the value of the pawned item.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If the 'adl delivers the pawned item to the rahin without authorization, and the item is destroyed in the rahin's hand, what happens?
A) The 'adl is not liable because he acted in good faith.
B) The 'adl is liable for the value of the item.
C) The rahin must return the item's value to the murtahin.
D) The murtahin loses his right to the pledge.

Key Takeaway
The 'adl becomes liable for the value of the pawn if he delivers it to either party without authorization, and he cannot retain that value as a new pledge; instead, the parties must agree or seek judicial resolution.
