Fate of the Value After the Debt is Paid
Ruling on who takes the value when the pawner pays the debt after the trustee became liable

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on ownership of the compensatory value after the pawner pays the debt, distinguishing the two cases based on delivery by the 'adl, and derive the ruling using qiyas.

Core Idea
The substitute (badal) follows the same rules as the original pledge; no one may combine both.

When a pawned item is destroyed due to the trustee's ('adl) liability, he must pay its value. The judge may place this value as a new pledge. Later, when the pawner (rahin) pays the debt, a question arises: who owns that value? The Hanafi school answers using a clear analogy to the original pledge, ensuring that neither the pledge nor its substitute is unjustly combined in one ownership.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and the initial event
The 'adl (trustee) became liable for the value of the destroyed pledge. The judge took that value and placed it back with the 'adl as a new pledge. Now the rahin pays the debt.
Focus on the fact that the value is now held as a pledge by the 'adl.
2
Distinguish the two delivery scenarios
Determine to whom the 'adl originally delivered the pledge: (a) to the rahin, or (b) to the murtahin. This determines the ruling.
The delivery happened before the destruction; it is the cause of liability.
3
Apply the qiyas (analogy)
The value stands in place (qā'im maqām) of the original pledge. Thus, after the debt is paid, whoever would have taken the original pledge now takes the value.
The illa (effective cause) is substitution: the value inherits the legal position of the original asset.
4
State the ruling for each case
If the 'adl delivered to rahin → the value stays with the 'adl (since rahin already had the original). If the 'adl delivered to murtahin → the rahin takes the value from the 'adl (since he would have taken the original).
The rule prevents badal and mubdal from combining in one ownership.
5
Verify the principle: no combining substitute and original
Ensure that in both cases the party who gets the value does not also possess the original pledge. This is the underlying rationale.
In case (a) rahin had the pledge, so value goes to 'adl; in case (b) murtahin had the pledge (destroyed), so value goes to rahin.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو فعل ذالك ثم قضى الراهن الدين وقد ضمن العدل القيمة بالدفع الى الراهن فالقيمة سالمة له لوصول المرهون الى الراهن ووصول الدين الى المرتهن فلا يجتمع البدل والمبدل في ملك واحد وان كان ضمنها بالدفع الى المرتهن فالراهن ياخذ القيمة منه لان العين لو كانت قائمة فى يده ياخذها اذا ادى الدين فکذالک یأخذ ماقام مقامها ولا جمع فيه بين البدل والمبدل. ترجمہ اور اگر قاضی نے ایسا کر دیا ( یعنی عادل سے قیمت لیکر اسی کے پاس رہن رکھدی ) پھر راہن نے قرض ادا کر دیا حالانکہ عادل قیمت کا ضامن راہن کو دینے کی وجہ سے ہوا تھا تو قیمت عادل کے لئے سالم رہی مرہون کے پہنچ جانے کی وجہ سے راہن کی جانب اور دین کے پہنچ جانے کی وجہ سے مرتہن کی جانب تو ملک واحد میں بدل اور مبدل جمع نہ ہوں گے اور اگر عادل قیمت کا ضامن مرتہن کو دینے کی وجہ سے ہوا تھا تو راہن عادل سے قیمت لیگا اس لئے کہ اگر عادل کے قبضہ میں عین مرہون موجود ہوتا تو راہن جب قرض ادا کرتا تو اس کو لیتا ایسے ہی وہ عین کے قائم مقام کو لیگا اور اس میں بدل اور مبدل کے درمیان جمع کرنا نہیں ہے۔ تشریح اب مصنف یہ بتائیں گے کہ جب قاضی نے عادل کے پاس قیمت رہن رکھدی تھی اور راہن نے مرتبہن کا قرض ادا کر دیا تو قیمت کس کی ہوگی ؟ تو فرمایا کہ اگر عادل نے مرہون راہن کو دیا تھا تو بس قیمت عادل کی ہو جائے گی کیونکہ مرتن کو اس کا قرض مل چکا ہے اور راہن کو اس کی ملک ( مرهون ) مل چکی ہے کیونکہ اس کے پاس ہلاک ہوا ہے لہذا قیمت عادل کی ہوگی کیونکہ اگر اس قیمت کو راہن ہی کو دیدیا جائے تو بدل اور مبدل دونوں کا اجتماع ملک راہن میں لازم آتا ہے اور یہ نا جائز ہے۔ اور اگر عادل نے مرہون مرتبہن کو دیا اور اب راہن نے مرتہن کا قرض ادا کر دیا تو قیمت راہن کی ہوگی کیونکہ اگر اصل مرہون ہوتا تو راہن قرض ادا کر کے اس کو لیتا لہذا یہاں مرہون کے قائم مقام قیمت کو لے گا اور یہاں بدل اور مبدل کا اجتماع بھی لازم نہیں آتا۔
And if the judge does that, then the rahin pays the debt, and the 'adl had guaranteed the value by delivering to the rahin, then the value remains safe for the 'adl because the pledged item has reached the rahin and the debt has reached the murtahin, so the substitute and the original do not combine in one ownership. And if the 'adl had guaranteed by delivering to the murtahin, then the rahin takes the value from him, because if the original item were in his hand, he would take it when he pays the debt; likewise he takes what stands in its place, and there is no combining of substitute and original. Translation: And if the judge did that (i.e., took the value from the 'adl and placed it as a pledge with him), then the rahin paid the debt, while the 'adl had become liable for the value by delivering to the rahin, then the value remains safe for the 'adl, because the pledged item reached the rahin and the debt reached the murtahin, so the substitute and original do not combine in one ownership. And if the 'adl had become liable by delivering to the murtahin, then the rahin takes the value from him, because if the original item were in his hand, he would take it when he pays the debt; likewise he takes what stands in its place, and there is no combining of substitute and original. Explanation: The author now explains that when the judge placed the value with the 'adl and the rahin pays the debt, who owns the value? He says: If the 'adl had given the pledged item to the rahin, then the value belongs to the 'adl, because the murtahin has received his debt, and the rahin has received his property (the pledged item was destroyed in his hands), so giving the value to the rahin would combine substitute and original in his ownership, which is invalid. If the 'adl had given the pledged item to the murtahin, then the rahin takes the value, because if the original pledge existed, the rahin would take it after paying the debt; so he takes what stands in its place, and there is no combining.
Source pages p. 261

Commentary
This passage details the distribution of the value that the 'adl paid as compensation, after the rahin (pawner) pays off the debt. The judge has already placed that value as a pledge with the 'adl (or another). Two cases are distinguished based on whom the 'adl originally delivered the pledge to. In the first case, if the 'adl became liable because he gave the pledge to the rahin, then the value remains with the 'adl. The reasoning: the rahin's debt is paid to the murtahin, and the rahin already received the actual pledge (which was destroyed in his hands). If the value were also given to the rahin, he would combine both the actual item (mubdal) and its substitute (badal) in his ownership, which is not allowed. In the second case, if the 'adl became liable because he gave the pledge to the murtahin, then after the rahin pays the debt, the rahin takes the value from the 'adl. This is analogous to the original pledge: had it been intact, the rahin would retrieve it after paying. The value stands in its place (qāma maqāmahu). There is no double gain because the murtahin already held the actual pledge and it was destroyed; the rahin gets only the substitute. The ruling uses qiyas (analogy) to the original pledge, which is clear and obvious (qiyās jaliyy).

Key Terms
بدل (badal): Substitute, here the monetary value paid by the 'adl in place of the destroyed pledge.
مبدل (mubdal): The original item, here the pawned item itself.
قائم مقام (qā'im maqām): Stand in place of; the value is treated as a substitute under the same legal rulings as the original pledge.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If the 'adl delivered the pawned item to the murtahin, and then the rahin pays the debt, who takes the value?
A) The murtahin keeps it.
B) The 'adl keeps it.
C) The rahin takes it from the 'adl.
D) The judge takes it.

Key Takeaway
The compensatory value after the 'adl's liability is distributed according to whom the original pledge was delivered, to avoid combining the substitute and the original in one ownership.

The 'Adl's Recourse Against the Murtahin in Pledge Cases
Clarifications on the ruling of the value and recourse against the murtahin

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to determine whether an 'adl can recover compensation from the murtahin by distinguishing between transfers as trust (āriyyah/wadīʿah) and as pledge (rahn).

Core Idea
The 'adl's right to recover hinges on the nature of the transfer: trust (no liability) vs. pledge (liability).

In pawn (rahn) transactions, the 'adl (trustee) sometimes delivers the pledged item to the murtahin (creditor). If the item is lost or destroyed, a key question arises: can the 'adl, after compensating the rahin (debtor), recover that amount from the murtahin? This lesson examines two clarificatory notes from the commentary: the first confirms that the ruling applies universally regardless of how the value was placed; the second provides a scenario-dependent answer based on whether the transfer was a loan/deposit or a pledge.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two notes (tanbīh)
The passage contains two separate notes: the first universalizes the value ruling; the second answers a practical question about the 'adl's recourse.
Note 1 is brief; the bulk is Note 2.
2
Understand the universal scope of Note 1
Note 1 states that the earlier ruling about the value (price of the pawned item) applies whether the value is held by the same 'adl or another, and whether it was placed by a judge or by mutual consent.
This eliminates procedural exceptions.
3
Analyze the three scenarios in Note 2
Note 2 presents three possible characterizations of the transfer from 'adl to murtahin: (a) loan ('āriyyah), (b) deposit (wadī'ah), (c) pledge (rahn). For each, determine liability.
The key distinction is trust (amānah) vs. guarantee (ḍamān).
4
Apply the principle: ownership of the paid value
Once the 'adl pays compensation to the rahin, he becomes the owner of the pawned item retroactively. Thus any subsequent transfer is treated as his own property.
This affects the nature of the transfer from the 'adl's perspective.
5
Conclude the ruling on recourse
If the transfer was a trust (loan or deposit), the murtahin is not liable without ta'dī (transgression). If it was a pledge (rahn) in lieu of the original right, the 'adl can recover whether the item was destroyed or consumed.
The authority cited is Shami (Ibn 'Abidin).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تنبيها قیمت اسی عادل کے پاس رہن ہو یا کسی دوسرے کے پاس دونوں صورتوں میں یہی حکم ہے نیز عادل کے پاس قیمت رہن حکم قاضی ہو یارا ہن اور مرتہن کے اتفاق سے بہر صورت یہی حکم ہے۔ تنبیه - ۲ مذکورہ دوسری صورت میں جبکہ مرتہن کو مرہون دیا گیا تھا جس کی وجہ سے عادل پر ضمان آیا تھا اور راہن نے مرتہن کا قرض دیگر قیمت کو لے لیا تو کیا عادل کو حق ہے کہ وہ مرتہن سے اپنا تاوان وصول کرے؟ جواب ... اس میں تحقیق کی جائے اگر عادل نے مرہون اس کو عاریہ دیا ہے اور وہ اس کے پاس خود بخود بغیر تعدی کے ہلاک ہو گیا تو مرتہن پر ضمان نہ ہو گا۔ اور اگر مرتہن اس کے پاس خود بخود بغیر تعدی کے ہلاک ہو گیا کیونکہ عادل اداء ضمان کی وجہ سے مرہون کا مالک شمار ہوگا تو گویا اس نے اپنی ملک ودیعت یا عاریت دی ہے اور امانت میں مستعغیر اور مودع تعدی کی وجہ سے ضامن ہوا کرتے ہیں لہذا مرتین پر ضمان واجب ہوگا اور اگر عادل نے مرہون اس کو رہن کے طریقہ پر دیا ہے اس کے حق کے بدلہ میں یوں کہتے ہوئے کہ اس کو اپنے حق کے بدلہ میں لے لے یا اس کو اپنے پاس محبوس رکھ تو اب عادل کو حق ہو گا کہ ہلاک و استبلاک دونوں صورتوں میں اس تاوان کو مرتہن سے وصول کرے کیونکہ عادل نے مرتہن کو مرہون ضمانت کے طریقہ پر دیا تھا۔ شامی ۴۲۳ ج ۵
Note: Whether the value is held as a pledge with this same 'adl or with someone else, the same ruling applies. Also, whether the value is held by the 'adl by order of the judge or by agreement of the rahin and murtahin, the same ruling applies. Note 2: In the second mentioned case, when the pledge was given to the murtahin (causing the 'adl's liability) and the rahin paid the debt and took the value, does the 'adl have the right to recover his loss from the murtahin? Answer: Investigation is needed. If the 'adl gave the pledge to him as a loan ('āriyya) and it perished without ta'dī, then the murtahin is not liable. But if the 'adl gave it as a deposit (wadī'a) or loan, and it perished without ta'dī, then the 'adl, having become owner of the pledge by paying compensation, is considered to have given his own property as deposit or loan, and the borrower/depositee becomes liable only for ta'dī. Therefore, the murtahin is not liable unless he committed ta'dī. And if the 'adl gave the pledge to him as a pledge (rahn) in lieu of his right, saying 'take it in lieu of your right' or 'hold it as collateral,' then the 'adl has the right to recover the compensation from the murtahin in both cases (destruction or consumption), because the 'adl gave it as a pledge by way of guarantee. (Shami, vol. 5, p. 423)
Source pages p. 262

Commentary
This passage contains two important clarifications (tanbīh) by the commentator. The first note confirms that the rulings previously given about the value apply universally: whether the value is held by the same 'adl or a different third party, and whether it was placed by a judge's order or by mutual consent of the rahin and murtahin. The second note addresses a practical follow-up: when the 'adl became liable by delivering the pledge to the murtahin, and the rahin later paid the debt and took the value from the 'adl, does the 'adl have a right to recover that compensation from the murtahin? The answer depends on the nature of the transfer from the 'adl to the murtahin. Three scenarios are distinguished: (1) If the 'adl gave the pledge as a loan (āriyyah) or deposit (wadī'ah) and it perished without ta'dī (transgression), the murtahin is not liable, because the 'adl, having paid the value, becomes the owner of the pledge from the moment of liability; thus he is lending or depositing his own property, and a trustee is not liable without ta'dī. (2) If the 'adl gave the pledge to the murtahin as a pledge (rahn) in substitution for the murtahin's original right over the item, saying 'take it in lieu of your right' or 'hold it as security,' then the 'adl can recover the compensation from the murtahin regardless of whether the item was destroyed or consumed. This is because the transfer was itself a form of guarantee (ḍamān), and the murtahin received it as a pledgee, making him a possessor with liability. The commentator cites al-Durr al-Mukhtar and Shami (Ibn 'Abidin) as authority.

Key Terms
عاریہ (‘āriyyah): A gratuitous loan of an item for use, where the borrower is not liable for loss without ta'dī.
ودیعت (wadī‘ah): Deposit for safekeeping; the depositee (mūda‘) is an amīn and not liable without ta'dī.
تاوان (tāwān): Compensation or indemnity paid by the 'adl; he seeks to recover it from the murtahin.
تعدی (ta‘dī): Transgression or wrongful act; the condition that makes a trustee liable.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, in which scenario does the 'adl have the right to recover compensation (tāwān) from the murtahin?
A) When the transfer was a loan ('āriyyah) and the item perished without ta'dī.
B) When the transfer was a deposit (wadī'ah) and the item perished without ta'dī.
C) When the transfer was a pledge (rahn) in lieu of the murtahin's right.
D) In all cases where the 'adl pays the rahin.

Key Takeaway
The 'adl's right to recover compensation from the murtahin depends on whether the transfer of the pawned item was characterized as a trust (no recovery) or a guarantee (recovery allowed).

The Rahin Appointing an Agent to Sell the Pledge at Maturity
Ruling on agency in rahn at maturity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on the rahin appointing an agent to sell the pledge at maturity and explain the legal basis.

Core Idea
The rahin may appoint any person, even the pledgee, as agent to sell his property because ownership remains his.

A pawner (rahin) owns the pledged item and may delegate its sale at debt maturity to anyone, including the pledgee (murtahin), trustee ('adl), or a stranger. This ruling removes the misconception that the murtahin has a conflict of interest; the rahin's ownership validates any agency appointment.

Guided Path
1
Identify the actors
Recognize the three parties: rahin (pawner), murtahin (pledgee), 'adl (trustee), and 'ghayruh' (any other person).
2
State the condition
The agency is only valid at the time of maturity (hulūl ajal) of the debt.
The text explicitly mentions 'when the debt matures'.
3
Recall the ruling
The agency is valid (jā'iz) for all mentioned appointees. There is no restriction on appointing the murtahin despite his interest as creditor.
The reason: the rahin is selling his own property (tawkīl bi-bay'i mālihi).

Source Text

راہن کا مرتہن یا عادل یا کسی غیر کو حلول اجل پر رہن کے بیچنے کا وکیل بنانا کیسا ہے؟ قال واذا وكل الراهن المرتهن او العدل او غيرهما ببيع الرهن عند حلول الدين فالوكالة جائزة لانه توكيل ببيع ماله
How is it for the rahin to appoint the murtahin or the 'adl or someone else as agent to sell the pledge at the maturity of the term? He said: If the rahin appoints the murtahin or the 'adl or others as agents to sell the pledge at the maturity of the debt, the agency is valid, because it is an appointment to sell his own property.
Source pages p. 262

Commentary
This is a concise ruling (hukm) about agency (wakāla) in the context of rahn. The rahin (pawner) is the owner of the pawned item and has the right to sell it when the debt matures. He may delegate this authority to anyone, including the murtahin (pledgee), the 'adl (trustee), or another third party. The agency is valid (jā'iz) because the rahin is selling his own property; he retains ownership, and the pledge is merely security. The text uses the phrase 'tawkīl bi-bay'i mālihi' (appointment to sell his property), which establishes the legal basis: the rahin's ownership gives him full authority to appoint an agent for sale. The ruling is straightforward and does not contain additional conditions or disagreements; it is a memorization anchor for students.

Key Terms
توكيل (tawkīl): Appointment of an agent (wakīl) to perform a legal act, here selling the pledge.
حلول أجل (hulūl ajal): Maturity of the term, the time when the debt becomes due and the pledge may be sold.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Ownership of the Substitute Price in Pledge (Rahn) Scenarios
Explains two scenarios regarding ownership of the substitute when the pledge is destroyed

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two scenarios determining ownership of the substitute price (badal) when a pledge is destroyed while deposited with a just person (adil), and apply the principle that substitute and original cannot be combined in one ownership.

Core Idea
The substitute price cannot be owned by the same person who has the original pledge, as that would combine badal and mubdal.

When a pledged property is destroyed and its substitute price is deposited with a just person (adil), who owns that price? This lesson explains two scenarios based on whom the adil guaranteed the price to. The underlying principle is that the substitute (badal) and the original (mubdal) cannot coexist in the same ownership.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two parties in a pledge (rahn)
The rahin (pledgor) gives a pledge to the murtahin (pledgee) as security for a debt. A just person (adil) may hold the pledge on behalf of the judge.
2
Understand the first scenario: adil guarantees price to rahin
If the adil became guarantor for the price by giving it to the rahin, then when the rahin pays the debt, the price remains with the adil because the rahin already received the original pledge (destroyed) and the murtahin received the debt.
Giving the price to the rahin would combine badal and mubdal in his ownership, which is invalid.
3
Understand the second scenario: adil guarantees price to murtahin
If the adil became guarantor for the price by giving it to the murtahin, then when the rahin pays the debt, the rahin takes the price from the adil because it stands in place of the pledge he would reclaim.
In this case, there is no combination of substitute and original.
4
Apply the principle: no combining badal and mubdal
The key rule is that the substitute (badal) and the original (mubdal) cannot be owned by the same person at the same time. This determines the outcome in each scenario.
This principle is derived from the Hanafi legal maxims.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فکذالک یأخذ ماقام مقامها ولا جمع فيه بين البدل والمبدل.
ترجمہ اور اگر قاضی نے ایسا کر دیا ( یعنی عادل سے قیمت لیکر اسی کے پاس رہن رکھدی ) پھر راہن نے قرض ادا کر دیا حالانکہ عادل قیمت کا ضامن راہن کو دینے کی وجہ سے ہوا تھا تو قیمت عادل کے لئے سالم رہی مرہون کے پہنچ جانے کی وجہ سے راہن کی جانب اور دین کے پہنچ جانے کی وجہ سے مرتہن کی جانب تو ملک واحد میں بدل اور مبدل جمع نہ ہوں گے اور اگر عادل قیمت کا ضامن مرتہن کو دینے کی وجہ سے ہوا تھا تو راہن عادل سے قیمت لیگا اس لئے کہ اگر عادل کے قبضہ میں عین مرہون موجود ہوتا تو راہن جب قرض ادا کرتا تو اس کو لیتا ایسے ہی وہ عین کے قائم مقام کو لیگا اور اس میں بدل اور مبدل کے درمیان جمع کرنا نہیں ہے۔ تشریح اب مصنف یہ بتائیں گے کہ جب قاضی نے عادل کے پاس قیمت رہن رکھدی تھی اور راہن نے مرتبہن کا قرض ادا کر دیا تو قیمت کس کی ہوگی ؟
تو فرمایا کہ اگر عادل نے مرہون راہن کو دیا تھا تو بس قیمت عادل کی ہو جائے گی کیونکہ مرتن کو اس کا قرض مل چکا ہے اور راہن کو اس کی ملک ( مرهون ) مل چکی ہے کیونکہ اس کے پاس ہلاک ہوا ہے لہذا قیمت عادل کی ہوگی کیونکہ اگر اس قیمت کو راہن ہی کو دیدیا جائے تو بدل اور مبدل دونوں کا اجتماع ملک راہن میں لازم آتا ہے اور یہ نا جائز ہے۔ اور اگر عادل نے مرہون مرتبہن کو دیا اور اب راہن نے مرتہن کا قرض ادا کر دیا تو قیمت راہن کی ہوگی کیونکہ اگر اصل مرہون ہوتا تو راہن قرض ادا کر کے اس کو لیتا لہذا یہاں مرہون کے قائم مقام قیمت کو لے گا اور یہاں بدل اور مبدل کا اجتماع بھی لازم نہیں آتا۔ تنبیها قیمت اسی عادل کے پاس رہن ہو یا کسی دوسرے کے پاس دونوں صورتوں میں یہی حکم ہے نیز عادل کے پاس قیمت رہن حکم قاضی ہو یارا ہن اور مرتہن کے اتفاق سے بہر صورت یہی حکم ہے۔ تنبیه - ۲ مذکورہ دوسری صورت میں جبکہ مرتہن کو مرہون دیا گیا تھا جس کی وجہ سے عادل پر ضمان آیا تھا اور راہن نے مرتہن کا قرض دیگر قیمت کو لے لیا تو کیا عادل کو حق ہے کہ وہ مرتہن سے اپنا تاوان وصول کرے؟
جواب ... اس میں تحقیق کی جائے اگر عادل نے مرہون اس کو عاریہ دیا ہے اور وہ اس کے پاس خود بخود بغیر تعدی کے ہلاک ہو گیا تو مرتہن پر ضمان نہ ہو گا۔ اور اگر مرتہن اس کے پاس خود بخود بغیر تعدی کے ہلاک ہو گیا کیونکہ عادل اداء ضمان کی وجہ سے مرہون کا مالک شمار ہوگا تو گویا اس نے اپنی ملک ودیعت یا عاریت دی ہے اور امانت میں مستعغیر اور مودع تعدی کی وجہ سے ضامن ہوا کرتے ہیں لہذا مرتین پر ضمان واجب ہوگا اور اگر عادل نے مرہون اس کو رہن کے طریقہ پر دیا ہے اس کے حق کے بدلہ میں یوں کہتے ہوئے کہ اس کو اپنے حق کے بدلہ میں لے لے یا اس کو اپنے پاس محبوس رکھ تو اب عادل کو حق ہو گا کہ ہلاک و استبلاک دونوں صورتوں میں اس تاوان کو مرتہن سے وصول کرے کیونکہ عادل نے مرتہن کو مرہون ضمانت کے طریقہ پر دیا تھا۔ شامی ۴۲۳ ج ۵
Thus he takes that which stands in its place, and there is no combining between the substitute and the original. Translation: And if the judge did that (i.e., took the price from the just person [adil] and placed it as a pledge with him), then the rahin (pledgor) paid the debt, even though the adil had become the guarantor of the price due to giving it to the rahin, then the price remains for the adil because the pledge (marhun) reached the rahin, and the debt reached the murtahin (pledgee), so in one ownership the substitute (badal) and the original (mubdal) are not combined. And if the adil had become the guarantor of the price due to giving it to the murtahin, then the rahin will take the price from the adil, because if the original pledge was in the adil's possession, the rahin would take it when he paid the debt; similarly, he will take what stands in its place, and there is no combining between the substitute and the original. Explanation: Now the author will explain that when the judge placed the price as a pledge with the adil, and the rahin paid the murtahin's debt, then to whom does the price belong? He said: If the adil gave the pledge to the rahin, then the price becomes the adil's, because the murtahin has received his debt, and the rahin has received his ownership (the pledge) because it was destroyed in his possession; so the price is the adil's, because if this price were given to the rahin, then both the substitute and the original would be combined in the rahin's ownership, which is invalid. And if the adil gave the pledge to the murtahin, and then the rahin paid the murtahin's debt, then the price belongs to the rahin, because if the original pledge existed, the rahin would take it after paying the debt; so here he will take the price which stands in place of the pledge, and there is no combination of substitute and original. Note 1: Whether the price is deposited with this adil or another, the ruling is the same; also whether the price is with the adil by the judge's order or by agreement of the rahin and murtahin, the ruling is the same in all cases. Note 2: In the aforementioned second scenario, where the pledge was given to the murtahin, causing the adil to become a guarantor, and the rahin took the price after paying the debt, does the adil have the right to recover compensation from the murtahin? Answer: This requires investigation. If the adil gave the pledge to the murtahin as a loan (ariyah) and it was destroyed without any transgression (ta'addi), then the murtahin is not liable. And if it was destroyed without transgression, because the adil is considered the owner of the pledge due to paying the guarantee, then it is as if he gave his own property as a deposit (wadi'ah) or loan, and in trust (amanah) the borrower and depositor are only liable for transgression; so the murtahin is not liable for guarantee. And if the adil gave the pledge to the murtahin in the manner of a pledge (rahn) in exchange for his right, saying 'take it in exchange for your right' or 'keep it in your possession,' then the adil has the right to recover compensation from the murtahin in both cases of destruction or loss, because the adil gave the pledge to the murtahin in the manner of a guarantee. (Shami, vol. 5, p. 423)
Source pages p. 262

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling on the price (qimat) when a judge places it with a just person (adil) as a substitute for a destroyed pledge. The passage is a ruling_statement from the Hanafi school, specifically from the commentary on al-Hidayah. The author explains two scenarios based on whether the adil became guarantor due to giving the price to the rahin or to the murtahin. In the first scenario (adil gave price to rahin), the price remains with the adil because the rahin received the pledge (destroyed) and the murtahin received his debt, so giving the price to the rahin would combine substitute and original in one ownership, which is impermissible. In the second scenario (adil gave price to murtahin), the price goes to the rahin because it stands in place of the pledge he would have reclaimed upon paying the debt. Two notes follow: the ruling is consistent regardless of who deposited the price or by whose order; and in the second scenario, the adil may recover compensation from the murtahin depending on the nature of the transfer (loan vs. pledge). This illustrates the Hanafi principle that a substitute cannot be combined with the original in one ownership.

Key Terms
بدل (badal): Substitute or price that stands in place of the original pledged property.
مبدل (mubdal): The original asset that has been replaced or for which a substitute is given.
ضمان (daman): Guarantee or liability; here it refers to the adil becoming liable for the price toward either the rahin or the murtahin.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Because the rahin already has the original pledge, so giving him the price would combine substitute and original in his ownership.
C) Because the judge ordered so.
D) Because the murtahin refused the price.

Key Takeaway
The ownership of the substitute price in a destroyed pledge depends on who the adil guaranteed the price to, driven by the principle that substitute and original cannot be combined in one ownership.

Permissibility of Appointing an Agent to Sell the Pledge at Maturity
States the ruling on appointing an agent to sell the pledge at maturity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on the rahin appointing an agent to sell the pledge at maturity and identify the condition for the agent's authority.

Core Idea
Appointing an agent to sell one's own property at a future date is permissible.

In pledge (rahn) contracts, the pledgor (rahin) often needs to authorize someone to sell the pledged property if the debt is not repaid on time. This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on such an appointment. The passage from al-Quduri clarifies that the rahin may appoint the pledgee (murtahin), an impartial person (adil), or any other individual as an agent to sell the pledge at maturity, and the agency is valid because the pledgor is merely appointing an agent to sell his own property.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties involved
The rahin (pledgor), the murtahin (pledgee), the adil (trusted third party), or any other person (ghair) can be appointed as agent. Note that the murtahin himself can be the agent.
The permissibility applies regardless of who the agent is.
2
Identify the act being appointed
The rahin appoints the agent to sell the pledge (al-rahn) at the time when the debt matures (hulul al-ajal). The agent's authority is conditional on the maturity of the debt.
The agency is specifically for sale after maturity, not before.
3
State the ruling
The ruling is that such an agency (wakalah) is permissible (ja'iz). The text says 'al-wikalah ja'izah'.
The ruling is not obligatory or recommended beyond general permissibility.
4
Understand the rationale
The reason given is that the rahin is appointing an agent to sell his own property. Since the pledge is owned by the rahin, he has full authority to sell it or authorize its sale, even to the pledgee.
This reasoning overcomes any potential conflict of interest when the agent is the pledgee.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
راہن کا مرتہن یا عادل یا کسی غیر کو حلول اجل پر رہن کے بیچنے کا وکیل بنانا کیسا ہے؟
قال واذا وكل الراهن المرتهن او العدل او غيرهما ببيع الرهن عند حلول الدين فالوكالة جائزة لانه توكيل ببيع ماله
ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور جبکہ راہن نے مرتہن یا عادل یا ان دونوں کے غیر کو مرہون کی مبیع کا وکیل بنایا ہوادائیگی دین کا وقت آنے پر تو وکالت جائز ہے اس لئے کہ یہ جائز اپنے مال کی بیع کا وکیل بنانا ہے۔
تشریح راہن نے اگر کسی کوبھی وکیل بنا دیا کہ جب ادا دین کا وقت آ جائے تو مرہون کو فروخت کر کے قرض ادا کر دے تو چونکہ یہ اپنے مال کی بیع کا وکیل بنانا ہے لہذا اس کے جواز میں شبہ نہیں ہے۔
How is it for the rahin to appoint the murtahin, the adil, or someone else as an agent to sell the pledge at maturity? He said: And when the rahin appoints the murtahin, the adil, or others as an agent to sell the pledge at the maturity of the debt, the agency is permissible, because it is appointing an agent to sell his property. Translation: Quduri said: And when the rahin appoints the murtahin, the adil, or someone other than these two as an agent for the sale of the pledge when the time for payment of the debt comes, then the agency is permissible, because it is appointing an agent to sell his own property. Explanation: If the rahin appoints anyone as an agent that when the time for payment of the debt arrives, he should sell the pledge and pay off the debt, then since this is appointing an agent to sell his own property, there is no doubt about its permissibility.
Source pages p. 263

Commentary
This passage is a ruling_statement from the Hanafi school. The matn from al-Quduri states that it is permissible for the pledgeor (rahin) to appoint the pledgee (murtahin), the just person (adil), or any third party as an agent to sell the pledge once the debt matures. The reasoning is straightforward: the rahin is appointing an agent to sell his own property (the pledge), and such an agency is generally valid. The commentary repeats this rationale, emphasizing that since it is the rahin's own property, there is no issue. This ruling applies regardless of the identity of the agent.

Key Terms
وکالت (wakalah): Agency; appointing someone to perform a legal act on one's behalf.
حلول اجل (hulul al-ajal): The arrival of the maturity date of a debt; when payment becomes due.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) The debt must have matured (hulul al-ajal).
C) The murtahin must consent.
D) The pledge must be movable.

Key Takeaway
A rahin may appoint any agent, even the murtahin, to sell the pledge at maturity, as it is a sale of his own property.

Agency Stipulated in Pledge Contract is Irrevocable
Ruling with reasoning on stipulated agency in pledge.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on agency stipulated in a pledge contract and explain the legal reasoning that makes it irrevocable.

Core Idea
A stipulated agency in a pledge becomes a right of the pledgee and cannot be revoked without his consent.

In pledge contracts, the pledgor often authorizes the pledgee to sell the collateral if the debt is unpaid. But what if the pledgor later changes his mind? This lesson explores the Hanafi position that once the agency is stipulated as a condition of the pledge, it becomes binding and irrevocable, protecting the pledgee's security interest.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Legal Scenario and Ruling
Read the passage to determine the act (stipulated agency in rahn) and its ruling (irrevocable). The rahin cannot dismiss the agent.
The ruling is that the agent is not dismissed even if the rahin attempts it.
2
Understand the Reasoning: Agency as Attribute of Pledge
The passage states that the agency becomes an attribute and right of the pledge contract itself, so it inherits the binding nature of the pledge.
Stipulations in a binding contract become binding as well.
3
Analyze the Qiyas (Analogy) to Litigation Agency
The text compares the stipulated agency to an agent appointed for litigation at the plaintiff's request, which is also irrevocable. Identify the shared illa: the third party's right becomes attached.
The difference is that in pledge, the rahin can dismiss only with murtahin's consent; in litigation, only the plaintiff's knowledge is required.
4
Identify the Condition for Revocability
The rahin can dismiss the agent only if the murtahin agrees, since the agency is now a right of the murtahin.
This shows the agency is not absolutely irrevocable; mutual consent can revoke it.
5
Distinguish the Hanafi Position from Other Schools
The passage implies that other schools may allow revocation, but Hanafi law, following Imam Zufar, holds it binding.
The commentary attributes the reasoning to Imam Zufar.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وکالت کی عقد رہن میں شرط ہو تو راہن وکیل کو معزول نہیں کر سکتا
وان شرطت في عقد الرهن فليس للراهن ان يعزل الوكيل وان عزله لم ينعزل لانها لما شرطت في ضمن عقد الرهن صار وصفا من اوصافه وحقا من حقوقه الأترى انه لزيادة الوثيقة فيلزم بلزوم اصله ولانه تعلق به حق المرتهن وفى العزل اتو أحقه وصار كالوكيل بالخصومة بطلب المدعى
ترجمہ اور اگر وکالت عقد ر ہن میں مشروط ہوئی ہو تو را ہن کو یہ حق نہیں کہ وہ وکیل کو معزول کر دے اور اگر اس کو معزول کر دیا تو وہ معزول نہ ہوگا اس لئے کہ وکالت جب عقد رهن کے ضمن میں مشروط ہو تو وہ رہن کے اوصاف میں سے ایک وصف اور اس کے حقوق میں سے ایک حق ہو گیا کیا آپ نہیں دیکھتے کہ عقد وکالت مضبوطی کی زیادتی کے لئے ہے تو عقد وکالت اپنی اصل ( رہن زد سے لازم ہو جائیگا اور اس لئے کہ عقد وکالت کے ساتھ مرتہن کا حق وابستہ ہو گیا ہے اور عزل میں اس کے حق کو ہلاک کرنا ہے اور یہ مدعی کی طلب پر وکیل بالخصومت کے مثل ہو گیا ۔ تشریح بدایہ کے ص ۵۱۸ ج ۴ پر امام زفر کی دلیل میں یہ مسئلہ گذر چکا ہے جہاں انہوں نے کہا تھا کالو كالة المشروطة في الرهن فیلزمہ بلزومہ ۔ جس کا خلاصہ یہ ہے کہ اگر عقد ر ہن میں وکالت مشروط ہوگئی ہو تو اب وہ لازم ہو جائے گی لہذا اگر راہن چاہے کہ وکیل کو معزول کر دوں تو نہیں کر سکتا اور اگر کرے تو وکیل معزول نہ ہوگا کیونکہ اب وکالت حقوق عقد ر ہن میں سے ایک حق ہو چکا ہے جو رہن کے لزوم کی وجہ سے لا زم ہو جائے گی کیونکہ وکالت کی شرط کا مقصد پختگی کی زیادتی ہے اور دوسری وجہ یہ بھی ہے کہ اب اس سے مرتبہن کا حق متعلق ہو چکا ہے اور عزل وکیل میں حق مرتہن کا ابطال ہے جس کا راہن کو حق نہیں ہے۔ اور اس کی مثال بالکل ایسی ہے کہ مدعی نے مدعی علیہ سے مطالبہ کیا کہ عدالت میں جواہد ہی کے لئے کسی کو وکیل بنائے جس پر مدعی علیہ نے کسی کو وکیل بنا دیا تو اب مدعی علیہ کو حق نہ ہوگا مامی علم کے بغیر وکیل کو معزول کر دے اس لئے کہ اس کے ساتھ مدعی کا حق وابستہ ہو گیا ہے اسی طرح وکیل رہن سے بھی مرتبہن کا حق متعلق ہو چکا ہے لیکن ان دونوں میں اتنا اتفاق ہے کہ رہن کی صورت میں راہن کو عزل وکیل کا حق صرف جب ہوگا کہ مرتین راضی ہو جائے اور وکیل بالخصومت میں رضاء مدعی ضروری نہیں بلکہ اس کا علم
ضروری ہے۔
Agency stipulated in the pledge contract – the rahin cannot dismiss the agent. And if agency is stipulated in the contract of pledge, then it is not for the rahin to dismiss the agent, and if he dismisses him, he is not dismissed. Because when it is stipulated within the pledge contract, it becomes one of its attributes and one of its rights. Do you not see that it is for additional security? So it becomes binding by the binding nature of its origin. And because the right of the murtahin is attached to it, and in dismissal there is annulment of his right. And it becomes like the agent for litigation at the request of the plaintiff. Translation: And if the agency is stipulated in the contract of pledge, then the rahin does not have the right to dismiss the agent, and if he dismisses him, he is not dismissed. Because when the agency is stipulated within the pledge contract, it becomes one of the attributes of the pledge and one of its rights. Do you not see that it is for additional security? So the agency becomes binding by the binding nature of its origin (the pledge). And because the right of the murtahin is attached to it, and in dismissal there is annulment of his right. And it becomes like the agent for litigation at the request of the plaintiff. Explanation: This issue has been mentioned in Badayah (vol. 4, p. 518) in the proof of Imam Zufar, where he said: 'The stipulated agency in the pledge becomes binding by its binding nature.' The summary is that if the agency is stipulated in the pledge contract, then it becomes binding. Therefore, if the rahin wishes to dismiss the agent, he cannot, and if he does, the agent is not dismissed, because the agency has become a right of the pledge contract, which becomes binding due to the binding nature of the pledge. This is because the purpose of stipulating agency is to increase security. The second reason is that the right of the murtahin is now attached to it, and dismissing the agent would annul the murtahin's right, which the rahin is not entitled to do. The analogy is to the agent for litigation (wakil bi al-khusumah): when the plaintiff demands from the defendant to appoint an agent for presenting evidence in court, and the defendant does so, then the defendant cannot dismiss that agent without the plaintiff's knowledge, because the plaintiff's right has become attached. Similarly, in the case of the agency in pledge, the murtahin's right is attached. However, there is a difference: in the case of pledge, the rahin can dismiss the agent only if the murtahin agrees; whereas in the case of litigation agent, the plaintiff's consent is not necessary, only his knowledge is required.
Source pages p. 263

Commentary
This passage is a ruling_statement with reasoning from the Hanafi school. It addresses a specific scenario where the agency to sell the pledge is stipulated as a condition within the contract of pledge (rahn). The ruling is that once such a condition is included, the rahin (pledgor) loses the right to revoke the agency. If he attempts to dismiss the agent, the dismissal is ineffective. The reason given is that the agency becomes an attribute and a right of the pledge contract itself. Since the contract of pledge is binding (lazim), the agency attached to it also becomes binding. Moreover, the murtahin's (pledgee's) right is now attached to this agency; revoking it would nullify his right. The text draws an analogy to an agent appointed for litigation at the request of the plaintiff: once the defendant appoints such an agent, he cannot dismiss him unilaterally because the plaintiff's right is attached. The commentary adds a nuance: in the pledge case, the rahin may dismiss the agent only if the murtahin agrees, whereas in litigation, only the plaintiff's knowledge (not consent) is needed.

Key Terms
عقد رهن (aqd al-rahn): The contract of pledge; a security contract where property is held as collateral for a debt.
وکالت مشروطہ (wakalah mashrutah): Agency that is stipulated as a condition within another contract, here the pledge contract.
معزول (ma'zul): Dismissed or removed from the position of agent.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the effect of stipulating the agency in the pledge contract?
A) The agency becomes revocable at will by the rahin.
B) The agency becomes binding and cannot be revoked without the murtahin's consent.
C) The agency is invalid because it conflicts with the pledge.
D) The agency becomes a separate contract independent of the pledge.

Key Takeaway
Agency stipulated in a pledge contract is binding and cannot be revoked without the pledgee's consent because it becomes a right of the pledgee and an attribute of the pledge contract.

Absolute Agency for Sale: The Ineffective Prohibition
Ruling on absolute agency and effect of subsequent prohibition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling that an absolute agency for sale includes both cash and credit, and explain why a principal's later prohibition on credit sales is ineffective.

Core Idea
An absolute agency binds the principal; subsequent restrictions are legally ineffective.

This lesson examines a specific ruling from the Hanafi school regarding agency in the context of a pledged property (rahn). Even if the principal later tries to restrict the agent from selling on credit, that prohibition carries no legal weight. Understanding this principle is essential for grasping the binding nature of absolute agency in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its context
The passage concerns a rahin (pledgor) who appoints an agent to sell the pledged item. The agency is granted absolutely (mutlaq), meaning no restrictions are placed on the mode of sale.
Absolute agency covers both cash (naqd) and credit (nasi'ah) sales.
2
State the ruling
If the rahin later prohibits the agent from selling on credit, that prohibition is not effective (lam ya'mal nahyuhu). The agent retains the authority to sell on credit.
The prohibition does not revoke or limit the existing authority.
3
Understand the reasoning
The agency is binding by its origin (lazim bi aslihi) and by its description (bi wasfihi). Since the grant was absolute, the principal cannot unilaterally alter its scope after the fact.
This builds on the principle that a binding agency cannot be revoked by the principal without cause.
4
Apply to analogous cases
The same ruling applies to any absolute agency for sale outside of rahn. If the principal grants absolute authority, subsequent restrictions are ineffective.
The underlying principle is general to the law of agency (wakalah).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
راہوں کا مطلقاً بیچ کا وکیل بنانے کا حکم
ولو وكله بالبيع مطلقا حتى ملك البيع بالنقد والنسيئة ثم نهاه عن البيع نيسئة لم يعمل نهيه لانه لازم با صله فكذا بوصفه لما ذكرناه
The ruling of the rahin appointing an agent absolutely for sale. And if he appoints him absolutely for sale, so that he has the right to sell for cash or on credit, then he prohibits him from selling on credit; his prohibition is not effective, because it is binding by its origin, and likewise by its description, for what we have mentioned.
Source pages p. 263

Commentary
This passage is a concise ruling_statement from the Hanafi school. It deals with the case where the rahin appoints an agent with absolute authority to sell the pledge—meaning the agent may sell for cash or on credit. If the rahin later tries to restrict the agent by prohibiting credit sales, that prohibition has no effect. The reasoning is that the agency is binding in its origin (since it was absolute) and also in its description (the authority to sell on credit is part of the absolute grant). The agent's authority remains intact; the rahin cannot unilaterally alter the scope of a binding agency. This builds on the previous lesson's principle that agency can become irrevocable.

Key Terms
بيع مطلقا (bay' mutlaqan): An absolute authorization to sell, without specifying terms, thus including both cash and credit.
نقد و نسیئہ (naqd wa nasi'ah): Cash and credit sale; two modes of sale.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a rahin appoints an agent with absolute authority to sell the pledge, and later prohibits him from selling on credit, what happens?
A) The agent must obey the prohibition.
B) The prohibition is ineffective because the agency is binding in its scope.
C) The agent may only sell for cash.
D) The agency is automatically revoked.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, an absolute agency for sale binds the principal, and a subsequent prohibition on credit sales is legally ineffective.

Appointing an Agent to Sell Pledged Property upon Maturity
States the ruling on agency for selling pledged property upon maturity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the permissibility of appointing the pledgee or any other person as agent to sell the pledged property upon debt maturity and explain the legal basis for this ruling.

Core Idea
A pledgor retains ownership of the pawned item and may authorize any agent—including the pledgee—to sell it when the debt matures.

When property is pledged as collateral for a debt, ownership remains with the pledgor. A key question is whether the pledgor can authorize the pledgee or another person to sell the property when the debt falls due. This lesson examines the ruling from the matn of Quduri and clarifies the Hanafi position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and act
The pledgor (rahin) appoints an agent (the pledgee, a just person, or someone else) to sell the pawned item (marhun) when the debt matures.
2
Determine the legal question
Is it valid for a pledgor to appoint an agent to sell the pawned property upon debt maturity?
3
State the ruling
The agency is permissible (ja'iz) according to Quduri.
4
Explain the reasoning
The property belongs to the pledgor, so appointing an agent to sell it is akin to any ordinary sale agency. There is no prohibition.
5
Note cross-madhhab consideration
Some other schools may restrict this due to perceived conflict of interest, but Hanafis allow it based on ownership.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور جبکہ راہن نے مرتہن یا عادل یا ان دونوں کے غیر کو مرہون کی مبیع کا وکیل بنایا ہوادائیگی دین کا وقت آنے پر تو وکالت جائز ہے اس لئے کہ یہ جائز اپنے مال کی بیع کا وکیل بنانا ہے۔ تشریح راہن نے اگر کسی کوبھی وکیل بنا دیا کہ جب ادا دین کا وقت آ جائے تو مرہون کو فروخت کر کے قرض ادا کر دے تو چونکہ یہ اپنے مال کی بیع کا وکیل بنانا ہے لہذا اس کے جواز میں شبہ نہیں ہے۔
Translation: Quduri said: And when the pledgor appoints the pledgee or a just person or someone else as agent for the sale of the pledged property when the time for payment of the debt arrives, then the agency is permissible because it is appointing an agent to sell his own property. Explanation: If the pledgor appoints anyone as agent to sell the pledged property when the time for payment arrives and repay the debt, then since this is appointing an agent to sell his own property, there is no doubt about its permissibility.
Source pages p. 263

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from the matn of Quduri. It addresses a scenario where the pledgor (rahin) appoints the pledgee (murtahin), a just person ('adl), or someone else as an agent to sell the mortgaged property when the debt matures. The author declares this agency valid because it is simply appointing an agent to sell one's own property. The essence is that the pledgor retains ownership of the pawned item, so he may authorize its sale. The commentary reinforces that there is no legal impediment since it is akin to any ordinary sale agency.

Key Terms
وکالت (wakālah): Agency, the act of appointing someone to act on one's behalf in a legal transaction.
رہن (rahn): Pledge, mortgage, collateral for a debt.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Quduri, what is the ruling on a pledgor appointing the pledgee as agent to sell the pledged property upon maturity?
A) It is not permissible because the pledgee has a conflicting interest.
B) It is permissible because the pledgor is selling his own property.
C) It is only permissible if the agent is a just person.
D) It is makruh.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits a pledgor to appoint any person, including the pledgee, as agent to sell the pawned property upon debt maturity because the pledgor retains ownership.

The Binding Agency Stipulated in the Pledge Contract
Ruling with proof on binding agency in pledge contract

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on agency stipulated in a pledge contract and explain the two proofs (qiyas) that establish its binding nature.

Core Idea
Agency stipulated in a pledge becomes a right of the pledgee, making dismissal ineffective.

In Hanafi fiqh, not all agencies are revocable. When an agency is stipulated as part of a binding contract like a pledge (rahn), it takes on a binding character. This lesson unpacks the ruling and the careful qiyas that supports it, showing how the pledgee's right becomes attached to the agent's appointment.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its condition
Note that the ruling only applies when agency is stipulated within the pledge contract itself (shart fi al-rahn). Outside this, agency is generally revocable.
2
Trace the first proof: agency as a description of the pledge
The agency becomes a description (wasf) of the pledge, like a feature that strengthens security. Since the pledge is binding, its description is also binding.
This is qiyas jali: the character of the principal transfers to the accessory.
3
Trace the second proof: the pledgee's attached right
The pledgee (murtahin) has a right (haqq) linked to the agency through the stipulation. Dismissing the agent would destroy that right, which is impermissible.
This is qiyas khafi, also analogized to agency in litigation.
4
Compare with agency in litigation (wakil bi al-khusuma)
Just as a defendant, after appointing an agent at the plaintiff's request, cannot dismiss without the plaintiff's knowledge, so here the pledgor cannot dismiss without the pledgee's consent.
Distinction: in rahn, consent is needed; in litigation, only knowledge suffices.
5
State the practical consequence
If the pledgor attempts to dismiss, the dismissal is ineffective; the agent continues to act. This protects the pledgee's interest.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وکالت کی عقد رہن میں شرط ہو تو راہن وکیل کو معزول نہیں کر سکتا كے وان شرطت في عقد الرهن فليس للراهن ان يعزل الوكيل وان عزله لم ينعزل لانها لما شرطت في ضمن عقد الرهن صار وصفا من اوصافه وحقا من حقوقه الأترى انه لزيادة الوثيقة فيلزم بلزوم اصله ولانه تعلق به حق المرتهن وفى العزل اتو أحقه وصار كالوكيل بالخصومة بطلب المدعى ترجمہ اور اگر وکالت عقد ر ہن میں مشروط ہوئی ہو تو را ہن کو یہ حق نہیں کہ وہ وکیل کو معزول کر دے اور اگر اس کو معزول کر دیا تو وہ معزول نہ ہوگا اس لئے کہ وکالت جب عقد رهن کے ضمن میں مشروط ہو تو وہ رہن کے اوصاف میں سے ایک وصف اور اس کے حقوق میں سے ایک حق ہو گیا کیا آپ نہیں دیکھتے کہ عقد وکالت مضبوطی کی زیادتی کے لئے ہے تو عقد وکالت اپنی اصل ( رہن زد سے لازم ہو جائیگا اور اس لئے کہ عقد وکالت کے ساتھ مرتہن کا حق وابستہ ہو گیا ہے اور عزل میں اس کے حق کو ہلاک کرنا ہے اور یہ مدعی کی طلب پر وکیل بالخصومت کے مثل ہو گیا ۔ تشریح بدایہ کے ص ۵۱۸ ج ۴ پر امام زفر کی دلیل میں یہ مسئلہ گذر چکا ہے جہاں انہوں نے کہا تھا کالو كالة المشروطة في الرهن فیلزمہ بلزومہ ۔ جس کا خلاصہ یہ ہے کہ اگر عقد ر ہن میں وکالت مشروط ہوگئی ہو تو اب وہ لازم ہو جائے گی لہذا اگر راہن چاہے کہ وکیل کو معزول کر دوں تو نہیں کر سکتا اور اگر کرے تو وکیل معزول نہ ہوگا کیونکہ اب وکالت حقوق عقد ر ہن میں سے ایک حق ہو چکا ہے جو رہن کے لزوم کی وجہ سے لا زم ہو جائے گی کیونکہ وکالت کی شرط کا مقصد پختگی کی زیادتی ہے اور دوسری وجہ یہ بھی ہے کہ اب اس سے مرتبہن کا حق متعلق ہو چکا ہے اور عزل وکیل میں حق مرتہن کا ابطال ہے جس کا راہن کو حق نہیں ہے۔ اور اس کی مثال بالکل ایسی ہے کہ مدعی نے مدعی علیہ سے مطالبہ کیا کہ عدالت میں جواہد ہی کے لئے کسی کو وکیل بنائے جس پر مدعی علیہ نے کسی کو وکیل بنا دیا تو اب مدعی علیہ کو حق نہ ہوگا مامی علم کے بغیر وکیل کو معزول کر دے اس لئے کہ اس کے ساتھ مدعی کا حق وابستہ ہو گیا ہے اسی طرح وکیل رہن سے بھی مرتبہن کا حق متعلق ہو چکا ہے لیکن ان دونوں میں اتنا اتفاق ہے کہ رہن کی صورت میں راہن کو عزل وکیل کا حق صرف جب ہوگا کہ مرتین راضی ہو جائے اور وکیل بالخصومت میں رضاء مدعی ضروری نہیں بلکہ اس کا علم ضروری ہے۔
And if the agency is stipulated in the pledge contract, then the pledgor has no right to dismiss the agent; and if he dismisses him, he is not dismissed because when the agency is stipulated within the pledge contract, it becomes a description of its descriptions and a right of its rights. Do you not see that it is for increasing the security, so it becomes binding by the binding of its origin, and because the right of the pledgee is attached to it, and in dismissal there is destruction of his right. And it becomes like the agent in litigation at the request of the plaintiff. Translation: And if the agency is stipulated in the pledge contract, then the pledgor has no right to dismiss the agent; and if he dismisses him, he is not dismissed because when the agency is stipulated within the pledge contract, it becomes a description of its descriptions and a right of its rights. Do you not see that it is for increasing the security, so it becomes binding by the binding of its origin, and because the right of the pledgee is attached to it, and in dismissal there is destruction of his right. And it becomes like the agent in litigation at the request of the plaintiff. Explanation: This issue has passed in the proof of Imam Zufar on page 518 volume 4 of al-Bidayah, where he said: 'The agency stipulated in the pledge is binding by its binding.' The summary is that if the agency is stipulated in the pledge contract, then it becomes binding. So if the pledgor wishes to dismiss the agent, he cannot; and if he does, the agent is not dismissed, because now the agency has become one of the rights of the pledge contract, which becomes binding due to the binding of the pledge, because the purpose of the condition of agency is to increase firmness. And a second reason is that the right of the pledgee has become attached to it, and dismissing the agent nullifies the pledgee's right, which the pledgor has no right to do. And its example is exactly like the case where a plaintiff demands from the defendant that he appoint someone as agent for the case in court, and the defendant appoints someone - then the defendant does not have the right to dismiss the agent without the knowledge of the plaintiff, because the plaintiff's right has become attached to it. Similarly, with the agent in rahn, the pledgee's right has become attached. But there is this difference: in the case of rahn, the pledgor may dismiss the agent only if the pledgee agrees; whereas in the agent in litigation, the consent of the plaintiff is not necessary, rather his knowledge is necessary.
Source pages p. 263

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof concerning agency stipulated within the pledge contract. The author presents the ruling: if the pledgor (rahin) stipulates the agency in the pledge contract, he cannot later dismiss the agent; and if he attempts to dismiss, it is ineffective. The proof is twofold: (1) The agency becomes an inseparable description and right of the pledge contract, so it is binding just as the pledge itself is binding (qiyas to the binding nature of the pledge). (2) The pledgee's right (haqq al-murtahin) has become attached to this agency through the stipulation; dismissing the agent would destroy that right, which is impermissible. The author draws an analogy to agency in litigation (wakālah bi al-khuṣūmah) where, after the defendant appoints an agent at the plaintiff's request, the defendant cannot dismiss the agent without the plaintiff's knowledge because the plaintiff's right is attached. However, a distinction is noted: in rahn, the pledgor may dismiss only with the pledgee's consent, while in litigation, the plaintiff's knowledge (not necessarily consent) suffices.

Key Terms
عزل (ʿazl): Dismissal of an agent; removal from agency.
وکیل بالخصومة (wakīl bi al-khuṣūmah): Agent appointed for litigation, specifically at the request of the plaintiff.
رھن (rahn): Pledge; a contract where property is given as security for a debt.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the primary reason the agency stipulated in a pledge contract becomes binding?
A) Because the agent must be paid.
B) Because the agency becomes a description and right of the binding pledge, with the pledgee's right attached.
C) Because the pledgor cannot change his mind after signing.
D) Because the pledge contract is invalid without an agent.

Key Takeaway
Agency stipulated in a pledge contract is binding (lazim) because it becomes an inseparable part of the pledge, protecting the pledgee's right.

The Binding Nature of Absolute Agency in Rahn
Extends the binding nature of agency to its details.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that an absolute agency in rahn is binding and explain why the pledgor cannot later restrict the agent to a cash-only sale.

Core Idea
An absolute agency in rahn is binding in its entirety; later restrictions are ineffective.

In this lesson, we examine a specific ruling from the Hanafi school regarding agency in a pledge contract. The passage extends the binding nature of the agency to the method of sale. You will learn why, once an absolute agency is granted, the pledgor cannot later prohibit credit sales, and how this follows from the principle that the pledge contract itself is binding.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
State the explicit ruling: if a pledgor appoints an agent absolutely for sale, the agent has authority to sell for cash or credit. If the pledgor later forbids credit sales, his prohibition is ineffective.
2
Locate the proof (dalil)
The proof is the principle that the pledge contract is binding in its origin. Since the agency is stipulated in a binding contract, it too is binding. The commentary says: 'the pledge contract is binding in its origin, so similarly it is binding in its description.'
The proof is a qiyas khafi: analogy from the binding nature of the contract to the binding nature of its attributes.
3
Understand the qiyas reasoning
The underlying analogy: just as the original agency (the origin) is binding, its descriptions (like the power to sell for cash or credit) are also binding. The description is treated as following the origin in binding force.
This is a qiyas khafi (subtle analogy) because the binding of the description is not explicit but derived from the binding of the origin.
4
Note the cross-madhhab ikhtilaf
Other schools may allow the principal to restrict the agent after appointment. The Hanafi position insists on the binding nature as a lazim (binding) contract, preventing such restriction.
This difference arises from different views on the binding nature of agency in pledge.
5
Apply the principle
Consider a scenario where the pledgor later changes his mind. According to Hanafi fiqh, the agent's authority remains intact. This reinforces the importance of clarity at the time of appointment.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
راہوں کا مطلقاً بیچ کا وکیل بنانے کا حکم ولو وكله بالبيع مطلقا حتى ملك البيع بالنقد والنسيئة ثم نهاه عن البيع نيسئة لم يعمل نهيه لانه لازم با صله فكذا بوصفه لما ذكرناه ترجمہ اور اگر راہن نے اس کو (یعنی تینوں میں سے کسی کو ) مطلق بیع کا وکیل بنایا یہاں تک کہ وکیل نفذ اور ادھار بیع کا مالک ہو گیا پھر راہن نے وکیل کو ادھار بیچ سے منع کر دیا تو اس کا منع کرنا کارگر نہ ہوگا اس لئے کہ عقد ر ہن اپنی اصل سے لازم ہے پس ایسے ہی اپنے وصف کے ساتھ ( لا زم ہوگا ) اسی دلیل کی وجہ سے جس کو ہم ذکر کر چکے ہیں۔ تشریح ابھی معلوم ہوا کہ مقدر بن میں میں وکالت کی شرط ہوئی ہو وہ لازم ہو جاتی ہے تو جب اصل وکالت لازم ہوگی تو اس کے اوصاف بھی لازم ہوں گے کیونکہ وصف بھی اصل کے مثل حقوق رہن میں سے شمار کیا جائیگا۔ لہذا اگر راہن نے مطلقا وکیل بنایا تھا جس میں نقد اور ادھار کی کوئی تعیین نہیں تھی تو وکیل کو حق حاصل ہو چکا تھا خواہ نقد بیچے خواہ ادھار لیکن بعد میں راہن ادھار بیچنے سے منع کرتا ہے تو اب اس کا منع کرنا کچھ کارگر نہ ہوگا کیونکہ اصل کے لازم ہونے سے وصف بھی لازم ہو جائیگا اور وصف میں اطلاق برقرار رہے گا۔
The ruling on the pledgor appointing an agent absolutely. And if he appointed him absolutely for sale, such that the agent owned the sale for cash and credit, then the pledgor forbade him from selling on credit, his prohibition is not effective because it is binding by its origin, and likewise by its description due to what we mentioned. Translation: And if the pledgor appointed him (i.e., one of the three) as agent for sale absolutely, such that the agent became entitled to sell for cash or credit, then the pledgor forbade him from selling on credit, his prohibition is not effective because the pledge contract is binding in its origin, so similarly it is binding in its description for the same reason we mentioned. Explanation: It is now known that if agency is stipulated in the pledge contract, it becomes binding. So when the original agency is binding, its descriptions are also binding, because the description is also counted among the rights of the pledge like the origin. Therefore, if the pledgor appointed an agent absolutely without specifying cash or credit, the agent had the right to sell either way. Later, if the pledgor forbids credit sale, his prohibition is ineffective because the binding of the origin causes the description to also be binding, and the absolute nature remains.
Source pages p. 263

Commentary
This ruling extends the principle of binding agency to the details of the sale. Since the agency is binding, all its attributes (like the power to sell for cash or credit) are also binding. Thus, if the pledgor initially grants absolute authority, he cannot later restrict the agent to cash sales only. The commentary clarifies that the binding nature of the origin (the agency) necessitates that its descriptions are also binding, so the agent retains the full authority originally granted.

Key Terms
مطلق (muṭlaq): Absolute, unrestricted; here referring to agency without specification of cash or credit.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) Only if the debt is not yet due.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, an absolute agency in a pledge contract is binding in all its aspects, and the pledgor cannot later restrict the agent's method of sale.

The Pledgee Cannot Dismiss the Agent
States that the pledgee cannot dismiss the agent because he is not the principal.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that the pledgee cannot dismiss the agent and explain the a fortiori reasoning.

Core Idea
Only the principal can dismiss an agent; the pledgee lacks authority.

In the previous lesson, we learned that the agency (wakala) in rahn is binding (lazim) on the pledgor. This ruling now clarifies that even the pledgee (murtahin) has no power to dismiss the agent, because he is not the principal. The commentary uses an a fortiori argument: if the principal cannot dismiss, then the pledgee certainly cannot.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is the pledgee dismissing the agent. The hanafi ruling is that the dismissal is ineffective; the agent remains appointed.
The source states: 'if the pledgee dismisses him, he is not dismissed'.
2
Understand the reason
The pledgee did not appoint the agent; only the person who appointed (the principal) can dismiss. Since the pledgee is not the principal, he has no authority.
Key term: muwakkil (principal).
3
Apply a fortiori reasoning
Since even the pledgor (the principal) cannot dismiss the agent because the agency is binding, then the pledgee, who has even less right, certainly cannot.
This is qiyas awla (a minore ad maius).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مرتہن وکیل کو معزول کر سکتا ہے یا نہیں وكذا اذا عزله المرتهن لا ينعزل لانه لم يوكله وإنما وكله غيره ترجمہ اور ایسے ہی جبکہ وکیل کو مرتین معزول کرے وہ معزول نہ ہو گا اس لئے اس کو مرتہن نے وکیل نہیں بنایا بلکہ اس کو اس کے غیر نے وکیل بنایا ہے۔ تشریح جب راہن کے عزل سے وکیل معزول نہیں ہوتا جو مؤکل ہے تو مرتہن کے عزل سے بڑجہ اولی معزول نہ ہوگا کیونکہ مرتہن موکل نہیں ہے۔
Can the pledgee dismiss the agent? And similarly, if the pledgee dismisses him, he is not dismissed, because he (the pledgee) did not appoint him; rather, someone else appointed him. Translation: And similarly, if the pledgee dismisses the agent, he is not dismissed, because the pledgee did not appoint him; rather, someone else appointed him. Explanation: Since the agent is not dismissed by the dismissal of the pledgor, who is the principal, then by greater reason he is not dismissed by the dismissal of the pledgee, who is not the principal.
Source pages p. 264

Commentary
This is a short ruling that logically follows from the previous: since the agency is binding, and the pledgee is not the principal, he cannot dismiss the agent. The commentary uses the principle of a minore ad maius (a fortiori): if the pledgor (the principal) cannot dismiss, the pledgee certainly cannot.

Key Terms
موکل (muwakkil): Principal who appoints an agent.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) Yes, if the agent is negligent.

Key Takeaway
The pledgee cannot dismiss the agent because he is not the principal, and even the principal cannot dismiss in a binding agency.

Agency in Pledge Not Terminated by Pledgor's Death
Rules that the death of the pledgor does not terminate the agency.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the effect of the pledgor's death on agency and explain the legal reasoning (talil) that supports it.

Core Idea
The death of the pledgor does not void the agency because the pledgee's right in the pledged property outranks the heirs' right.

The general principle in agency (wakalah) is that the death of the principal (muwakkil) terminates the agent's authority. However, when the agency is tied to a binding contract like rahn (pledge), the Hanafi school maintains that the agency survives the pledgor's death. This lesson examines the ruling and its underlying reasoning as presented in the source text.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
State explicitly what the Hanafi position is: the agent (wakeel) is not dismissed when the pledgor (rahin) dies. The Arabic phrase used is 'lam yan'azil'.
2
Recall the General Principle
Normally, agency terminates upon the death of the principal because ownership transfers to the heirs. Note that this is the baseline rule from which the current ruling is an exception.
3
Examine the First Reason
The pledge contract (rahn) itself is not invalidated by the death of the pledgor. Therefore, the rights and obligations originating from the pledge remain intact, including the agency that is part of its execution.
The text says: 'la yabtul bi mawtihi' – it is not voided by his death.
4
Examine the Second Reason
Even if one were to argue that agency should end, it would be due to the right of the heirs (since ownership passes to them). However, the pledgee's right (haqq al-murtahin) is prior to the heirs' right. Thus, the heirs cannot terminate the agency because their claim is subordinate.
The text uses the term 'muqaddam' (prior) to describe the pledgee's right.
5
Conclude
Combine both reasons: the pledge contract continues, and the pledgee's right trumps the heirs' right. Therefore, the agent's authority remains valid until the pledge is fully discharged.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
راہن کی موت پر وکیل معزول نہیں ہوگا وان مات الراهن لم ينعزل لان الرهن لا يبطل بموته ولانه لو بطل انما يبطل لحق الورثة وحق المرتهن مقدم ترجمہ اور اگر راہن مر گیا تو وکیل معزول نہ ہو گا اس لئے کہ راہن کے مرنے سے رہن باطل نہیں ہوتا اور اس لئے کہ اگر وکالت باطل تشریح جس طرح مذکورہ دونوں صورتوں میں وکیل معزول نہیں ہوتا اسی طرح راہن کی موت سے بھی معزول نہ ہوگا کیونکہ راہن کی موت سے رہن بھی باطل نہیں ہوتا تو حقوق رہن بھی باطل نہ ہوں گے ۔ اور مؤکل کی موت سے وکالت جہاں بھی باطل ہوتی ہے حق ورغلا کی وجہ سے ہوتی ہے کیونکہ ملکیت ورثا کی جانب منتقل ہو جاتی ہے مگر یہاں یہ بھی نہیں ہوسکتا کیونکہ مرتہن کا حق در خلو پر مقدم ہے ۔
And if the pledgor dies, he (the agent) is not dismissed, because the pledge is not invalidated by his death, and because if it were invalidated, it would only be invalidated for the right of the heirs, and the right of the pledgee is prior. Explanation: Just as in the two mentioned cases the agent is not dismissed, similarly he is not dismissed by the death of the pledgor, because the death of the pledgor does not invalidate the pledge, so the rights of the pledge are not invalidated. And wherever agency is invalidated by the death of the principal, it is only due to the right of the heirs, because ownership transfers to them. But here that cannot happen because the pledgee's right is prior over the right of the heirs.
Source pages p. 264

Commentary
This ruling clarifies that the death of the pledgor does not end the agency, because the pledge contract itself is not voided by death. The agency is a right of the pledgee that survives the pledgor's death. The commentary explains that normally agency ends with the death of the principal due to transfer of ownership to heirs, but here the pledgee's right takes precedence over the heirs' right.

Key Terms
ورثہ (wurathā): Heirs of the deceased pledgor.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What happens to the agency when the pledgor dies?
A) The agency terminates automatically.
B) The agency continues because the pledge is not invalidated by death.
C) The agency terminates only if the pledgee dies also.
D) The agent must seek permission from the heirs.

Key Takeaway
The death of the pledgor does not terminate the agency in a pledge because the pledge contract survives death and the pledgee's right is prior to the heirs' right.

Agent May Sell Without Heirs and Agency Continues After Pledgee's Death
Ruling with reason on agent's continued authority

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that the agent for sale of pledged property may sell without the heirs' presence and explain why the agency continues after the pledgee's death based on the contract's persistence.

Core Idea
The pledge contract survives death of either party; thus the agency to sell remains intact.

We have already learned that an agent appointed to sell a pledged property has the authority to execute the sale during the pledgor's life. Now the text extends that authority in two ways: first, the agent may sell even if the pledgor's heirs are not present; second, the death of the pledgee does not terminate the agency. The underlying reason is that the pledge contract itself is not extinguished by the death of either the pledgor or the pledgee, so its rights and descriptions—including the agency—persist.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two rulings
Read the text carefully and separate the two distinct legal rulings: (a) the agent may sell the pledge without the presence of the heirs; (b) if the pledgee dies, the agent remains on his agency.
The text links them with 'and' (وان).
2
Trace the legal reasoning (talil)
The text provides a reason: 'because the contract is not nullified by the death of either of them, nor by the death of one of them, so it remains with its rights and descriptions.' Identify why the contract's survival implies the agency's survival.
The agency is a right (haqq) and description (wasf) of the pledge contract.
3
Understand the scope
The ruling applies whether the pledgor or pledgee dies. The agent's authority is not dependent on the presence of the pledgor's heirs because the original appointment came from the pledgee, not from the pledgor or his heirs.
Heirs inherit the pledged property but not the right to revoke the agency unilaterally.
4
Contrast with a possible objection
Some might think that the agency ends upon the death of the pledgee (the principal). The Hanafi position refutes this because the pledge contract itself remains valid, so the agency attached to it remains.
This is based on the principle that rights arising from a valid contract survive the death of the parties.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وکیل در خاکی عدم موجودگی میں بھی رہن کو بیچ سکتا ہے قال وللوكيل ان يبيعه بغير محضر من الورثة كما يبيعه في حال حياته بغير محضر منه وان مات المرتهن فالوكيل على وكالته لان العقد لايطل بموتهما ولا بموت احدهما فيبقى بحقوقه واوصافه
The agent can sell the pledge even in the absence of the heirs, just as he sold it during his (the pledgor's) life without his presence. And if the pledgee dies, the agent remains on his agency, because the contract is not nullified by the death of either of them, nor by the death of one of them, so it remains with its rights and descriptions.
Source pages p. 264

Commentary
This final ruling addresses two scenarios. First, the agent may sell the pledged property even if the heirs of the pledgor are not present, just as he could during the pledgor's life without his presence. This reinforces that the agent's authority is independent of the heirs' presence. Second, the death of the pledgee does not terminate the agency, because the pledge contract is not voided by the death of either party. The agency, being a right of the contract, persists with all its rights and descriptions.

Key Terms
ورثة (wuratha): Heirs of the pledgor.
مرتهن (murtahin): Pledgee (creditor) who holds the pledge and appoints the agent.
وكيل (wakil): Agent appointed by the pledgee to sell the pledged property.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) The agent must be reappointed by the heirs of the pledgee.
C) The agency continues because the pledge contract remains valid.
D) The agency terminates only if the pledgor also dies.

Key Takeaway
The agent's authority to sell the pledge is independent of the heirs' presence and survives the pledgee's death because the pledge contract itself remains valid.
