Agent's Death in Pledge: Does the Executor Succeed?
Intra-Hanafi dispute on agency succession in rahn

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between rights binding upon a person and rights for a person, and apply that distinction to determine whether the agent's executor inherits the authority to sell the pawn.

Core Idea
Agency is personal; the principal trusts the agent, not his heir—so upon death, the agency ends.

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses a critical question: when an agent appointed to sell a pawn dies, does his executor step into his shoes? The majority of the Hanafi school (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) says no, while Imam Abu Yusuf argues yes, drawing an analogy to mudaraba. Understanding the underlying distinction between rights that are 'upon' a person and rights that are 'for' a person is key to grasping the Hanafi position.

Guided Path
1
State the majority Hanafi position
Identify the rule: upon the agent's death, the agency is annulled; neither heir nor executor stands in his place.
This is the mufta bihi position.
2
Identify Abu Yusuf's opposing view and his analogy
Abu Yusuf holds that the executor may sell the pawn because the agency is binding, analogous to mudaraba where the executor may sell goods after the mudarib's death.
The key analogy: binding contract → executor succeeds.
3
Follow the Hanafi response to the analogy
The response distinguishes: agency is binding upon the agent (lazim 'alayh), not for him, whereas mudaraba is the mudarib's right (for him). Inheritance applies to what is for a person, not to what is upon him.
This is a textual and rational distinction.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: under Abu Yusuf, the executor could sell the pawn; under the majority, the pawn remains unsold until a new agent is appointed.
This affects the rights of the pledgor's heirs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تشریح راہن کی حیات میں وکیل کے لئے جائز تھا کہ راہن کی عدم موجودگی میں مرہون کو فروخت کر دے لہذا راہن کی موت کے بعد بھی اس کو یہ حق حاصل رہیگا کہ ورثلہ کی عدم موجودگی میں مرہون کو فروخت کر دے اور اگر بجائے راہن کے مرتبین مرجائے تب بھی وکیل وکالت برقرار ہے کیونکہ ان دونوں کے یا کسی ایک کے مرنے سے عقد رہن باطل نہیں ہوتا تو اس کے حقوق و اوصاف بھی باطل نہ ہوں گے۔
تنبیہ حقوق سے مراد جبس و استیفاء اور وکالت ہے اور اوصاف سے مرا دلار دوم عقد وغیرہ ہے۔
وکیل کے مرنے سے وکالت ختم ہو جائیگی وکیل کا وارث یا وصی قائم مقام نہ ہوگا
وان مات الوكيل انتقضت الوكالة ولا يقوم وارثه ولا وصيه مقامه لان الوكالة لا يجرى فيها الارث ولان الموكل رضى برايه ولا برأى غيره وعن ابى يوسف ان وضى الوکيل يملك بيعه لان الوكالة لا زمة فيملكه الوصى كالمضارب اذامات بعد ما صار رأس المال اعيانا يملك وصى المضارب بيعها لما انه لازم بعد ماصار اعیانا قلنا التوكيل حق لازم لكن عليه والارث يجرى فى ماله بخلاف المضاربة لانها حق المضارب
ترجمہ اور اگر وکیل مرگیا تو وکالت ختم ہوگئی اور وکیل کا وارث یا اس کا وھی اس کے قائم مقام نہ ہو گا اس لئے کہ وکالت میں ارث جاری نہیں ہوتا اور اس لئے کہ موکل وکیل کی رائے سے راضی تھا نہ کہ اس کے غیر کی رائے سے اور ابو یوسف سے منقول ہے کہ وکیل کا وصی مرہون کو بیچنے کا مالک ہو گا اس لئے کہ و کالریعے لازم ہے تو وہی اس کا مالک ہوگا جیسے جب مضارب مرجائے راس المال کے اعیان ہو نیچے ہوگا لئے کہ کا ہو جانے کے بعد عقد مضاربت لازم ہے۔ ہم جواب دیں گے کہ توکیل حق لازم ہے لیکن وکیل کے اوپر اور میراث ان چیزوں میں جاری ہوتی ہے جو اس کے لئے ہوں بخلاف مضاربت کے اس لئے کہ وہ مضارب کا حق ہے۔
تشریح اولا دو باتیں ذہن نشین کیجئے :- بعض امور وہ ہوتے ہیں جس میں کسی شخص پر وجوب ہوتا ہے منفعت نہیں ہوتی اور بعض امور وہ ہوتے ہیں جس میں منفعت ہوتی ہے بالفاظ دیگر کبھی اپنے اوپر لزوم ہوتا ہے اور کبھی اپنے لئے دوسرے پر لزوم ہوتا ہے اول کی مثال وکالت ہے اور ثانی کی مضاربت ہے بہر حال اس میں یہ بتانا ہے پہلی قسم میں میراث جاری نہ ہوگی اور دوسری قسم میں میراث جاری ہوگی جیسے اگر میت کے اوپر قرض ہو تو اس کے ورثاو پر اس کو ادا کرنا واجب نہیں ہے اور اگر میت کا کسی کے اوپر قرض ہو تو ورثا اس کے وارث ہوں گے۔
- توکیل کا مقصد یہ ہوتا ہے کہ موکل وکیل کی دانائی سے فائدہ حاصل کرتا ہے اور ہر آدمی کی سمجھ بوجھ جدا جدا ہوتی ہے لہذا اگر کسی نے
زید کو وکیل بنایا اس کا مطلب یہ نہ ہو گا کہ مؤکل نے زید کے بیٹے پر بھی اعتماد کر لیا ہے لہذا مصنف یہ کہنا چاہتے ہیں کہ مرہون کی بیچ کے وکیل کا انتقال ہو گیا تو اب وکالت ختم ہو جائے گی اور چونکہ وکالت میں میراث نہیں چلتی لہذا وکیل کا وسی یا وارث اس کا قائم مقام ہو کر وکیل شمار نہیں کیا جائے گا ۔ نیز موکل نے وکیل مرحوم پر اعتماد کیا ہے اور اس کی رائے سے راضی ہوا ہے نہ کہ اس کے وصی یا بیٹے پر امام ابو یوسف" سے منقول ہے کہ وکیل کی موت کے بعد اس کا وصی اسکا قائم مقام ہوگا اور وصی کو حق ہوگا کہ مرہون کو فروخت کرے کیونکہ حسب تصریح سابق یہ وکالت لازم تھی جس کو فتح نہیں کیا جاسکتا ہے لہذا وصی بیچ مرہون کا مالک ہوگا۔ امام ابو یوسف نے اس کو مضارب کے ایک مسئلہ پیر قبلیس کیا ہے کہ اگر مضارب راس المال سے سامان خرید چکا ہے یعنی اب رأس المال نہیں بلکہ وہ اشیاء موجود ہیں جو راس المال سے خریدی گئی ہیں کہ مضارب کا انتقال ہو گیا تو مضارب کے وصی کو حق ہوتا ہے کہ ان اشیاء کو فروخت کر دے یہاں بھی وجہ یہی ہے کہ عقد مضاربت رأس المال کے اعیان بننے کے بعد لازم ہو جاتا ہے لہذا وکالت بھی لازم ہے تو اسمیں بھی وصی وکیل کا قائم ہو گا اور مرہون کو فروخت کرنے کا مالک ہوگا۔ تو امام ابو یوسف کو جواب دیا کہ ہاں وکالت لازم تو ہے مگر وکیل پر حق لازم ہے نہ کہ وکیل کیلئے لہذا مقدمہ اولی کے مطابق آسمیں میراث جاری نہ ہوگی اور اس کو مضاربت پر قیاس کرنا درست نہ ہوگا کیونکہ وکالت از قسم اول ہے اور مضاربت از قسم ثانی جس کو مصنف نے یوں تعبیر کیا ہے کہ مضاربت مضارب کا حق ہے۔
Explanation: During the pledgor's life, it was permissible for the agent to sell the pawn in the absence of the pledgor. So after the pledgor's death, he still has this right to sell the pawn in the absence of the heirs. And if instead of the pledgor, the mortgagee dies, then also the agency remains valid because the pledge contract is not invalidated by the death of either of them, so its rights and attributes are not invalidated. Warning: By rights are meant possession, collection, and agency; and by attributes are meant the second condition, contract, etc. The agent's death terminates the agency; his heir or executor will not stand in his place. And if the agent dies, the agency is annulled, and his heir or executor does not stand in his place because inheritance does not apply in agency, and because the principal was satisfied with his opinion and not with another's. And from Abu Yusuf: that the agent's executor owns its sale because the agency is binding, so the executor owns it like the mudarib when he dies after the capital has become specific goods, the executor of the mudarib owns their sale because it becomes binding after becoming specific goods. We said: The appointment of agency is a binding right, but upon him (the agent), and inheritance applies to his property, unlike mudaraba because it is the right of the mudarib. Translation: And if the agent dies, the agency is annulled, and the agent's heir or his executor will not stand in his place because inheritance does not run in agency, and because the principal was satisfied with the agent's opinion, not with another's. And from Abu Yusuf: that the agent's executor owns selling the pawn because the agency is binding, so the executor owns it, like when the mudarib dies after the capital has become specific goods, the executor of the mudarib owns their sale because the contract becomes binding after becoming specific goods. We will answer: The appointment of agency is a binding right, but upon the agent, and inheritance runs in what is for him, unlike mudaraba because it is the right of the mudarib. Explanation: First, keep two things in mind: Some matters are those in which an obligation falls on a person, with no benefit; and some matters are those in which there is benefit. In other words, sometimes there is binding obligation upon oneself, and sometimes for oneself on others. The first is exemplified by agency, and the second by mudaraba. In any case, the point is that in the first type inheritance will not apply, and in the second type inheritance will apply. So if the deceased has a debt upon him, it is not obligatory for his heirs to pay it; and if the deceased has a debt upon someone else, the heirs will inherit it. The purpose of appointing an agent is that the principal benefits from the agent's wisdom, and each person's understanding is separate. So if someone makes Zayd as agent, it does not mean that the principal has also trusted Zayd's son. Therefore the author means that if the agent responsible for selling the pawn dies, then the agency ends, and since inheritance does not run in agency, the agent's executor or heir will not be considered as substituting him. Also, the principal trusted the deceased agent and was satisfied with his opinion, not with his executor or son. It is narrated from Imam Abu Yusuf that after the agent's death, his executor will stand in his place and the executor will have the right to sell the pawn, because according to the previous clarification, this agency was binding and cannot be dissolved, so the executor will own selling the pawn. Imam Abu Yusuf analogized this to a case of mudaraba: if the mudarib has purchased goods with the capital, i.e., the capital no longer exists but the items bought with it exist, and the mudarib dies, then the mudarib's executor has the right to sell those items. Here too the reason is that the mudaraba contract becomes binding after the capital becomes specific goods. Thus, agency is also binding, so in this case too the executor will substitute for the agent and will own selling the pawn. So it is answered: Yes, agency is binding, but the right is binding upon the agent, not for the agent. Therefore, according to the primary principle, inheritance will not apply here, and analogizing it to mudaraba is incorrect because agency is of the first type and mudaraba of the second type, which the author expressed as: mudaraba is the right of the mudarib.
Source pages p. 265

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the effect of the agent's (wakil) death on the agency to sell a pawn (marhun) and whether the agent's heir or executor (wasi) succeeds to that right. The author begins by stating the general rule: during the pledgor's (rahin) life, the agent could sell the pawn in the pledgor's absence; this right continues after the pledgor's death, so the agent may sell the pawn in the absence of the heirs. Similarly, if the mortgagee (murtahin) dies, the agency remains valid because the pledge contract is not invalidated by the death of either party; thus its rights and attributes persist. Then the author warns that 'rights' here refer to possession, collection, and agency, while 'attributes' refer to the second condition, contract, etc. He then states the key rule: the agent's death terminates the agency; his heir or executor does not stand in his place. The justification is that inheritance does not apply in agency because the principal consented to the agent's personal judgment, not another's. The Arabic matn from Al-Hidayah is then quoted: 'And if the agent dies, the agency is annulled, and his heir or executor does not stand in his place because inheritance does not run in agency, and because the principal was satisfied with his opinion and not with another's. And from Abu Yusuf: that the agent's executor owns its sale because the agency is binding, so the executor owns it like the mudarib when he dies after the capital has become specific goods, the executor of the mudarib owns their sale because it becomes binding after becoming specific goods. We said: The appointment of agency is a binding right, but upon him (the agent), and inheritance applies to his property, unlike mudaraba because it is the right of the mudarib.' This presents a clear dispute: Abu Yusuf analogizes the binding agency to mudaraba (a silent partnership), where after the mudarib has converted capital into specific goods, the contract becomes binding, and upon the mudarib's death, his executor may sell those goods. Similarly, the agent's executor should have the right to sell the pawn. The response (from Abu Hanifa or the school) distinguishes: agency is binding upon the agent (lazim 'alayh), not for his benefit; inheritance runs in the agent's property (things owned by him), not in the agency right itself. In contrast, mudaraba is the mudarib's right (his own benefit), so inheritance applies to the mudarib's right. The author then provides a detailed explanation in Urdu: matters where the obligation is upon a person without benefit (like agency) versus matters where there is benefit for oneself (like mudaraba). In the first, inheritance does not apply; in the second, it does. The agent's personal judgment is key; the principal's trust is personal, not transferable. Thus, the executor does not inherit the agency.

Key Terms
وکالت (wakāla): Agency; a contract where one person appoints another to act on their behalf, which is binding upon the agent but not for the agent's benefit.
مضاربت (muḍāraba): A silent partnership where one party provides capital and the other provides labor; the mudarib (worker) has a right to profit, and after capital becomes specific goods, the contract becomes binding.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority Hanafi position, what happens to the agency to sell the pawn when the agent dies?
A) The agent's heir takes over as agent.
B) The agent's executor has the right to sell the pawn.
C) The agency ends and no one succeeds the agent.
D) The mortgagee becomes the agent.

Key Takeaway
Agency is a personal right of the principal, binding upon the agent, and thus does not pass to the agent's heirs or executor upon his death.

Sale of the Pawn: Consent of Both Parties Required
Ruling that neither pledgor nor mortgagee can sell without the other's consent

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on selling a pawn without mutual consent and explain the Hanafi reasoning (talil) for both the pledgor and mortgagee.

Core Idea
Neither pledgor nor mortgagee may sell the pawn without the other's consent.

The law of pledge (rahn) creates a unique relationship: the pledgor retains ownership, but the mortgagee holds possession with a superior claim to the pawn's value. This lesson explores the mutual consent requirement for any sale of the pawn, grounded in the rights of each party. Understanding this ruling prevents invalid transactions and clarifies the boundaries of ownership and security.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the sale of a pawn (marhun) by either the pledgor or the mortgagee. The ruling is that such a sale is impermissible without the other's consent.
The text states 'cannot sell' (ليس له ان يبيعه) which indicates prohibition.
2
Locate the reasoning (talil)
The author provides two separate reasons: for the mortgagee, the pawn is the pledgor's property and he has not consented; for the pledgor, the mortgagee has a prior right to the pawn's monetary value.
This is a rational proof (talil) based on the nature of rights in a pledge.
3
Apply the reasoning to the mortgagee
The mortgagee is not the owner; selling without the owner's consent violates the owner's property rights. Hence the sale is invalid.
Ownership (milk) is with the pledgor.
4
Apply the reasoning to the pledgor
Although the pledgor is the owner, the mortgagee has a superior claim to the pawn's monetary value (māliyya). The pledgor cannot deliver the pawn free of that claim, and delivery is a condition for a valid sale.
The right to value (haqq al-māliyya) acts as a restriction on the pledgor's ownership.
5
State the consequence
A sale without consent is invalid (batil); it does not transfer ownership. Mutual consent is essential.
The ruling applies regardless of whether the sale would benefit the other party.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مرتهن را بین کی رضاگر موکی بچ سکتا ہے
وليس للمرتهن ان يبيعه الا برضا الراهن لانه ملكه وما رضى ببيعه وليس للراهن ان يبيعه الا برضاء المرتهن لان المرتهن احق بماليته من الراهن فلا يقدر الراهن على تسليمه بالبيع
ترجمہ اور مرتہن کو حق نہیں ہے کہ مرہون کو فروخت کرے مگر راہن کی رضا مندی سے اس لئے کہ یہ راہن کی ملک ہے اروہ اس کے بیچنے سے راضی نہیں ہوا اور راہن کو حق نہیں ہے کہ وہ مرہموں کو بیچے مگر مرتین کی رضا مندی سے اس لئے کہ مرتہن اس کی مالیت کا راہن سے زیادہ حقدار ہے تو راہن قادر نہ ہوگا بیع کی وجہ سے مرہون کے سپر د کر نے پر ۔ تشریحی ... راہن اور مرتہن میں سے کسی کو یہ حق حاصل نہیں کہ وہ اپنے دوسرے ساتھی کی رضاء کے بغیر مرہون کو فروخت کر دے۔ مرتہن تو اسلئے نہیں بچ سکتا کہ مرہون کی مالیت میں مرتین را ہن سے زیادہ حقدار ہے البدار ان کو بیع سپرد کرنے پر قدرت نہیں ہوگی حلانکہ بچ کیلئے ضروری ہگہ وہ مقدور ا سلیم ہو۔
The mortgagee cannot sell it except with the consent of the pledgor because it is the pledgor's property and he has not consented to its sale. And the pledgor cannot sell it except with the consent of the mortgagee because the mortgagee has a greater right to its monetary value than the pledgor, so the pledgor will not be able to deliver it by sale. Translation: And the mortgagee has no right to sell the pawn except with the consent of the pledgor, because it is the pledgor's property and he has not consented to its sale. And the pledgor has no right to sell the pawn except with the consent of the mortgagee, because the mortgagee has a greater right to its monetary value than the pledgor, so the pledgor will not be able to deliver it due to the sale. Explanation: Neither the pledgor nor the mortgagee has the right to sell the pawn without the consent of the other. The mortgagee cannot sell because the mortgagee has a greater right to the monetary value of the pawn than the pledgor; the pledgor will not be able to deliver it, while delivery is necessary for the sale.
Source pages p. 266

Commentary
This passage states a fundamental ruling in the law of pledge (rahn): neither the pledgor (rahin) nor the mortgagee (murtahin) may sell the pawn (marhun) without the other's consent. The reasoning is given in the Arabic matn: The mortgagee cannot sell because the pawn is the pledgor's property, and the pledgor has not consented to its sale. The pledgor cannot sell because the mortgagee has a superior right to the monetary value (māliyya) of the pawn; the pledgor, despite being the owner, cannot deliver the pawn free of the mortgagee's claim, and delivery is a condition for a valid sale. The Urdu commentary elaborates: The mortgagee's claim on the pawn's value takes precedence over the pledgor's ownership right in terms of sale, so the pledgor cannot effect a valid sale without the mortgagee's permission. Conversely, the mortgagee is not the owner and cannot sell without the owner's (pledgor's) consent. Thus, mutual consent is required for any sale of the pawn.

Key Terms
مرہون (marhūn): The item pledged as collateral; it remains the property of the pledgor but is held by the mortgagee as security.
مالیت (māliyya): Monetary value; the court-recognized value of the pawn that the mortgagee claims as security for the debt.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why cannot the mortgagee (murtahin) sell the pawn without the pledgor's consent?
A) Because the mortgagee does not have possession.
B) Because the pawn is the pledgor's property and he did not consent to sale.
C) Because the mortgagee's right is only to the profit.
D) Because the pawn is owned jointly.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, a pawn cannot be sold by either the pledgor or mortgagee without the other's consent, due to the pledgor's ownership and the mortgagee's superior right to the pawn's monetary value.

Compelling the Agent to Sell the Pawn When Debt is Due
Ruling that the agent is compelled to sell when debt is due and he refuses

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which a judge compels a pawn agent to sell and explain the Hanafi reasoning for compulsion.

Core Idea
The agent must sell the pawn when debt is due, even without the pledgor's presence.

This passage from Al-Jami' al-Saghir presents a ruling by Imam Muhammad on the compulsion of an agent to sell a pawn when the debt matures and the pledgor is absent. The ruling establishes that the agency is binding (lazim) and thus the agent can be forced by the judge to execute the sale. Understanding this illustrates the Hanafi principle of enforcing obligations that are binding upon a person.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the agent's sale of the pawn when the debt is due. The ruling is that the agent is compelled (jabr) by the judge to sell.
2
List the conditions for compulsion
Three conditions are required: (1) the debt is due (ḥalla al-ajal), (2) the agent refuses to sell, (3) the pledgor is absent (rāhin ghā’ib).
The absence of the pledgor is crucial because otherwise the pledgor could be asked directly.
3
Understand the legal consequence
When conditions are met, the judge compels the agent to sell. The compulsion is an enforcement of an existing obligation (wujūb) upon the agent.
The obligation arises from the binding nature of the agency (luzūm) which is established by two earlier reasons.
4
Trace the reasoning (talīl)
The compulsion is justified by two reasons previously mentioned regarding the binding nature of the agency to sell. These reasons make the agency a binding obligation, so the agent cannot refuse to perform it.
The exact two reasons are not repeated in this passage but refer to earlier discussion in the text.
5
Note the cross-madhhab difference
Outside the Hanafi school, some other schools may not allow compulsion of the agent without the pledgor's consent. This is a legitimate ikhtilāf.
The practical difference: in non-Hanafi courts, the sale may be delayed until the pledgor is present.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ادائے دین کا وقت آجائے اور وکیل مرہون کے بیچنے سے انکار کر دے تو اس پر جبر کیا جائے گا
قال فان حل الاجل وابى الوكيل الذى فى يده الرهن ان يبيعه والراهن غائب اجبر على بيعه لما ذكرنا من الوجهين في لزومه
ترجمہ امام محمد نے فرمایا پس اگر ادا دین کا وقت آ جائے اور وہ وکیل جس کے قبضہ میں مرہون ہے اس کو بیچنے سے انکار کرے اور اہن
When the time for payment of the debt comes and the agent who has possession of the pawn refuses to sell it, he will be compelled to sell it for the two reasons mentioned regarding its binding nature. Translation: Imam Muhammad said: Then if the time for payment arrives and the agent who has the pawn in his hand refuses to sell it, and the pledgor is absent, he is compelled to sell it for the two reasons mentioned about its binding nature.
Source pages p. 266

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from Imam Muhammad (one of the three main Hanafi imams) regarding the agent's refusal to sell the pawn when the debt becomes due. The agent is the person appointed by the pledgor (rahin) to sell the pawn upon maturity. If the agent refuses and the pledgor is absent, the agent is compelled (jabr) by the court to sell the pawn. The reasoning refers back to two previously mentioned reasons for the binding nature of the agency to sell. The translation is incomplete, but the Arabic is clear: the condition is the maturity of the debt (ḥalla al-ajal) and the agent's refusal in the pledgor's absence. The legal consequence is that the judge compels the agent to execute the sale.

Key Terms
جبر (jabr): Legal compulsion; the judge forces the agent to sell the pawn when he refuses in the pledgor's absence.
حلول اجل (ḥulūl al-ajal): Maturity of the debt; the time when the debt becomes due and payable.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Under what condition is the agent compelled to sell the pawn?
A) When the pledgor requests it.
B) When the mortgagee demands payment.
C) When the debt is due and the agent refuses to sell in the pledgor's absence.
D) When the value of the pawn decreases.

Key Takeaway
The agent is legally compelled by the judge to sell the pawn when the debt is due, the agent refuses, and the pledgor is absent.

Death of the Agent in Rahn: Agency Not Inherited and Abu Yusuf's View
Intra-Hanafi dispute on inheriting agency rights in rahn

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school holds that agency terminates upon the agent's death and evaluate Abu Yusuf's analogical argument from mudarabah.

Core Idea
Agency is based on personal trust and is not inherited; Abu Yusuf's analogy fails because he conflated rights upon a person with rights owned by a person.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning the effect of an agent's death in a mortgage (rahn) contract. The majority of the school (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani) holds that the agency ends immediately and cannot be continued by the executor or heir. Imam Abu Yusuf, however, argues that the executor steps in, drawing an analogy to mudarabah. The core issue revolves around the nature of the right: is it a duty imposed on the agent (haqq 'alayhi) or a right owned by him (haqq lahu)? The answer determines whether inheritance applies.

Guided Path
1
State the majority position and its basis
Identify the ruling from Abu Hanifa and Muhammad: the agent's death terminates the wakalah. The basis is that wakalah is built on personal trust, which is not transferable. Furthermore, the right to sell is a right incumbent upon the agent (haqq 'alayhi), not a property right he owns.
This is the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school.
2
Identify Abu Yusuf's opposing view and his dalil
Recognize that Imam Abu Yusuf holds that the executor can sell the mortgaged property. His proof is an analogy (qiyas) to mudarabah: when a mudarib dies after purchasing goods, his executor sells those goods because the contract becomes binding (lazim). Since the wakalah in rahn is also binding, the executor should step in.
This analogy is classified as qiyas khafi because the commonality is the binding nature.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response distinguishing the types of rights
The majority replies by pointing out a fundamental difference: in wakalah, the right to sell is a duty imposed on the agent (haqq 'alayhi), whereas in mudarabah, the right to sell the goods is a right owned by the mudarib (haqq lahu). Inheritance applies only to owned rights, not to duties. Therefore, the analogy is invalid.
This distinction is crucial in Hanafi fiqh for determining inheritable interests.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and the tarjih
The practical consequence: under Abu Yusuf's view, the executor could sell; under the majority, any sale by the executor without fresh authorization would be invalid. The tarjih (preferred position) is the majority view, as explicitly upheld in the text and in later fatwa practice.
The text rejects Abu Yusuf's analogy, confirming the position from Zahir al-Riwayah.

اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد - ۱۴ زید کو وکیل بنایا اس کا مطلب یہ نہ ہو گا کہ مؤکل نے زید کے بیٹے پر بھی اعتماد کر لیا ہے لہذا مصنف یہ کہنا چاہتے ہیں کہ مرہون کی بیچ کے وکیل کا انتقال ہو گیا تو اب وکالت ختم ہو جائے گی اور چونکہ وکالت میں میراث نہیں چلتی لہذا وکیل کا وسی یا وارث اس کا قائم مقام ہو کر وکیل شمار نہیں کیا جائے گا ۔ نیز موکل نے وکیل مرحوم پر اعتماد کیا ہے اور اس کی رائے سے راضی ہوا ہے نہ کہ اس کے وصی یا بیٹے پر امام ابو یوسف" سے منقول ہے کہ وکیل کی موت کے بعد اس کا وصی اسکا قائم مقام ہوگا اور وصی کو حق ہوگا کہ مرہون کو فروخت کرے کیونکہ حسب تصریح سابق یہ وکالت لازم تھی جس کو فتح نہیں کیا جاسکتا ہے لہذا وصی بیچ مرہون کا مالک ہوگا۔ امام ابو یوسف نے اس کو مضارب کے ایک مسئلہ پیر قبلیس کیا ہے کہ اگر مضارب راس المال سے سامان خرید چکا ہے یعنی اب رأس المال نہیں بلکہ وہ اشیاء موجود ہیں جو راس المال سے خریدی گئی ہیں کہ مضارب کا انتقال ہو گیا تو مضارب کے وصی کو حق ہوتا ہے کہ ان اشیاء کو فروخت کر دے یہاں بھی وجہ یہی ہے کہ عقد مضاربت رأس المال کے اعیان بننے کے بعد لازم ہو جاتا ہے لہذا وکالت بھی لازم ہے تو اسمیں بھی وصی وکیل کا قائم ہو گا اور مرہون کو فروخت کرنے کا مالک ہوگا۔ تو امام ابو یوسف کو جواب دیا کہ ہاں وکالت لازم تو ہے مگر وکیل پر حق لازم ہے نہ کہ وکیل کیلئے لہذا مقدمہ اولی کے مطابق آسمیں میراث جاری نہ ہوگی اور اس کو مضاربت پر قیاس کرنا درست نہ ہوگا کیونکہ وکالت از قسم اول ہے اور مضاربت از قسم ثانی جس کو مصنف نے یوں تعبیر کیا ہے کہ مضاربت مضارب کا حق ہے۔
Book of Rahn. Ashraf al-Hidayah, Urdu commentary of Hidayah, Volume 14. When Zayd is made an agent, it does not mean that the principal has also trusted Zayd's son. Thus the author intends to say: When the agent appointed to sell the mortgaged property dies, then the agency ends. And since agency is not inherited, the deceased agent's executor or heir does not become the agent as his substitute. Also, the principal entrusted the deceased agent and was satisfied with his opinion, not with his executor or son. It is narrated from Imam Abu Yusuf that after the agent's death, his executor steps in and has the right to sell the mortgaged property, because as per previous clarification this agency was binding (lazim) and cannot be revoked, so the executor becomes the owner of selling the mortgaged property. Imam Abu Yusuf analogized this to an issue of mudarabah: if the mudarib has purchased goods with the capital, i.e., the capital is no longer present but the purchased items exist, and the mudarib dies, then the mudarib's executor has the right to sell those items. Here too the reason is that the mudarabah contract becomes binding after the capital becomes specific goods, so the agency is also binding, thus the executor stands in for the agent and has authority to sell the mortgaged property. In response to Imam Abu Yusuf, it is said: Yes, the agency is binding, but it is a right incumbent upon the agent (haqq 'alayhi), not a right belonging to him (haqq lahu). Therefore, according to the analogy of the first type, inheritance does not apply here, and analogizing it to mudarabah is not correct because agency is of the first type and mudarabah is of the second type, which the author has expressed as: mudarabah is a right of the mudarib.
Source pages p. 266

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the effect of the agent's death on a wakalah to sell a mortgaged property (rahn). The main ruling from the majority (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani) is that the agency terminates upon the agent's death, and neither his executor (wasi) nor his heir inherits the right to sell. This is because wakalah is a contract based on personal trust, and it is well established that wakalah is not inheritable. Additionally, the right to sell is classified as a right incumbent upon the agent (haqq 'alayhi), not a property right owned by him (haqq lahu) that could be inherited. Imam Abu Yusuf differs. He analogizes to mudarabah: if a mudarib dies after purchasing goods with capital, his executor may sell those goods because the mudarabah becomes binding once capital is converted into goods. Similarly, Abu Yusuf argues that the wakalah in rahn is binding (lazim), so the executor should step in. The Hanafi response (from the majority) clarifies that the analogy is flawed: wakalah is a right imposed on the agent (haqq 'alayhi), whereas mudarabah grants the mudarib a right owned by him (haqq lahu). Therefore, inheritance applies in mudarabah but not in wakalah. The mufta bihi (relied-upon) position is that the agency ends and the executor has no authority to sell. Tarjih: The text explicitly rejects Abu Yusuf's view, affirming the majority position from the Zahir al-Riwayah.

Key Terms
میراث (miraath): Inheritance of rights and obligations from a deceased person. In this context, it refers to the principle that agency rights are not inheritable upon the agent's death.
مضاربت (mudarabah): A partnership contract where one party (rabb al-mal) provides capital and the other (mudarib) provides labor, with profit sharing. Used as an analogy by Abu Yusuf for binding agency.
حق لازم (haqq lazim): A right that is binding/obligatory. In this text, it refers to the nature of the agency in rahn being binding (lazim) but still categorically a right upon the agent.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority Hanafi view, if the agent appointed to sell a mortgaged property (rahn) dies, what happens to the agency?
A) The agency continues with the executor or heir.
B) The agency terminates and cannot be continued by the executor or heir.
C) The agency only terminates if the principal objects.
D) The judge appoints a new agent.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, agency terminates upon the agent's death and is not inherited; inheritance applies only to rights owned (haqq lahu), not duties imposed (haqq 'alayhi).

Rule on Selling Pledged Property Without Consent
Ruling on sale of rahn without consent

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on selling pledged property (rahn) without the consent of the other party and explain the reasoning for both the pledgor (rahin) and pledgee (murtahin).

Core Idea
Neither the pledgor nor the pledgee may sell the pledged property without the other's consent.

In a pledge (rahn) contract, both parties have competing rights: the pledgor (rahin) owns the property, while the pledgee (murtahin) holds a prior claim to its value as security. This creates a restriction on the sale of the pledged item. The following passage from Al-Hidayah establishes that neither party can sell the property unilaterally, and explains the legal reasoning behind this prohibition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the parties
The act under discussion is the sale (bay') of the pledged property (rahn) during the period of pledge. The two parties are the pledgor (rahin) and the pledgee (murtahin).
2
State the ruling for the pledgee (murtahin) and its rationale
The murtahin cannot sell the rahn without the rahin's consent because the property belongs to the rahin, and the rahin did not consent to its sale. The murtahin only has a right to the value (maliyyah), not ownership.
Ownership (milk) remains with the rahin; the murtahin's right is a security interest.
3
State the ruling for the pledgor (rahin) and its rationale
The rahin cannot sell the rahn without the murtahin's consent because the murtahin has a superior right to the value (maliyyah) of the property. Since the rahin cannot deliver the property free of the pledge, delivery (taslim) is impossible, invalidating the sale.
A valid sale requires the seller to be able to deliver the item (maqdur 'alayhi al-taslim).
4
Note the key condition for a valid sale
The commentary highlights that ability to deliver (maqdur 'alayhi al-taslim) is a condition for sale. In this case, the murtahin's right to the value prevents the rahin from delivering the property unencumbered.
This condition is from the general rules of sale (bay') in Hanafi fiqh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وليس للمرتهن ان يبيعه الا برضا الراهن لانه ملكه وما رضى ببيعه وليس للراهن ان يبيعه الا برضاء المرتهن لان المرتهن احق بماليته من الراهن فلا يقدر الراهن على تسليمه بالبيع ترجمہ اور مرتہن کو حق نہیں ہے کہ مرہون کو فروخت کرے مگر راہن کی رضا مندی سے اس لئے کہ یہ راہن کی ملک ہے اروہ اس کے بیچنے سے راضی نہیں ہوا اور راہن کو حق نہیں ہے کہ وہ مرہموں کو بیچے مگر مرتین کی رضا مندی سے اس لئے کہ مرتہن اس کی مالیت کا راہن سے زیادہ حقدار ہے تو راہن قادر نہ ہوگا بیع کی وجہ سے مرہون کے سپر د کر نے پر ۔ تشریحی ... راہن اور مرتہن میں سے کسی کو یہ حق حاصل نہیں کہ وہ اپنے دوسرے ساتھی کی رضاء کے بغیر مرہون کو فروخت کر دے۔ مرتہن تو اسلئے نہیں بچ سکتا کہ مرہون کی مالیت میں مرتین را ہن سے زیادہ حقدار ہے البدار ان کو بیع سپرد کرنے پر قدرت نہیں ہوگی حلانکہ بچ کیلئے ضروری ہگہ وہ مقدور ا سلیم ہو۔
And it is not permissible for the murtahin (pledgee) to sell it except with the consent of the rahin (pledgor), because it is the rahin's property and he did not consent to its sale. And it is not permissible for the rahin to sell it except with the consent of the murtahin, because the murtahin has a greater right to its value (maliyyah) than the rahin. Therefore, the rahin is unable to deliver it through sale. Translation: The murtahin does not have the right to sell the mortgaged property except with the rahin's consent, because it is the rahin's property and he did not consent to its sale. And the rahin does not have the right to sell the mortgaged property except with the murtahin's consent, because the murtahin has a greater right to its value than the rahin. Thus, the rahin will not be able to deliver the mortgaged property due to the sale. Commentary: Neither the rahin nor the murtahin has the right to sell the mortgaged property without the consent of the other party. The murtahin does not sell because the murtahin has a greater right to the value of the mortgaged property than the rahin, but he does not have the ability to deliver the property through sale, while for a valid sale, the ability to deliver (maqdur 'alayhi al-taslim) is necessary.
Source pages p. 266

Commentary
This passage states a clear rule regarding the sale of pledged property (rahn) during the period of pledge. The Arabic text from the matn (foundational text) establishes that neither the pledgor (rahin) nor the pledgee (murtahin) may sell the property without the consent of the other. The reasoning is twofold: For the pledgee (murtahin), the property belongs to the pledgor (rahin), and the rahin has not consented to its sale. Additionally, the murtahin does not own the property; he only has a right to its value as security. Therefore, he cannot sell. For the pledgor (rahin), although he owns the property, the murtahin has a superior right to its value due to the pledge. The rahin cannot deliver the property free of the pledge through a sale without the murtahin's consent, and delivery is a condition for the validity of the sale (being maqdur 'alayhi al-taslim). The commentary clarifies that the inability to deliver is the key impediment. Thus, a unilateral sale by either party without the other's consent is invalid (ghayr ja'iz). This ruling is well-established in the Hanafi school and is consistent across the madhhab.

Key Terms
مالیت (maliyyah): The monetary value or consideration of the property. In this text, the murtahin has a greater right to the value (maliyyah) than the rahin, meaning the pledgee's security interest takes precedence.
تسلیم (taslim): Delivery of the sold item to the buyer. For a sale to be valid, the seller must be able to deliver (maqdur 'alayhi al-taslim). Here, the rahin cannot deliver the rahn because the murtahin's right prevents it.
حق (haqq): A legal right. In this context, the murtahin has a right to the value of the rahn, and the rahin has ownership rights. Neither is absolute.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is the murtahin (pledgee) prohibited from selling the pledged property without the rahin's (pledgor's) consent?
A) Because the murtahin does not have legal capacity to sell.
B) Because the property belongs to the rahin and the rahin did not consent.
C) Because the murtahin has already received the debt.
D) Because the murtahin has no right to the property at all.

Key Takeaway
Neither the pledgor nor the pledgee may sell the pledged property without the other's consent: the murtahin lacks ownership, and the rahin cannot deliver free of the murtahin's right to the value.

Compelling the Agent to Sell the Rahn When Debt is Due
Ruling on compelling the agent to sell rahn when debt is due and rahin absent

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on compelling the agent to sell the rahn when the debt is due and the rahin is absent, and apply the two legal reasons for compulsion.

Core Idea
An agent for selling rahn is compelled when the rahin is absent, because refusal nullifies the mortgagee's right.

When a debt secured by a pledge (rahn) becomes due, and the pledgor (rahin) is absent, the agent holding the pledged property may refuse to sell it. The Hanafi school provides a clear ruling: the judge compels the agent to sell. This lesson unpacks the two legal reasons behind this compulsion—binding nature of the agency and prevention of nullification of the mortgagee's right—and examines an analogy with agency for litigation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and ruling
Read the opening statement: when the debt is due, the agent refuses to sell, and the rahin is absent, the agent is compelled to sell. This is the basic ruling.
2
Extract the two reasons (wujuh)
The text mentions two reasons for compulsion: (1) the agency was conditioned in the rahn contract, making it a binding right (haqq lazim), and (2) refusal leads to nullification of the murtahin's right (ibtal haqq). Understand each reason.
The first reason is based on contract condition; the second on preventing harm.
3
Analyze the analogy with wakalah bil khusumat
The passage compares to an agent for litigation: if the principal is absent and the agent refuses to litigate, he is compelled because otherwise the plaintiff's right would be nullified. Note the distinguishing factor: in a general sale agency, the principal can sell himself, so no compulsion.
The illa (effective cause) is the inability of the right-holder to act personally.
4
Examine the intra-Hanafi dispute
The text presents a dispute: if the agency was not conditioned in the rahn contract but appointed later, some say no compulsion (based on first reason), others say compulsion (based on second reason). The text declares the second opinion more correct (asah).
Abu Yusuf holds the answer is the same in both cases, supported by general texts.
5
Apply the mufta bihi
The preferred ruling is that the agent is compelled regardless of whether the agency was conditioned in the contract or appointed later, due to the overriding reason of preventing nullification of the murtahin's right.
This is the operative position for fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال فان حل الاجل وابى الوكيل الذى فى يده الرهن ان يبيعه والراهن غائب اجبر على بيعه لما ذكرنا من الوجهين في لزومه ترجمہ امام محمد نے فرمایا پس اگر ادا دین کا وقت آ جائے اور وہ وکیل جس کے قبضہ میں مرہون ہے اس کو بیچنے سے انکار کرے اور اہن غائب ہو تو وکیل کو اس کی بیع پر مجبور کیا جائے گا ان دو دلیلوں کی وجہ سے جو وکالت کے لزوم کے بیان میں ہم ذکر کر چکے ہیں۔ تشریح ادائیگی دین کا وقت آگیا اور راہن غائب ہو اور وہ وکیل جس کے قبضہ میں مرہون ہے وہ بیج سے انکار کرتا ہے تو اب کیا کیا جائے تو فرمایا کہ قاضی اس پر جبر کرے تا کہ وہ مرہون کو فروخت کرے۔ کیوں؟ اس لئے کہ وکالت جب عقد رہن میں مشروط ہوتی ہے تو وہ حق لازم ہوتا ہے اور حق لازم کیلئے جبر جائز ہے نیز وکیل کے انکار کرنے میں مرتہن کے حق کا ابطال ہے اور دوسرے کے حق کو ابطال سے بچانے کیلئے جبر جائز ہوا کرتا ہے۔ یہی ان دو دلیلوں کا خلاصہ ہے جن کا مصنف نے حوالہ دیا ہے۔ تنبیہ اگر راہن غائب نہ ہو بلکہ حاضر ہو تو راہن پر جبر ہو گا نہ کہ وکیل پر بہر حال اگر وہ جبر کے باوجود نہ بیچے تو قاضی اسکو بیچ د.
شامی ص ۳۲۵، ج ۵
مذکورہ مسئلہ کی نظیر
وكذالك الرجل يوكل غيره بالخصومة وغاب الموكل فابى ان يخاصم اجبر على الخصومة للوجه الثاني هو ان فيه اتواء الحق بخلاف الوكيل بالبيع لان الموكل يبيع بنفسه فلا يتوى حقه أما المدعى لا يقدر على الدعوى والمرتهن لا يملك بيعه بنفسه
ترجمہ اور ایسے ہی کسی شخص نے اپنے غیر کو وکیل بالخصومت بنایا اور موکل غائب ہو گیا پس وکیل مخاصمت اس سے انکار کرے تو وکیل کو خصومت پر مجبور کیا جائے گا دوسری دلیل کی وجہ سے اور وہ یہ ہے کہ اس میں حق کا ابطال ہے خلاف وکیل بیچ کے اس لئے کہ موکل خود فروخت کر سکتا ہے تو اس کا حق باطل نہ ہوگا بہر حال مدعی دعوی پر قادر نہیں اور مرتہن خود بیچنے کا مالک نہیں۔ تشریح زید نے بکر کو وکیل بالخصومت بنایا اور زید غائب ہے اب بکر خصومت سے انکار کرتا ہے تو بکر کو خصومت پر مجبور کیا جائے گاورنہ مدعی کے حق کا ابطال لازم آئے گا۔
سوال اگر زید نے بکر کو اپنی چیز بیچنے کا وکیل بنایا ( رہن سے الگ ) اور وہ بیچ سے انکار کرے تو اسپر کیوں جبر نہیں کیاجاتا؟
جواب ... اس لئے کہ اس میں موکل کا کوئی نقصان نہیں کیونکہ وہ خود بیچ سکتا ہے تو ابطال حق موکل لازم نہیں آیا۔ سوال تو پھر اس میں مدعی (مؤکل) کا تو یہ نقصان ہے کہ اس نے وکیل پر اعتماد کر لیا ہے اس وجہ سے خود خصومت سے باز رہے گا اور جب وکیل بھی خصومت سے باز رہے تو مدعی کے حق کا ابطال لازم آتا ہے لہذا جبر کیا جائے گا۔ اور چونکہ مرتہن خود بیچنے پر قادر نہیں ہے اور یہ بھی بیع سے انکار کرے تو مرتہن کے حق کا ابطال ہے۔
اگر عقدرہن میں وکالت مشروط نہ ہوئی ہو بلکہ بعد میں وکیل بنایا تو اس پر جبر کیا جائے گایا نہیں
فلو لم يكن التوكيل مشروطا في عقد الرهن وانما شرط بعده قيل لا يجبر اعتبارا للوجه الاول وقيل يجبر رجوعا الى الوجه الثانى وهذا اصح وعن ابى يوسف ان الجواب فى الفصلين واحد ويؤيده اطلاق الجواب
في الجامع الصغير وفي الاصل
He (Imam Muhammad) said: When the time of payment arrives and the agent who has possession of the rahn refuses to sell it while the rahin is absent, he is compelled to sell it, due to the two reasons we mentioned regarding the binding nature of the agency. Translation: Imam Muhammad said: When the time for repayment comes and the agent in whose possession the rahn is refuses to sell it, while the rahin is absent, the agent is compelled to sell it, because of the two proofs we mentioned regarding the binding nature of the agency. Commentary: The time of payment has come, and the rahin is absent, and the agent who has possession of the rahn refuses to sell. So what is to be done? He said that the judge should compel him so that he sells the rahn. Why? Because when the agency is conditioned in the contract of rahn, it becomes a binding right (haqq lazim), and for a binding right, compulsion is permissible. Also, the agent's refusal results in the nullification of the murtahin's right, and to prevent the nullification of another's right, compulsion is permissible. This is the summary of the two proofs to which the author referred. Note: If the rahin is not absent but present, then compulsion is upon the rahin, not the agent. In any case, if he does not sell despite compulsion, the judge sells it. Shami vol. 5, p. 325. An analogy to this issue: Similarly, if a man appoints another as an agent for litigation (wakalah bil khusumat) and the principal is absent, and the agent refuses to litigate, he is compelled to litigate because of the second reason, i.e., there is nullification of the right. Unlike an agent for sale, because the principal can sell himself, so his right is not nullified. But a plaintiff cannot file a lawsuit himself, and the murtahin cannot sell by himself. Commentary: Zayd appointed Bakr as an agent for litigation, and Zayd is absent. Now Bakr refuses to litigate, so Bakr is compelled to litigate, otherwise nullification of the plaintiff's right would occur. Question: If Zayd appointed Bakr as an agent to sell his property (separate from rahn) and he refuses to sell, why is he not compelled? Answer: Because in that case, there is no loss to the principal, as he can sell himself, so nullification of the principal's right does not occur. Question: Then here, the plaintiff (principal) has the loss that he trusted the agent and therefore refrained from litigation, and when the agent also refrains, the nullification of the plaintiff's right occurs, so he is compelled. And since the murtahin is not able to sell himself, and if the agent also refuses to sell, there is nullification of the murtahin's right. If the agency was not conditioned in the contract of rahn but was appointed later, then is he compelled or not? He said: If the agency was not conditioned in the contract of rahn but rather appointed afterward, it is said he is not compelled, considering the first reason; and it is said he is compelled, reverting to the second reason, and this is more correct. And from Abu Yusuf that the answer in both cases is the same, and this is supported by the general answer in Al-Jami' al-Saghir and Al-Asl.
Source pages p. 266

Commentary
This passage provides a detailed ruling on compelling the agent (vakil) to sell the pledged property when the debt becomes due and the pledgor (rahin) is absent. The main ruling from Imam Muhammad is that the agent is compelled to sell. The commentary explains two reasons: (1) The agency conditioned in the rahn contract is binding (lazim), and for a binding right, compulsion is allowed. (2) The agent's refusal leads to the nullification of the murtahin's right, and preventing such nullification justifies compulsion. The note clarifies that if the rahin is present, compulsion is on the rahin, not the agent. Then the passage draws an analogy with wakalah bil khusumat (agency for litigation): if the agent refuses to litigate while the principal is absent, he is compelled because otherwise the plaintiff's right would be nullified. This is contrasted with a general sale agency where the principal can sell himself, so no compulsion. A further question explores why compulsion applies even though the principal trusted the agent; the answer is that the reliance justifies compulsion to prevent harm to the plaintiff (in litigation) and the murtahin (in rahn). Finally, there is a dispute about whether compulsion applies if the agency was not conditioned in the rahn contract but only appointed later. Two opinions are reported: the first considers the first reason (binding nature) and says no compulsion; the second considers the second reason (preventing nullification) and says compulsion, and this second opinion is deemed more correct (asah). Abu Yusuf holds that the answer is the same in both scenarios, supported by general statements in Al-Jami' al-Saghir and Al-Asl. The mufta bihi is that the agent is compelled even if the agency was not initially conditioned.

Key Terms
جبر (jabr): Legal compulsion by a judge or authority to perform an act. In this context, the judge forces the agent to sell the rahn.
ابطال حق (ibtal haqq): Nullification or destruction of a legal right. The text states that the agent's refusal would lead to ibtal of the murtahin's right, justifying compulsion.
وکالت بالخصومت (wakalah bil khusumat): Agency for litigation. The passage draws an analogy: if a litigation agent refuses to act while the principal is absent, he is compelled to avoid nullifying the plaintiff's right.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred Hanafi view, what is the ruling if the agent to sell the rahn was appointed after the contract of rahn (not conditioned) and later refuses to sell when the debt is due and the rahin is absent?
A) The agent is not compelled because the agency was not originally binding.
B) The agent is compelled to prevent nullification of the murtahin's right.
C) The judge sells the property without compelling the agent.
D) The murtahin must appoint a new agent.

Key Takeaway
An agent for selling rahn is compelled to sell when the debt is due and the rahin is absent, to prevent nullification of the mortgagee's right, even if the agency was not originally conditioned in the contract.

Compelling the Agent to Sell the Pawned Item When the Pledgor is Absent
Explains compulsion of agent to sell pawn when pledgor absent and if agency was stipulated

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the two proofs for compelling an agent to sell a pawn when the pledgor is absent, and distinguish the ruling when agency is stipulated in the contract versus appointed afterwards.

Core Idea
A judge can compel an agent to sell a pawn when the pledgor is absent, because the agency is binding and refusal nullifies the creditor's right.

In pledge law, a crucial issue arises when the debt is due, the pledgor is absent, and the agent holding the pawn refuses to sell. How is the creditor's right protected? This lesson explores the Hanafi ruling that the judge may compel the agent. We will study the two proofs behind this rule – the binding nature of agency and the prevention of right nullification – and the intra-Hanafi debate over whether the agency must be stipulated in the original pledge contract.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling
What authority does the judge have when the pledgor is absent and the agent refuses to sell? The text states the judge compels the agent to sell.
2
Unpack the first proof: agency as a binding right
Agency stipulated in the pledge contract creates a haqq lazim (binding right). Compulsion is permissible for binding rights according to Hanafi usul.
3
Unpack the second proof: prevent nullification of the creditor's right
The agent's refusal would nullify the creditor's right because the creditor cannot sell the pawn himself. Compulsion is allowed to prevent ibtal haqq.
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on timing of agency
If agency was not stipulated in the original contract but appointed later, two narrations exist: one says no compulsion, the other says yes. The more correct view (sahih) is compulsion, as per Abu Yusuf and absolute statements of Imam Muhammad.
Sahih view: compulsion in both cases.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The operative position for fatwa is that compulsion applies in both cases (stipulated or afterwards), based on tarjih of the second proof and the authority of Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad.

غائب ہو تو وکیل کو اس کی بیع پر مجبور کیا جائے گا ان دو دلیلوں کی وجہ سے جو وکالت کے لزوم کے بیان میں ہم ذکر کر چکے ہیں۔ تشریح ادائیگی دین کا وقت آگیا اور راہن غائب ہو اور وہ وکیل جس کے قبضہ میں مرہون ہے وہ بیع سے انکار کرتا ہے تو اب کیا کیا جائے تو فرمایا کہ قاضی اس پر جبر کرے تا کہ وہ مرہون کو فروخت کرے۔ کیوں؟ اس لئے کہ وکالت جب عقد رہن میں مشروط ہوتی ہے تو وہ حق لازم ہوتا ہے اور حق لازم کیلئے جبر جائز ہے نیز وکیل کے انکار کرنے میں مرتہن کے حق کا ابطال ہے اور دوسرے کے حق کو ابطال سے بچانے کیلئے جبر جائز ہوا کرتا ہے۔ یہی ان دو دلیلوں کا خلاصہ ہے جن کا مصنف نے حوالہ دیا ہے۔ تنبیہ اگر راہن غائب نہ ہو بلکہ حاضر ہو تو راہن پر جبر ہو گا نہ کہ وکیل پر بہر حال اگر وہ جبر کے باوجود نہ بیچے تو قاضی اسکو بیچ د۔
شامی ص ۳۲۵، ج ۵
مذکورہ مسئلہ کی نظیر
وكذلك الرجل يوكل غيره بالخصومة وغاب الموكل فابى ان يخاصم اجبر على الخصومة للوجه الثاني هو ان فيه اتواء الحق بخلاف الوكيل بالبيع لان الموكل يبيع بنفسه فلا يتوى حقه أما المدعى لا يقدر على الدعوى والمرتهن لا يملك بيعه بنفسه
ترجمہ اور ایسے ہی کسی شخص نے اپنے غیر کو وکیل بالخصومت بنایا اور موکل غائب ہو گیا پس وکیل مخاصمت اس سے انکار کرے تو وکیل کو خصومت پر مجبور کیا جائے گا دوسری دلیل کی وجہ سے اور وہ یہ ہے کہ اس میں حق کا ابطال ہے خلاف وکیل بیع کے اس لئے کہ موکل خود فروخت کر سکتا ہے تو اس کا حق باطل نہ ہوگا بہر حال مدعی دعوی پر قادر نہیں اور مرتہن خود بیچنے کا مالک نہیں۔ تشریح زید نے بکر کو وکیل بالخصومت بنایا اور زید غائب ہے اب بکر خصومت سے انکار کرتا ہے تو بکر کو خصومت پر مجبور کیا جائے گا ورنہ مدعی کے حق کا ابطال لازم آئے گا۔
سوال اگر زید نے بکر کو اپنی چیز بیچنے کا وکیل بنایا ( رہن سے الگ ) اور وہ بیع سے انکار کرے تو اسپر کیوں جبر نہیں کیا جاتا؟
جواب ... اس لئے کہ اس میں موکل کا کوئی نقصان نہیں کیونکہ وہ خود بیچ سکتا ہے تو ابطال حق موکل لازم نہیں آیا۔ سوال تو پھر اس میں مدعی (موکل) کا تو یہ نقصان ہے کہ اس نے وکیل پر اعتماد کر لیا ہے اس وجہ سے خود خصومت سے باز رہے گا اور جب وکیل بھی خصومت سے باز رہے تو مدعی کے حق کا ابطال لازم آتا ہے لہذا جبر کیا جائے گا۔ اور چونکہ مرتہن خود بیچنے پر قادر نہیں ہے اور یہ بھی بیع سے انکار کرے تو مرتہن کے حق کا ابطال ہے۔
اگر عقد رہن میں وکالت مشروط نہ ہوئی ہو بلکہ بعد میں وکیل بنایا تو اس پر جبر کیا جائے گا یا نہیں

في الجامع الصغير وفي الاصل

ترجمہ پس اگر توکیل عقد رہن میں مشروط نہ ہو بلکہ اس کے بعد میں شرط ہوئی ہو کہا گیا ہے کہ جبر نہیں کیا جائے گا پہلی دلیل کا اعتبار کرتے ہوئے اور کہا گیا ہے کہ جبر کیا جائے گا دوسری دلیل کی جانب رجوع کرتے ہوئے اور یہی اصح ہے اور ابو یوسف سے منقول ہے کہ دونوں صورتوں میں جواب ایک ہے اور جامع صغیر اور مبسوط میں جواب کا اطلاق اس کا مؤید ہے۔
تشریح یہ تفصیل جبر علی الوکیل اس صورت میں سے جب کہ وکالت عقد رہن میں مشروط ہوئی ہو اور اگر عقد رہن میں وکالت مشروط نہ ہو بلکہ بعد میں وکالت مشروط ہو تو اس میں دو قول ہیں:
- جبر نہیں ہوگا کیونکہ یہ وکالت عقد میں نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے حقوق عقد میں سے نہ ہوئی ۔
- جبر ہوگا کیونکہ ابطال حق مرتہن لازم آتا ہے ان دونوں روایتوں میں اصح یہی ہے کہ جبر ہوگا۔ امام ابو یوسف سے منقول ہے کہ وکالت عقد میں مشروط ہو یا بعد میں شرط ہو بہر صورت ایک ہی حکم ہے یعنی جبر ہو گا اور امام محمد کے اسلوب سے اس کی تائید ہوتی ہے کیونکہ انہوں نے جامع صغیر اور مبسوط میں یہ مطلق وکالت کا حکم بیان فرمایا ہے مشروط فی العقد و غير مشروط في العقد کی کوئی تخصیص نہیں ہے کیونکہ امام محمد نے جامع صغیر اور مبسوط میں یوں فرمایا ہے کہ واذا ابی الوکیل عن البيع يجبر اور یہ قول مطلق ہے جو دونوں صورتوں کو شامل ہے۔
He said: If the pledgor is absent, the agent will be compelled to sell it, due to the two proofs which we have mentioned regarding the binding nature of agency. Explanation: The time for payment of the debt has come, and the pledgor is absent, and the agent who has possession of the pawned item refuses to sell it. So what should be done? He said: The judge will compel him to sell the pawned item. Why? Because when agency is stipulated in the contract of pledge, it becomes a binding right, and compulsion is permissible for a binding right. Also, in the agent's refusal there is nullification of the creditor's right, and compulsion is permissible to prevent nullification of another's right. This is the summary of the two proofs to which the author referred. Note: If the pledgor is not absent but present, then compulsion will be on the pledgor, not on the agent. In any case, if he does not sell despite compulsion, the judge will sell it. (Shami, vol. 5, p. 325) A parallel to the mentioned issue: Similarly, a man appoints another as agent for litigation, and the principal is absent, and he refuses to litigate; he will be compelled to litigate, due to the second proof, which is that it involves the nullification of a right. Unlike the agent for sale, because the principal can sell himself, so his right is not nullified. But the claimant cannot sue, and the creditor (murtahin) does not have the right to sell it himself. Translation: And similarly, if a person appointed someone as agent for litigation and the principal became absent, then the agent refuses to litigate, the agent will be compelled to litigate due to the second proof, which is that it involves nullification of the right, unlike the agent for sale, because the principal can sell himself, so his right is not nullified. In any case, the claimant is not able to sue, and the creditor is not able to sell it himself. Explanation: Zayd appointed Bakr as agent for litigation, and Zayd is absent. Now Bakr refuses to litigate, so Bakr will be compelled to litigate; otherwise, the nullification of the claimant's right becomes necessary. Question: If Zayd appointed Bakr as agent to sell his property (separate from pledge) and he refuses to sell, why is he not compelled? Answer: Because there is no loss to the principal, as he can sell himself, so the nullification of the principal's right does not occur. Question: Then in this case, the claimant (principal) does suffer loss because he relied on the agent and therefore refrained from litigation himself, and when the agent also refrains from litigation, the nullification of the claimant's right becomes necessary, so compulsion should be applied. And because the creditor is not able to sell himself, and if he also refuses to sell, it nullifies the creditor's right. If the agency was not stipulated in the contract of pledge but was stipulated afterwards, is he compelled or not? For if the appointment was not stipulated in the contract of pledge but was stipulated after it: it is said he will not be compelled, considering the first proof; and it is said he will be compelled, referring to the second proof, and this is more correct. And from Abu Yusuf it is narrated that the answer in both cases is the same, and the absolute answer in al-Jami' al-Saghir and al-Asl supports it. Translation: So if the appointment was not stipulated in the contract of pledge but was stipulated after it, it is said that he will not be compelled, considering the first proof, and it is said that he will be compelled, referring to the second proof, and this is more correct. And from Abu Yusuf it is narrated that the answer in both cases is one, and the absolute answer in al-Jami' al-Saghir and al-Mabsut supports it. Explanation: This detail of compulsion on the agent is in the case where the agency was stipulated in the contract of pledge. If the agency was not stipulated in the contract of pledge but was stipulated afterwards, there are two sayings: (1) He will not be compelled, because this agency, not being in the contract, is not among the rights of the contract. (2) He will be compelled, because nullification of the creditor's right becomes necessary. Of these two narrations, the more correct is that he will be compelled. From Imam Abu Yusuf it is narrated that whether the agency is stipulated in the contract or after, in all cases the ruling is one, i.e., compulsion. And it is supported by the style of Imam Muhammad, because he stated this absolute ruling of agency in al-Jami' al-Saghir and al-Mabsut, with no specification of being stipulated in the contract or not specified in the contract, because Imam Muhammad said in al-Jami' al-Saghir and al-Mabsut: 'And when the agent refuses to sell, he is compelled.' And this is an absolute statement that includes both cases.
Source pages p. 267

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof discussing the compulsion (jabr) of an agent (wakil) to sell a pawned item (marhun) when the pledgor (rahin) is absent. The author first states the ruling: if the pledgor is absent and the agent who possesses the pawned item refuses to sell it when the debt is due, the judge compels the agent to sell. Two proofs are given: first, agency stipulated in the contract of pledge creates a binding right (haqq lazim), and compulsion is valid for a binding right. Second, the agent's refusal leads to nullification (ibtal) of the creditor's right, and compulsion is valid to prevent such nullification. The author then notes a parallel case: an agent for litigation (wakil bil khusuma) can also be compelled to litigate when the principal is absent, because the claimant cannot sue himself. In contrast, an agent for a simple sale (not involving a pledge) is not compelled because the principal can sell himself. However, the reason for compulsion in the pledge case is that the creditor (murtahin) cannot sell the pawn himself. The passage then addresses whether compulsion applies if the agency was not stipulated in the initial contract of pledge but was added later. Two narrations exist: one says no compulsion (because it is not part of the contract's rights), the other says compulsion (to prevent nullification of the creditor's right). The more correct (asahh) view is that compulsion applies. Imam Abu Yusuf is reported to hold that both cases are the same, and this is supported by the absolute wording of Imam Muhammad in al-Jami' al-Saghir and al-Mabsut where he says: 'When the agent refuses to sell, he is compelled,' without any specification.

Key Terms
وکالت (wakala): Agency; the appointment of another to act on one's behalf in a legal matter.
جبر (jabr): Legal compulsion by the judge to perform an act.
حق لازم (haqq lazim): A binding right that cannot be unilaterally revoked.
ابطال حق (ibtal haqq): Nullification or destruction of a legal right.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the reason an agent for sale in a pledge contract can be compelled to sell, while a simple agent for sale cannot?
A) The agent in a pledge contract is paid more.
B) The creditor cannot sell the pawn himself, so refusal nullifies his right.
C) The pledgor is always absent in pledge cases.
D) The judge has more authority in pledge matters.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school allows a judge to compel an agent to sell a pawn when the pledgor is absent, both when the agency is stipulated in the contract and when appointed later, to protect the creditor's right.
